It is not a second independent quantum theory inside the article.
Its purpose is transitional and interpretive:
to preserve continuity with earlier drafts while making clear how the
new Level~A / Level~B / Open discipline changes the meaning of the
claims.

\subsection*{Why the old standalone quantum section is no longer kept}

In earlier drafts, several quantum-mechanical statements were grouped
together in one large section:
loop quantisation, Schr\"odinger-type dynamics, canonical commutators,
Born-type probabilities, decoherence, vacuum effects, and black-hole
information logic.
That organisation is no longer optimal.
The present article distributes these topics according to the actual
internal architecture of the coherent branch:
phase/winding structure, pre-quantum action scale, wave reduction,
canonical structure, uncertainty, statistics, decoherence,
vacuum-response effects, defect sectors, and strong-field horizon logic
are now developed in distinct parts of the Quantum Sector itself.

This is not merely editorial reordering.
It reflects the fact that not all such statements have the same status:
some are structural, some are effective, and some remain open.
The older unified presentation compressed these differences too strongly.

\subsection*{The new quantum logic in one chain}

The coherent-topological branch is organised by the following sequence:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
  \item a phase-sensitive condensate sector exists once the ordered
  branch is selected;
  \item single-valuedness of the order parameter gives winding sectors
  and a minimal loop action;
  \item this defines the structural action scale $S_0$ of the coherent
  branch;
  \item reduced wave dynamics takes a Schr\"odinger-type form with
  $S_0$ in the role of the action parameter;
  \item canonical structure, uncertainty relations, and probability
  assignments are then addressed at the level appropriate to their
  status;
  \item subsystem--environment splitting yields decoherence and
  effective reduced-state irreversibility without fundamental loss of
  global coherence;
  \item vacuum-response phenomena and black-hole thermality are
  interpreted as organised probes of the same coherent vacuum structure.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{What has been strengthened relative to the old presentation}

The new Quantum Sector strengthens the framework in several ways.

First, the existence of the coherent action scale $S_0$, the winding
structure, and the subsystem--environment logic are now stated
structurally and separated from later physical identifications.

Second, the article no longer presents the Born rule, the full Pauli
principle, or the final identification $S_0=\hbar$ as unconditional
bare-postulate theorems.

Third, the horizon-thermality discussion is now integrated with the
general reduced-state logic rather than treated as an isolated
exception.

Fourth, the coherent-topological branch is now visibly parallel to the
macroscopic branch: both are branches of one ordered condensate, rather
than independent theories awkwardly glued together.

\subsection*{What becomes weaker, and why that is acceptable}

The price of the new discipline is that some statements once presented
as final derivations are now explicitly conditional.
This is intentional.
The current article does not claim that the old quantum section was
simply wrong; rather, it claims that its status assignments were too
strong.
The new formulation is therefore more modest but also more reliable.

In particular:
\begin{itemize}
  \item $S_0$ exists structurally, but $S_0=\hbar$ is not yet a
  completed Level~A theorem;
  \item Schr\"odinger-type reduction is structurally strong, but the
  completed observational quantum equation is still conditional on
  further identifications;
  \item the Born rule is stronger than a mere guess, but still not an
  unconditional bare-postulate theorem;
  \item black-hole information loss is ruled out as a fundamental
  non-unitary resolution, but the constructive strong-field mechanism is
  not yet complete.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{Map of old topics to the present Quantum Sector}

For continuity with earlier drafts, the correspondence is:
\begin{itemize}
  \item loop/winding quantisation
    $\rightarrow$ Sections~\ref{sec:qs_phase_dynamics}
    and~\ref{sec:qs_hbar};
  \item Schr\"odinger-type reduction
    $\rightarrow$ Section~\ref{sec:qs_wave};
  \item canonical structure and commutators
    $\rightarrow$ Section~\ref{sec:qs_ccr};
  \item uncertainty and extremal action
    $\rightarrow$ Sections~\ref{sec:qs_uncertainty}
    and~\ref{sec:qs_extremal_action};
  \item conservation and statistics
    $\rightarrow$ Sections~\ref{sec:qs_conservation},
    \ref{sec:qs_statistics}, and~\ref{sec:qs_dirac};
  \item decoherence, influence functionals, and effective entropy
    $\rightarrow$ Section~\ref{sec:qs_decoherence};
  \item Born-type probability assignment
    $\rightarrow$ Section~\ref{sec:qs_born};
  \item vacuum response (Casimir, particle production, Unruh, Hawking)
    $\rightarrow$ Sections~\ref{sec:qs_vacuum_intro}--
    \ref{sec:qs_vacuum_summary};
  \item defect sectors and dark-sector bridge
    $\rightarrow$ Section~\ref{sec:qs_defects};
  \item black holes and information-loss logic
    $\rightarrow$ Section~\ref{sec:qs_black_holes}.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{Compatibility labels}

To preserve backward compatibility with earlier internal references,
the labels
\label{sec:loops}
\label{sec:CCR}
\label{par:real_vs_complex}
are retained here as compatibility anchors only.
They should not be interpreted as signalling surviving independent
legacy derivations.
Their physical content is now developed in the coherent-topological
Quantum Sector proper.

\subsection*{Interpretive conclusion}

This section should therefore be read as a bridge, not as a second,
parallel quantum theory inside the paper.
The old quantum language has not been discarded; it has been absorbed,
reclassified, and redistributed into a more precise coherent-branch
architecture.
That is why the article becomes shorter here without becoming
physically poorer: the real development now lives in the new QS block,
and this section explains how to read that transition correctly.

\paragraph{Practical reading instruction.}
A reader familiar with older ECT drafts should therefore use this
section as a translation layer.
The real quantum development of the present article is no longer here,
but in the coherent-topological Quantum Sector itself.
This section exists to prevent discontinuity of interpretation, not to
recreate the older structure in parallel.
