\paragraph{The pre-Lorentzian Euclidean scenario~(Level~B).}

\textit{All content in this paragraph and the two following is
a Level~B cosmological scenario, not a theorem derived from bare~P3.
The scenario is structurally motivated by the postulate architecture
(P1--P4), but quantitative details require explicit dynamics of the
effective order-field potential~(OP3).}

The most distinctive structural difference between ECT and $\Lambda$CDM
is the admission of a pre-Lorentzian Euclidean regime.
In $\Lambda$CDM the classical theory is undefined before $t_{\rm Pl}$,
and the initial singularity marks the formal boundary.
In the ECT macroscopic closure scenario~(Level~B), the four-dimensional
Euclidean manifold $\mathcal{M}=\mathbb{R}^4$ is posited to be active
prior to the ordering transition.  In this pre-Lorentzian regime the
$O(4)$ symmetry is unbroken, the Lorentzian metric and causal structure
are not yet established, and temporal evolution in the Lorentzian sense
is absent.  Lorentzian signature, causal structure, and the macroscopic
arrow of time are all structurally motivated consequences of the
$O(4)\to O(3)$ ordering transition (Level~A in the broken-phase EFT;
see Section~\ref{sec:mp_cosmo}).
This is an ECT-inspired scenario; the explicit dynamics of the transition
itself require OP3.

\paragraph{Two possible far-future branches~(Level~B closure-dependent scenarios).}

The long-term fate of the ordered Lorentzian domain depends on the
asymptotic behaviour of the effective Lorentz-order variables.
Within the present $\phi$-first macroscopic closure two structurally
distinct branches are possible~(Level~B; both require explicit
order-field dynamics, OP3):
\begin{itemize}
  \item \textbf{Scenario~A} ($\chi\to\chi_\infty=\text{const}$,
    Level~B): the macroscopic ordering variables stabilise; the
    geometric branch remains active with $G_{\rm eff}\approx G_N$
    and the universe enters an asymptotic de~Sitter-like phase.
    This is the structurally simpler branch and qualitatively
    compatible with current observations.
  \item \textbf{Scenario~B} ($\chi\to0$, Level~B speculative):
    the ordering variables relax toward the Euclidean phase on
    a closure-dependent timescale; the macroscopic closure formally
    drives $G_{\rm eff}$ upward as $\chi$ decreases, eventually
    driving a possible recollapse of the ordered domain.
    The quantitative timescale is closure-dependent~(OP3) and
    not a fixed prediction of ECT.
\end{itemize}
The key observational discriminant between the two scenarios is
$|\dot{G}/G|$ (sensitivity expected from next-generation lunar
laser ranging and pulsar timing) and non-zero $w_a$ from future
BAO surveys.  Current data are consistent with both.

\paragraph{Schematic evolution of the ordered branch~(Level~B closure).}

In the ECT macroscopic closure scenario, the evolution across
cosmological epochs can be summarised schematically as follows
(all statements Level~B; explicit field dynamics require OP3):
\begin{itemize}
  \item \textit{Pre-Lorentzian regime:} Euclidean condensate phase;
    $O(4)$ symmetry unbroken; Lorentzian metric and causal structure
    absent.
  \item \textit{Ordering transition:} $O(4)\to O(3)$ spontaneous
    symmetry breaking; Lorentzian signature and macroscopic arrow
    of time emerge; effective order-field potential drives the
    condensate to the ordered vacuum.
  \item \textit{Inflation and reheating:} ordering transition
    serves as the candidate inflation mechanism within the
    macroscopic closure; condensate excitations thermalise into
    the SM plasma~(Level~B; reheating mechanism requires OP3).
  \item \textit{From reheating to today:} ordering variables
    approximately stationary; $G_{\rm eff}\approx G_N$;
    residual kinetic energy in the order field acts as dark-energy
    source with $w_0>-1$ (ECT structural prediction; specific value open)~(Level~B closure).
  \item \textit{Far future:} Scenario~A or Scenario~B as above.
\end{itemize}
The three-scale structure of the macroscopic closure
($u_0\sim\bar{M}_{\rm Pl}$, $v_{\rm EW}=246$\,GeV,
$v_{\rm gal}\sim r_0^{-1}$) represents three effective regimes
of the condensate at different scales; connecting them via a
renormalisation-group flow is Open Problem~OP-new-6
(Section~\ref{sec:open_problems}).


\subsubsection*{Universe size, structure, and effective dimensionality}
\label{sec:universe_size}

\textit{Status: Level~B (ECT-inspired cosmological scenario).
The discussion below concerns a possible large-scale completion
of the macroscopic closure in which the ordered Lorentzian domain
is finite and may be embedded in a pre-Lorentzian Euclidean regime.
This is a structurally motivated scenario, not a first-principles
theorem from bare~P3~(OP3).}

\paragraph{Size of the ECT domain.}

In the ECT macroscopic scenario~(Level~B), the physical universe
is a finite ordered Lorentzian domain in which the macroscopic
geometric branch is active. Beyond the causal boundary of this domain
the geometric branch degenerates: the macroscopic closure formally
drives $G_{\rm eff}$ upward, while the Lorentzian geometric description
ceases to remain well-defined~(Level~B scenario;
explicit dynamics requires OP3). The $O(4)$-symmetric
pre-Lorentzian condensate regime is conjectured to take over.

The domain radius $R_{\rm domain}$ can be estimated from the number of
inflationary e-folds $N_e$ and the current Hubble radius $R_H$:
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:R_domain}
R_{\rm domain}
= R_H\, e^{N_e}
= (1.37\times10^{26}\,\text{m})\,e^{60}
\approx 1.56\times10^{52}\,\text{m}
\approx 1.65\times10^{36}\,\text{ly}
\approx 5\times10^{33}\,\text{Gly}.
\end{equation}
This is the causal horizon of the Lorentzian phase, not a boundary in
the sense of an edge or wall.  Beyond $R_{\rm domain}$ the macroscopic geometric branch is conjectured to be
no longer active~(Level~B scenario). The ordered Lorentzian
structure gives way to a pre-Lorentzian condensate regime;
the physical interpretation of this boundary requires OP3.

\textbf{Numerical check.}
$R_H = c/H_0 \approx (3\times10^8\,\text{m/s})/(2.2\times10^{-18}\,\text{s}^{-1}) \approx 1.37\times10^{26}$\,m.
$e^{60}\approx1.14\times10^{26}$, giving
$R_{\rm domain}\approx1.56\times10^{52}$\,m
$\approx1.65\times10^{36}$\,ly $\approx5\times10^{33}$\,Gly.

\paragraph{Effective dimensionality at different scales.}

A characteristic feature of ECT is that the effective dimensionality
of structure depends on the scale of observation through the condensate
coherence properties.

\begin{figure}[H]
\centering
\includegraphics[width=0.95\textwidth]{figures/fig_dimensionality_phi.png}
\caption{Force-law effective dimensionality in ECT.
\textbf{(a)}~$d_{\rm force}(r)$ for three galaxy masses,
computed analytically from the $\phi$-closure
$\mu(g_{\rm obs}/g_\dagger)\,g_{\rm obs} = GM/r^2$.
In the screened regime ($g_{\rm obs} \gg g_\dagger$):
$d_{\rm force} \to 3$ (Newtonian).
Beyond the transition radius $r_* = \sqrt{GM/g_\dagger}$
(filled dots): $d_{\rm force} \to 2$
($g \propto 1/r \Rightarrow v_{\rm flat} = \mathrm{const}$).
At $r_*$ (where $x = g_{\rm obs}/g_\dagger = 1$):
$d_{\rm force} = 7/3 \approx 2.33$.
Curves fade beyond the isolation radius ($\sim 1$--$3\,$Mpc),
where the single-galaxy approximation breaks down.
The shaded region at $r > 3\,$Mpc indicates cosmic-web scales
where $d_{\rm force}$ is not yet derivable from the present
$\phi$-closure.
\textbf{(b)}~Universal curve $d_{\rm force}(x)$ with the
closed-form analytic expression
$d_{\rm force} = 1 + 2(1+x^2)/(2+x^2)$;
every galaxy falls on the same curve, because the formula
depends only on $x = g_{\rm obs}/g_\dagger$, not on $M$ or $r$
separately.  Different galaxies differ only in the mapping
$x(r)$: heavier galaxies reach higher $x$ at any given $r$.
This universality is the dimensionality counterpart of the
radial acceleration relation.}
\label{fig:dimensionality}
\end{figure}

\paragraph{Force-law effective dimensionality.}

The effective dimensionality of the gravitational interaction
in ECT is defined by the force-law exponent:
\begin{equation}
d_{\rm force}(r)
\;\equiv\; 1 - \frac{d\ln g_{\rm obs}}{d\ln r}\,.
\label{eq:dforce_def}
\end{equation}
In $d$ spatial dimensions the gravitational force scales as
$g \propto 1/r^{d-1}$; eq.~\eqref{eq:dforce_def} reads off
$d$ from the local force law.

\paragraph{General formula.}
\textit{Note on interpolation function: the $d_{\rm force}$
analysis below uses the analytic closure
$\mu(x)=x/\sqrt{1+x^2}$ for analytical transparency.
The main observational RAR/BTFR comparison
(Section~\ref{sec:mp_galactic}) uses the McGaugh~2016 empirical
form~\cite{McGaugh2016}; the qualitative dimensionality
behaviour is closure-independent.}

Starting from the $\phi$-closure
$\mu(x)\,g_{\rm obs} = g_N(r)$ with $x \equiv g_{\rm obs}/g_\dagger$,
one obtains by logarithmic differentiation:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
d_{\rm force}(r) = 1 + \frac{p_N(r)}
  {1 + \dfrac{d\ln\mu}{d\ln x}}\,,
}
\label{eq:dforce_general}
\end{equation}
where $p_N(r) \equiv -d\ln g_N/d\ln r$.
For a point mass $p_N = 2$.
The derivation is given in Appendix~\ref{app:deff_method}.

\paragraph{Closed-form result.}
For the ECT closure function
$\mu(x) = x/\sqrt{1+x^2}$ one finds
$d\ln\mu/d\ln x = 1/(1+x^2)$, and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
d_{\rm force}(x)
=
1 + 2\,\frac{1+x^2}{2+x^2}
}
\label{eq:dforce_closed}
\end{equation}
for a point-mass Newtonian source $p_N=2$.
Thus:
\begin{itemize}
  \item in the screened Newtonian regime $x\gg1$:
    $d_{\rm force}\to 3$, corresponding to $g\propto 1/r^2$;
  \item in the deep critical regime $x\ll1$:
    $d_{\rm force}\to 2$, corresponding to $g\propto 1/r$
    and asymptotically flat rotation curves;
  \item at the transition point $x=1$:
    $d_{\rm force}(1)=1+\tfrac{4}{3}=\tfrac{7}{3}\approx2.33$.
\end{itemize}

This force-law dimensionality is a macroscopic closure diagnostic
(Level~B), not a theorem about the microscopic topological dimension
of the arena.  It measures how the effective gravitational response
interpolates between Newtonian and critical-branch behaviour.

\paragraph{Size of the ECT domain.}

In the ECT macroscopic scenario~(Level~B), the physical universe
is a finite ordered Lorentzian domain in which the macroscopic
geometric branch is active. Beyond the causal boundary of this domain
the geometric branch degenerates: the macroscopic closure formally
drives $G_{\rm eff}$ upward, while the Lorentzian geometric description
ceases to remain well-defined~(Level~B scenario;
explicit dynamics requires OP3). The $O(4)$-symmetric
pre-Lorentzian condensate regime is conjectured to take over.


\subsubsection*{Physical interpretation}

Cosmology in ECT is the large-scale history of the ordered condensate
branch.
Inflation corresponds to ordering; dark energy corresponds to residual
order-field vacuum energy; variation of $G_{\rm eff}$ reflects the slow
cosmological evolution of the order variable.
These interpretations are not yet first-principles theorems from bare
P3, but they form a consistent and physically motivated closure of the
geometric branch.

\subsubsection*{What is established and what is not}

\textbf{Structurally motivated / developed~(Level~B):}
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
  \item A pre-Lorentzian ordering scenario is natural in ECT.
  \item Homogeneous FLRW branch of the $\phi$-first closure is
    well-defined.
  \item Inflation and dark energy admit natural reinterpretation in
    terms of the ordered condensate branch.
\end{enumerate}

\textbf{Open:}
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
  \item Full nonequilibrium derivation of the ordering transition from
    bare P3.
  \item Microscopic derivation of $U(\phi)$~(OP3).
  \item Quantitative baryogenesis model within the same closure.
  \item Precision cosmological fitting of $G_{\rm eff}(z)$ across
    all datasets.
\end{enumerate}


% ============================================================
\subsection{Galactic sector: the Lorentz-order field}
\label{sec:mp_galactic}
% ============================================================

\textit{Status: all Level~B (phenomenological closure of the
$\phi$-first critical-branch strategy). Not first-principles from
bare~P3. One free parameter $r_0$ per galaxy.}

\subsubsection*{Why the condensate-amplitude route fails}

A direct galactic role of the heavy radial condensate mode is strongly
disfavoured for two independent reasons.

First, under the phenomenological matching hypothesis
$\xi_{\rm cond}\sim\ell_{\rm Pl}$ used in the present ECT closure,
the radial mode is extremely heavy, of order the microscopic cutoff,
so it cannot naturally generate kpc-scale structure.
Attempting to stretch that mode to galactic distances would require an
extreme and radiatively unstable tuning of the underlying parameters.

Second, an ordinary linear scalar-tensor realisation of the same
sector falls into the Brans--Dicke-like regime and generically produces
post-Newtonian deviations far too large for Solar-System data.

For these reasons the galactic branch of ECT is not built from the bare
radial condensate amplitude itself, but from the nonlinear critical
dynamics of the Lorentz-order field~$\phi$.


\begin{figure}[htb]
\centering
\includegraphics[width=0.82\textwidth]{figures/fig_regime_diagram.png}
\caption{ECT regime diagram in the plane of the Lorentz-order
field $\phi$ and local acceleration $g/g_\dagger$.  Different
physical regimes --- Quantum/Planckian, Newtonian (GR),
MOND-like critical branch, and deep-MOND / void ---
are controlled by the local degree of Lorentzian ordering.
Dense environments (high $\phi$) are screened and recover
standard GR; dilute outskirts and voids approach the critical
boundary where the nonlinear $\phi$-branch activates.
Representative astrophysical systems are indicated.}
\label{fig:regime_diagram}
\end{figure}

%%% -----------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Screening in dense environments}
\label{subsec:lof_screening}

\textit{Status: Level~B (phenomenological $\phi$-first closure).
The screening mechanism follows from the $\phi$-equation of
motion~\eqref{eq:phi_eom} under the quasi-static approximation;
a first-principles derivation from bare~P3 remains open~(OP-screen).}

Once the local condensate shifts $\bar\phi(\rho)$ upward in
denser environments, the Lorentz-order field acquires an
effective mass for perturbations around the local equilibrium.
Expanding $\phi = \bar\phi(\rho) + \delta\phi$, small fluctuations
obey a Yukawa-type equation with effective mass (Level~B):
\begin{equation}
m_\phi^2(\rho)
= \frac{U_0''(\bar\phi(\rho))
        + 4\pi\rho/(\bar\chi^2 c^2)}
       {K(\bar\phi(\rho))}\,.
\label{eq:mphi_main}
\end{equation}
Both numerator terms are positive and increase with $\rho$ for
convex $U_0$; in the one-loop estimate $K \propto e^{-\phi/2}$,
which \emph{decreases} at larger $\bar\phi$ and thus reinforces
the growth of $m_\phi^2$ (Level~B; $U_0$ not yet derived from
bare~P3, OP3).  Hence $m_\phi$ grows with density,
and the Yukawa screening length $\lambda_\phi = 1/m_\phi$ shrinks
in dense environments. This is the mechanism that screens
the fifth-force contribution of $\phi$ inside galaxies and in the
Solar System, rendering the theory consistent with the Cassini
bound~\cite{Bertotti2003}~(Level~B).

\paragraph{Physical interpretation.}
In the present framework, screening is not an external fix
appended to save the theory. It is a direct consequence of the
fact that dense matter holds the vacuum in a deep Lorentzian
phase, where the order-field sector is effectively frozen.
The recovery of GR in the Solar System is therefore not in
conflict with the existence of a nonlinear galactic branch;
it is an expected feature of the same underlying mechanism.


%%% -----------------------------------------------------------
%%% -----------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Hierarchy of length scales}
\label{subsec:lof_scales}

\textit{Status: Level~A for the identification of distinct
physical scales; Level~B for numerical estimates based on the
$\phi$-first phenomenological closure.}

The galactic closure of the macroscopic branch contains several
physically distinct scales that must not be conflated.

\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
  \item \textbf{Microscopic condensate scale.}
  The correlation length of the heavy radial mode,
  $\xi_{\rm cond}\sim m_\sigma^{-1}\sim\ell_{\rm Pl}$,
  marks the breakdown of the coarse-grained geometric EFT.
  This scale plays no role in galactic dynamics.

  \item \textbf{Environmental screening length.}
  In regions of high baryonic density the $\phi$-branch
  is driven into the screened Newtonian regime; the
  corresponding Yukawa screening length $\lambda_\phi(\rho)=m_\phi^{-1}(\rho)$
  is density-dependent~(Level~B; eq.~\eqref{eq:mphi_main}).
  This scale governs Solar-System and laboratory suppression
  of the fifth-force correction.

  \item \textbf{Critical galactic transition scale.}
  The transition from screened Newtonian behaviour to the
  critical $\phi$-branch is governed by the acceleration scale
  $g_\dagger$, or equivalently by the galactic transition
  radius $r_0=\sqrt{GM_{\rm bar}/g_\dagger}$.
  This is the characteristic IR scale of the galactic closure.

  \item \textbf{Cosmological reference scale.}
  In the present closure, $g_\dagger\sim cH_0$, which explains
  the quasi-universality of the acceleration scale while still
  allowing environment-dependent deviations~(Level~B).
\end{enumerate}

The four scales form a clear hierarchy:
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:scale_hierarchy}
\xi_{\rm cond}
\;\ll\;
\lambda_\phi(\rho)
\;\lesssim\;
r_0
\;\ll\;
H_0^{-1}.
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Physical significance.}
This hierarchy explains why ECT can simultaneously exhibit:
(i)~a strongly ordered microscopic vacuum,
(ii)~screened Solar-System and laboratory behaviour,
(iii)~critical galactic $\phi$-branch phenomenology, and
(iv)~a quasi-universal cosmological acceleration scale.
The success of the galactic closure depends precisely on keeping
these scales conceptually distinct.

\subsubsection*{One-loop bridge and breakdown near criticality}
\label{subsec:lof_oneloop}

\textit{Status: Level~B (one-loop EFT estimate within the
$\phi$-first macroscopic closure; the one-loop coefficient
$a\simeq 1/2$ is scheme-dependent and constitutes an open
problem, OP-screen; see Appendix~\ref{app:lof:oneloop_calc}).}

The next question is what happens as the ambient density decreases
and the vacuum approaches the critical region. Integrating out the
fast Goldstone modes generates a nontrivial kinetic response for
$\phi$ (the one-loop calculation is presented in
Appendix~\ref{app:lof:oneloop_calc}). At the one-loop level this
can be parametrised as
\begin{equation}
K(\phi) \propto e^{-a\phi}\,,
\qquad a > 0\,,
\label{eq:kphi_main}
\end{equation}
with the one-loop estimate suggesting $a \simeq 1/2$. The precise coefficient is scheme-dependent~(Level~B; OP-screen) and
should not be overinterpreted,
but the qualitative structural point is robust~(Level~B): the effective quadratic kinetic
sector acquires a strong $\phi$-dependence near the critical region.

Higher-order gradient terms become increasingly important in the
same limit. A generic static expansion takes the form
\begin{equation}
\Gamma[\phi]
= \int d^3x\left[
  \frac{K(\phi)}{2}(\nabla\phi)^2
  + \frac{L(\phi)}{3}|\nabla\phi|^3
  + \cdots
\right].
\label{eq:gamma_gradient_main}
\end{equation}
If the ratio $L(\phi)/K(\phi)$ grows toward criticality
(which is expected on general EFT grounds: near criticality,
higher-gradient operators become increasingly sensitive to
the small Lorentz-order parameter and may therefore outgrow
the quadratic sector, even if their detailed coefficients are
not yet known from first principles), then
the field-dependent transition gradient
\begin{equation}
|\nabla\phi|_{\rm trans}(\phi)
= \frac{K(\phi)}{L(\phi)}
\;\xrightarrow[\phi\to-\infty]{}\; 0
\label{eq:transition_gradient_main}
\end{equation}
falls toward zero.

\paragraph{Resolution of the regime-ordering problem.}
This observation resolves a crucial difficulty that plagues
constant-threshold nonlinear models. If the transition scale were
a fixed constant, the nonlinear (MOND-like) regime would activate
at \emph{large} gradients (near masses) and the linear (Newtonian)
regime at \emph{small} gradients (far away) --- the opposite of
what is observed. With a field-dependent threshold:
\begin{itemize}
\item Near massive bodies ($\bar\phi > 0$, deep Lorentzian phase):
  $|\nabla\phi|_{\rm trans}$ is large, so the system stays in its
  linear screened branch.
\item On galactic outskirts ($\bar\phi \to 0^-$, near-critical):
  $|\nabla\phi|_{\rm trans} \to 0$, so even weak gradients
  activate the nonlinear branch.
\end{itemize}
This gives the physically correct ordering: GR near masses,
MOND-like dynamics in dilute regions.

The exact scaling of $L(\phi)$ is not yet fully derived from the
microscopic theory; accordingly, this step should be viewed as
EFT-supported rather than fully established. The essential
requirement is the hierarchy $L/K \to \infty$ near criticality,
not any specific exponent.


%%% -----------------------------------------------------------
%%% -----------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Critical infrared regime}
\label{subsec:lof_critical}

\textit{Status: Level~B (phenomenological critical infrared
closure of the $\phi$-first macroscopic branch). The
$Y_\phi^{3/2}$ critical kinetic form is supported by a
scale-invariance argument, but not yet derived from bare~P3~(OP2).}

Once the perturbative gradient expansion breaks down, it is
natural to replace it by a critical infrared effective theory for
the dimensionless order field $\phi$. Defining
$Y_\phi \equiv (\nabla\phi)^2$, the deep-IR static free energy
can be written as
\begin{equation}
F_{\rm IR}[\phi]
= \int d^3x\left[
  \Lambda^4\,\mathcal{F}\!\left(\frac{Y_\phi}{Y_*}\right)
  + U_{\rm eff}(\phi;\rho)
\right].
\label{eq:fir_main}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Scale-invariance argument~(Level~B).}
At a 3D scale-invariant fixed point, if $\phi$ is treated as
dimensionless ($[\phi] = 0$), then $[Y_\phi] = L^{-2}$ and
the free-energy density must have dimension $L^{-3}$.  For a
power-law $\mathcal{F} \sim Y_\phi^p$:
\begin{equation}
[Y_\phi^p] = L^{-2p} \;\stackrel{!}{=}\; L^{-3}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\boxed{p = 3/2\,.}
\end{equation}
This is not a claim of absolute uniqueness among all conceivable
nonlocal or logarithmically corrected structures. Rather, it is
the unique simple local power-law form built only from $Y_\phi$
that is consistent with 3D scale invariance when $[\phi] = 0$.
(An anomalous dimension $\Delta_\phi \neq 0$ would shift the
exponent to $p = 3/[2(1+\Delta_\phi)]$; for a Lorentz-order
parameter this correction is expected to be small.)

\paragraph{Physical interpretation.}
The $Y_\phi^{3/2}$ form means that at criticality the ``cost''
of a gradient in $\phi$ grows faster than quadratic: the system
resists non-uniformity in the degree of Lorentzianness more
strongly than a linear theory would predict.  This nonlinear
stiffness is what produces the $1/r$ force law needed for flat
rotation curves.

\paragraph{Full interpolating equation.}
The complete static equation, valid from the Newtonian to the
deep-MOND regime, takes the AQUAL-like form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\nabla\cdot\left[
  \mu_\phi\!\left(
    \frac{|\nabla\phi|}{\phi_*(\phi)}
  \right)\nabla\phi
\right]
= \frac{4\pi\rho}{c^2}\,,
}
\label{eq:aqual_phi_main}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\mu_\phi(x) \to 1 \quad (x \ll 1)\,,
\qquad
\mu_\phi(x) \to x \quad (x \gg 1)\,.
\label{eq:mu_limits_main}
\end{equation}
The key structural difference from standard MOND is that the
transition scale $\phi_*(\phi)$ depends on the local
Lorentz-order background. This field dependence is what makes
the nonlinear branch appear in dilute near-critical regions
rather than near dense sources.


%%% -----------------------------------------------------------

\subsection{Early galaxy and black hole formation (JWST anomalies)}
\label{sec:jwst}

\textit{Observational context.}
The James Webb Space Telescope has revealed a population of unexpectedly massive
galaxies and supermassive black holes at redshifts $z>10$, corresponding to
cosmic ages $<500$\,Myr after the Big Bang \cite{Labbe2023,Finkelstein2022}.
The observed stellar masses ($M_\star\sim 10^{9}$--$10^{11}\,M_\odot$) and black-hole
masses ($M_{\rm BH}\sim 10^{7}$--$10^{9}\,M_\odot$) exceed the expectations of
standard $\Lambda$CDM by factors of several within the available assembly time.

\textit{ECT mechanism ($\phi$-first).}
In ECT $\phi$-logic, the effective gravitational coupling on the
cosmological background is controlled by the background order field
$\phi_b(z)$ (Section~\ref{sec:mp_nonlinear}):
\begin{equation}
  G_{\rm eff}(z) = G_N\,e^{-\phi_b(z)},
  \qquad
  M^2_{\rm eff}(z) = \bar M^2_{\rm Pl}\,e^{\phi_b(z)}.
  \label{eq:Geff_jwst}
\end{equation}
This is the same relation that governs the nonlinear gravity and
galactic-scale $\phi$-branch — a single order field unifies the
cosmological and galactic gravitational sectors.

The full field decomposes as $\phi(X)=\phi_b(z)+\delta\phi(X)$,
where $\phi_b(z)$ is the slowly evolving cosmological background
and $\delta\phi(X)$ encodes local deviations.
The $\phi$-logic suggests qualitatively that dense collapsing
regions may screen $\delta\phi$, driving the local dynamics back
toward the GR branch; a derivation of this screening from the
nonlinear $\phi$-equation remains open.

\textit{Background structure.}
The $\phi$-first framework identifies the cosmological background
as a slowly evolving order field $\phi_b(z)$, with
\begin{equation}
  G_{\rm eff}(z) = G_N\,e^{-\phi_b(z)}.
  \label{eq:phi_b_ansatz}
\end{equation}
The specific functional form of $\phi_b(z)$ is not yet derived
from the ECT background equations; a first-principles solution
of the coupled $\phi$--Friedmann system remains an open problem.
Any specific numerical parameterisation (such as a power-law ansatz)
should be treated as an illustrative closure, not a prediction.
A power-law profile $\phi_b(z)=-2\varepsilon\ln(1+z)$ would recover
$G_{\rm eff}(z)=G_N(1+z)^{2\varepsilon}$, but any specific $\varepsilon$
should be treated as an illustrative closure only.

\textit{Structure growth.}
In the leading sub-horizon approximation, and neglecting explicit
perturbations of the $\phi$-sector in the growth equation, one may
write the standard continuity--Euler--Poisson system with the
effective coupling:
\begin{equation}
  \ddot\delta + 2H\dot\delta
  - 4\pi G_{\rm eff}(z)\,\bar\rho\,\delta = 0.
\end{equation}
At leading order in $\varepsilon$ this gives
\begin{equation}
  \frac{D_{\rm ECT}(z)}{D_{\Lambda{\rm CDM}}(z)}
  \approx 1 + \varepsilon\ln(1+z) + O(\varepsilon^2).
\end{equation}
At $z=10$: $D_{\rm ECT}/D_{\Lambda{\rm CDM}}\approx 1.024$.

\textit{Halo abundance (Press--Schechter).}
Setting $f(z)\equiv G_{\rm eff}(z)/G_N = e^{-\phi_b(z)}$,
the effective rarity of a $\nu$-$\sigma$ peak becomes
$\nu_{\rm eff}=\nu/\sqrt{f}$, giving
\begin{equation}
  \frac{n_{\rm ECT}}{n_{\Lambda{\rm CDM}}}
  = \exp\!\left[\frac{\nu^2}{2}\!\left(1-\frac{1}{f(z)}\right)\right].
  \label{eq:PS_phi}
\end{equation}
Illustrative values for a slow-roll background profile are given in
Table~\ref{tab:jwst_ps}; they are \emph{unchanged} from the
previous estimate --- the improvement here is conceptual
(unified $\phi$-language with the gravity section) rather than
numerical.

\begin{table}[H]
\centering
\caption{Halo abundance enhancement in ECT vs.\ $\Lambda$CDM,
eq.~\eqref{eq:PS_phi} for an illustrative slow-roll profile.
$\nu$ = peak rarity parameter; JWST anomalies correspond to
$\nu\sim5$--6.
The ansatz $\phi_b(z)=-2\varepsilon\ln(1+z)$ gives $f(z)=e^{-\phi_b}$;
specific $\varepsilon$ is illustrative only.}
\label{tab:jwst_ps}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{ccccc}
\hline
$z$ & $\phi_b(z)$ & $f=e^{-\phi_b}$ & $\nu=5$ & $\nu=6$ \\
\hline
 7  & $-0.043$ & 1.043 & $\times 1.7$ & $\times 2.1$ \\
10  & $-0.048$ & 1.049 & $\times 1.8$ & $\times 2.3$ \\
12  & $-0.052$ & 1.053 & $\times 1.9$ & $\times 2.5$ \\
15  & $-0.055$ & 1.057 & $\times 2.0$ & $\times 2.6$ \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{table}

\textit{Quantitative assessment.}
For the most anomalous JWST sources ($\nu\sim5$--6),
the ECT $\phi$-mechanism predicts an overabundance of $\times2$--3
relative to $\Lambda$CDM.
The observed deficit is $\times10$--100~\cite{BoylanKolchin2023},
so in its present controlled $\phi$-first form ECT \emph{alleviates
but does not resolve} the JWST early-structure tension.
With the background ansatz~\eqref{eq:phi_b_ansatz}, no additional
numerical improvement over the leading-order estimate is obtained.

The $\phi$-logic suggests that early-time global enhancement
($\phi_b<0$) and local screening in dense proto-galactic cores
may ultimately be described within a single order-field framework.
A derivation of this mechanism from the full nonlinear $\phi$-equation,
and the question of whether a nontrivial background history $\phi_b(z)$
could provide stronger early enhancement, are left as open problems
(Section~\ref{sec:open_problems}).

The late-time background apparatus developed in
Appendices~\ref{app:late_cosmo_background} and~\ref{app:late_cosmo_algorithm}
provides the first controlled connection between the Hubble tension, the
age of the Universe, and the JWST background effects in ECT.  The same
$\phi$-background drift that shifts the inferred late $H_0$ also modifies
luminosity distances to high-$z$ galaxies, the lookback time available
for early structure formation, and the effective growth environment; see
Fig.~\ref{fig:ect_hubble_jwst_background} and
Table~\ref{tab:ect_hubble_jwst_summary}.

sense: status entries reflect the Level~A / Level~B / Open discipline established
in the revised postulate structure.

\section{Comparison with Existing Approaches}
\label{sec:comparison}

This section compares ECT with several alternative approaches
to gravity and cosmology, highlighting structural differences
and shared features.

\subsection{Galactic dynamics: BTFR, rotation curves, and the effective critical scale}
\label{sec:galactic_dynamics}


\subsubsection*{Matter stabilises the Lorentzian phase}

From the $\phi$-equation of motion~(varying \eqref{eq:phi_first_action}
and combining with the Einstein equation trace):
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:phi_eom}
  \mathcal{K}(\phi)\,\Box\phi \approx
  \frac{8\pi G_N}{c^4}\,\rho_{\rm bar}\,\xi_1(\phi),
  \qquad \xi_1\sim O(1),
\end{equation}
matter drives $\phi>0$: the condensate becomes more ordered near
baryons~(Level~B from field equations).

\subsubsection*{The critical branch $\mathcal{F}\propto Y_\phi^{3/2}$}

The effective galactic Lagrangian for $\phi$:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:phi_galactic}
  \mathcal{L}_\phi = \frac{\bar M_{\rm Pl}^2}{2}\,\mathcal{F}(Y_\phi),
  \qquad
  Y_\phi \equiv -\frac{(\partial_\mu\phi)^2}{2M_\phi^4}.
\end{equation}
In the critical branch $\mathcal{F}=A_{\rm ECT}Y_\phi^{3/2}$:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:critical_branch}
  \mathcal{L}_\phi^{\rm crit}
  = -\frac{\bar M_{\rm Pl}^2 A_{\rm ECT}}{2M_\phi^4}\,
  |(\partial_\mu\phi)^2|^{3/2},
\end{equation}
producing MOND-like dynamics in deep weak fields without a fifth force
in the screened limit.

\subsubsection*{Baryonic Tully--Fisher Relation}

In the critical branch:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:BTFR}
  v_{\rm flat}^4 = G_N M_{\rm bar}\,g_\dagger,
  \qquad
  g_\dagger \equiv c^2\sqrt{\frac{A_{\rm ECT}}{M_\phi^4\bar M_{\rm Pl}^2}},
\end{equation}
with $g_\dagger\propto cH_0$: BTFR as exact algebraic consequence of the
critical branch~(Level~B).

\paragraph{Numerical bridge to the SPARC fits.}
The galactic SPARC analysis below provides a direct numerical
realisation of this analytic result.  In the present closure language
the BTFR slope remains structural, while the normalisation is governed
by the effective galactic critical scale $g^\dagger_{\rm eff}$.  The
sample-level fits show that the preferred baseline value is of order
$cH_0/(2\pi)$, with the residual scatter interpreted as an effective
environmental renormalisation rather than a failure of the critical
branch itself.

\begin{figure}[htb]
\centering
\includegraphics[width=0.90\linewidth]{figures/ect_btfr_new_bw.pdf}
\caption{ECT BTFR test from the new SPARC galactic closure.  The points
show the effective outer baryonic mass proxy
$M_{\rm bar,eff}=R_{\rm tail}^2 g_N(R_{\rm tail})/G_N$ inferred from the
same baryonic decomposition used in the rotation-curve fits, plotted
against the observed outer-tail velocity estimator $V_{\rm flat}$.
The solid line shows the ECT baseline relation
$V_{\rm flat}^4=G_N M_{\rm bar,eff} g^\dagger_0$ with
$g^\dagger_0=cH_0/(2\pi)$, while the dashed line shows the MOND
reference line with $a_0$.  This figure should be read as an
internally consistent BTFR test of the new ECT closure, not yet as a
replacement for the standard catalogue-level BTFR built from an
independent global baryonic-mass table.}
\label{fig:btfr_new_main}
\end{figure}

The resulting BTFR test shows that the new galactic closure reproduces
the expected quartic scaling in a numerically stable way.  Because the
present implementation uses an internal outer-mass proxy
$M_{\rm bar,eff}$ derived from the same fitted SPARC decomposition, this
plot should be interpreted as a self-consistency test of the new ECT
galactic machinery rather than as the final catalogue-level BTFR
benchmark.  The latter can be added later by replacing
$M_{\rm bar,eff}$ with an independently tabulated total baryonic mass.

\subsubsection*{Practical ECT closure for rotation curves}

The galactic sector of the $\phi$-first formulation is treated as a
nonlinear static response problem for the effective gravitational
potential $\Phi$. In the screened regime the theory reduces to the
ordinary Newtonian/GR branch, whereas in the dilute critical regime the
infrared free-energy density is controlled by the non-quadratic
Lorentz-order-field term
\[
\mathcal{F}_{\rm IR}\propto Y_\phi^{3/2},
\qquad
Y_\phi=(\nabla\phi)^2.
\]
A full first-principles derivation of the interpolation family from the
bare condensate action is not yet available. The present work therefore
adopts the phenomenologically simplest smooth closure that is
compatible with both required asymptotic branches.

For practical rotation-curve fitting we use the effective acceleration law
\begin{equation}
g(R)=\frac{1}{2}\left[g_N(R)+\sqrt{g_N^2(R)+4\,g_N(R)\,g^\dagger_{\rm eff}}\right],
\label{eq:ect_rotation_closure_main}
\end{equation}
where $g_N(R)$ is the baryonic Newtonian acceleration inferred from the
SPARC mass model and $g^\dagger_{\rm eff}$ is the effective critical
acceleration scale of the given galaxy. This closure is not presented
as a Level~A theorem of bare P3; it is the minimal Level~B
interpolation consistent with the screened Newtonian limit
\[
g\to g_N \qquad (g_N\gg g^\dagger_{\rm eff}),
\]
and the deep critical branch
\[
g\to \sqrt{g_N g^\dagger_{\rm eff}}
\qquad (g_N\ll g^\dagger_{\rm eff}),
\]
the latter leading directly to the BTFR.

The practical baryonic input is computed from the SPARC decomposition as
\begin{equation}
g_N(R)=
\frac{
V_{\rm gas}^2(R)+\Upsilon_{\rm d}V_{\rm disk}^2(R)+
\Upsilon_{\rm b}V_{\rm bul}^2(R)
}{R},
\label{eq:gn_sparc_main}
\end{equation}
with either fixed stellar mass-to-light ratios
($\Upsilon_{\rm d}=0.5$, $\Upsilon_{\rm b}=0.7$) or a free disk
mass-to-light ratio $\Upsilon_{\rm d}$.

\subsubsection*{SPARC sample fits and model comparison}

We fitted the closure~\eqref{eq:ect_rotation_closure_main} to the SPARC
mass-model sample. The fixed-$M/L$ mode provides the cleaner test of
the ECT galactic closure because it removes the strongest stellar disk
$M/L$ degeneracy. In that mode the fitted sample gives
\[
{\rm median}\!\left(g^\dagger_{\rm eff}/(cH_0/2\pi)\right)\approx 0.86,
\]
while the clean sub-sample yields
\[
{\rm median}\!\left(g^\dagger_{\rm eff}/(cH_0/2\pi)\right)\approx 0.94.
\]
This does not prove the coefficient $1/(2\pi)$, but it strongly
supports the claim that the preferred ECT galactic acceleration scale
is of order $cH_0/(2\pi)$ rather than $cH_0$.

At the sample level the new ECT closure is numerically competitive with
MOND on comparable parameter footing. In the fixed-$M/L$ mode the
median reduced $\chi^2$ is lower than in the MOND benchmark fits,
whereas $\Lambda$CDM still performs better in a purely numerical sense,
as expected for a more flexible halo family with more parameters.
Allowing the disk $M/L$ ratio to vary improves the ECT fit further, but
this improvement must be interpreted cautiously because it partly tracks
the reintroduction of the strongest nuisance degeneracy in the galactic
problem.  The correct conclusion is therefore not that ECT has already
surpassed all competing models, but that the minimal $\phi$-branch
closure is numerically viable, competitive with MOND, and naturally
tied to a cosmological acceleration scale.

\begin{figure*}[htb]
\centering
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth]{figures/set2_sparc_sample.pdf}
\caption{Representative SPARC rotation curves fitted with the new ECT
galactic closure in the fixed-$M/L$ mode. Black points with error bars
show the observed rotation velocities. The baryons-only Newtonian
contribution is shown separately, together with the best-fit ECT curve,
the baseline ECT curve corresponding to $g^\dagger_0=cH_0/(2\pi)$, and
the MOND and $\Lambda$CDM comparison curves produced by the same
numerical pipeline. Where displayed, auxiliary fit statistics such as
$\chi_r^2$ and AIC are shown for visual comparison only.  The fits use
the new algebraic closure \eqref{eq:ect_rotation_closure_main}, not the
older empirical RAR interpolation used in preliminary versions of the
manuscript.}
\label{fig:sparc_sample_new}
\end{figure*}

$\Lambda$CDM/NFW. The fixed-$M/L$ ECT mode provides the cleaner test of
the galactic critical scale because it removes the strongest stellar
disk $M/L$ degeneracy, while the free-$M/L$ mode shows the best-fit
performance once that nuisance freedom is restored.}
\label{fig:chi2_comparison_main}
\end{figure}

\subsubsection*{Interpretation of the effective critical scale}

A key distinction from standard MOND is that ECT does not require the
critical acceleration scale to be exactly universal. The SPARC fits are
best interpreted in terms of an effective quantity
\[
g^\dagger_{\rm eff}=g^\dagger_0\,Z_{\rm env},
\]
where $g^\dagger_0$ is the cosmological baseline and $Z_{\rm env}$
captures residual environmental and branch-state dependence.

The fitted values cluster around the loop-motivated baseline
\[
g^\dagger_0 \sim \frac{cH_0}{2\pi},
\]
but retain a substantial galaxy-to-galaxy scatter. This scatter should
not yet be over-interpreted. At the current stage it may contain both
genuinely physical environment dependence and residual modelling
systematics, especially from stellar $M/L$ choices, bulge treatment,
and the still incomplete implementation of an external-field sector.

\begin{figure*}[htb]
\centering
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth]{figures/fig_gdagger_analysis_new_bw.pdf}
\caption{Summary analysis of the fitted effective critical scale in the
new ECT galactic pipeline.  Panel~(a) shows the fitted
$g^\dagger_{\rm eff}$ values against the effective outer baryonic-mass
proxy, together with the MOND reference $a_0$ and the ECT baseline
$cH_0/(2\pi)$.  Panel~(b) shows selected representative systems and
their deviation from a strictly universal MOND acceleration scale.  The
figure summarises the central galactic conclusion of the present ECT
analysis: a cosmological baseline scale is preferred, but strict
universality is not required.}
\label{fig:gdagger_analysis_new_main}
\end{figure*}


The two-panel $g^\dagger$ analysis condenses the sample-level result
into a more transparent diagnostic than the earlier legacy
$\phi_{\rm env}$ plot.  The left panel shows that the fitted critical
scale clusters around a cosmological baseline rather than around a
strictly universal MOND constant, while the right panel visualises how
representative galaxies deviate from the universal-$a_0$ picture by
different amounts.  This should not yet be over-read as a completed
environment theory, but it strongly motivates the ECT interpretation in
which $g^\dagger_{\rm eff}$ is an effective branch-dependent quantity
rather than a fundamental universal constant.

\subsubsection*{Milky Way as a representative case}

The Milky Way deserves separate display because it combines a precise
local rotation-curve reconstruction with particular relevance for
testing whether the effective critical scale must be exactly universal.
As a well-measured single system, it also provides a useful anchor
between the sample-level histogram of fitted $g^\dagger_{\rm eff}$ and
the detailed shape of an individual rotation curve.  The fit shown in
Fig.~\ref{fig:mw_new} gives
\[
g^\dagger_{\rm eff}\approx 1.72\,(cH_0/2\pi),
\]
illustrating that the ECT galactic scale need not be strictly
universal even when the cosmological baseline is fixed.

\begin{figure}[htb]
\centering
\includegraphics[width=0.82\linewidth]{figures/set1_milky_way.pdf}
\caption{Milky Way rotation-curve fit in the new ECT galactic closure.
The figure compares the best-fit ECT curve, the baseline
$g^\dagger_0=cH_0/(2\pi)$ curve, the baryonic disk model, and the MOND
and $\Lambda$CDM comparison curves from the same numerical pipeline.
The shaded/supplementary sensitivity band, where shown, represents only
order-unity variations of the effective critical scale and is not
interpreted here as a completed physical EFE calculation.  The best-fit
effective critical scale is
$g^\dagger_{\rm eff}\approx1.72\,(cH_0/2\pi)$.}
\label{fig:mw_new}
\end{figure}

\subsection{Radial Acceleration Relation}

The RAR provides a complementary representation of the same galactic
closure tested in the rotation-curve analysis.  Instead of plotting
$V(R)$ directly, it compares the observed acceleration
\[
g_{\rm obs}(R)=\frac{V_{\rm obs}^2(R)}{R}
\]
with the baryonic Newtonian acceleration
\[
g_{\rm bar}(R)=\frac{V_{\rm gas}^2(R)+\Upsilon_{\rm d}V_{\rm disk}^2(R)+
\Upsilon_{\rm b}V_{\rm bul}^2(R)}{R}.
\]
In the present ECT closure the corresponding predicted relation is
\begin{equation}
g_{\rm ECT}(R)=\frac{1}{2}\left[g_{\rm bar}(R)+
\sqrt{g_{\rm bar}^2(R)+4\,g_{\rm bar}(R)\,g^\dagger_{\rm eff}}\right],
\label{eq:rar_ect_new}
\end{equation}
to be compared with the universal-$a_0$ MOND relation obtained by the
replacement $g^\dagger_{\rm eff}\to a_0$.

Figure~\ref{fig:rar_new_main} shows the new six-panel RAR diagnostic.
Panels (a)--(e) display representative galaxies spanning dwarf, spiral,
edge-on, and giant-spiral systems.  Panel~(f) shows the full SPARC cloud
together with the same selected galaxies and the baseline ECT branch.

\begin{figure*}[htb]
\centering
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth]{figures/ect_rar_new_6panel_bw.pdf}
\caption{RAR from the new ECT galactic closure.  Panels~(a)--(e) show
representative galaxies; panel~(f) shows the full SPARC cloud together
with the selected systems.  Black solid lines denote the fitted ECT
closure, dashed lines denote MOND with universal $a_0$, and the grey
diagonal marks the Newtonian limit $g_{\rm obs}=g_{\rm bar}$.  The ECT
curves are computed from the new practical closure
\eqref{eq:ect_rotation_closure_main} using the same fitted
$g^\dagger_{\rm eff}$ values as in the rotation-curve analysis.}
\label{fig:rar_new_main}
\end{figure*}

The RAR representation confirms the same structural picture seen in the
rotation curves: the ECT branch reduces to the Newtonian regime at large
$g_{\rm bar}$, approaches the critical square-root branch at small
$g_{\rm bar}$, and naturally allows galaxy-to-galaxy variation through
$g^\dagger_{\rm eff}$.  In this sense the RAR is not an independent fit
law added on top of the theory, but a different projection of the same
galactic closure already used in the SPARC velocity analysis.
% ============================================================
\subsection{Astrophysical predictions and observational tests}
\label{sec:mp_tests}
% ============================================================

\textit{Status: all Level~B unless explicitly noted.}

\subsubsection*{Late-time cosmology: Hubble tension, age, and JWST implications}
\label{sec:hubble_jwst}

The earlier phenomenological power-law background ansatz has been
replaced by a minimal late-time $\phi$-first background apparatus.
The starting point is the effective scalar--tensor action
\begin{equation}
S_{\rm eff}
=
\int d^4x\,\sqrt{-g}\,
\left[
\frac12 f(\phi)R
-\frac12 K(\phi)(\partial\phi)^2
-V(\phi)
+\mathcal L_m
\right],
\label{eq:late_cosmo_action_main}
\end{equation}
with effective gravitational stiffness and Newton coupling
\[
M_{\rm eff}^2(\phi)=f(\phi),
\qquad
G_{\rm eff}(\phi)=\frac{1}{8\pi f(\phi)}.
\]

For a homogeneous FRW background, the late-time expansion history
is controlled by the coupled system for $H(z)$ and $\phi(z)$.
In the variable $N=\ln a$, the ECT Friedmann relation takes the form
\begin{equation}
E^2(N)
=
\frac{
\Omega_{m0}e^{-3N}
+\Omega_{r0}e^{-4N}
+\Omega_{V0}
+\frac{\mu^2}{6}u^2
}{
e^{\beta u}
-\frac{\kappa}{6}q^2
+\beta e^{\beta u}q
},
\label{eq:ect_late_friedmann_main}
\end{equation}
where $E(N)=H/H_0^{\rm ref}$, $u(N)=\phi(N)$, $q(N)=d\phi/dN$,
and the Level~B closure is $f(\phi)=f_0 e^{\beta\phi}$,
$K(\phi)=K_0$, $V(\phi)=V_0+\frac12 m_\phi^2\phi^2$.

At the present-epoch level, the late-time Hubble shift is controlled by
\begin{equation}
\frac{\Delta H_0}{H_0}
\approx
\frac{\mu^2u_0^2}{12}
-\frac12\beta u_0.
\label{eq:ect_h0_shift_main}
\end{equation}
For benchmark parameters $\beta=0.8$, $\mu=1.5$, $\kappa=15$, $u_0=-0.12$
this yields $\Delta H_0/H_0\approx 2.9\%$,
corresponding to $H_0^{\rm late}\approx 69.3$\,km\,s$^{-1}$\,Mpc$^{-1}$.
This numerical value is the output of the present semi-numerical
quasi-static benchmark solver and should not yet be read as the result
of a fully self-consistent ECT background integration.
The corresponding analytic benchmark window is shown in
Appendix~\ref{app:late_cosmo_algorithm},
Fig.~\ref{fig:app_h0_scan}.

The same background drift also changes the distance--redshift
relation and available lookback time:
\begin{equation}
D_L(z)=(1+z)\int_0^z \frac{dz'}{H(z')},
\qquad
t_{\rm lookback}(z)=\int_0^z \frac{dz'}{(1+z')H(z')}.
\label{eq:ect_dist_time_main}
\end{equation}
The benchmark run gives an ECT age of $13.1$\,Gyr vs.\ the
reference LCDM age of $13.8$\,Gyr, with luminosity-distance
shifts of $\Delta D_L/D_L\approx-5\%$ at $z=5$--12.

The net effect on the JWST early-structure tension is mixed.
Smaller luminosity distances ($\Delta D_L<0$) reduce the required
intrinsic luminosities and stellar masses, partially softening the
tension.  However, the same background also reduces the cosmic age
at any fixed redshift ($\Delta t_{\rm lookback}<0$), leaving less
time for early galaxy formation.  In the present benchmark these
two effects are comparable in magnitude ($\approx 5\%$ each),
so the overall JWST improvement is partial: distance inference
softens, growth is slightly enhanced (growth proxy $\approx 1.017$
at $z=10$), but the time budget worsens.  A stronger JWST
improvement would require either a non-trivial early-time $\phi$-background
history that localises the growth enhancement without compressing the
formation time-window, or a full perturbation-level growth-equation
analysis beyond the present heuristic $G_{\rm eff}/H^2$ proxy~(Level~Open):
\begin{equation}
D'' + \left(2+\frac{H'}{H}\right)D'
-\frac{3}{2}\Omega_m(z)\frac{G_{\rm eff}(z)}{G_N}D = 0.
\label{eq:growth_ode}
\end{equation}
Solving~\eqref{eq:growth_ode} with the ECT background is a natural
next step for a more definitive JWST assessment.

\begin{figure}[htb]
\centering
\includegraphics[width=0.82\linewidth]{figures/ect_h0_scan_bw.pdf}
\caption{Analytic parameter-window scan for the late-time Hubble shift
in the minimal ECT closure, based on
$\Delta H_0/H_0 \approx \mu^2 u_0^2/12 - \beta u_0/2$
at fixed $\mu=1.5$, $\kappa=15$.
Shaded contours show the fractional Hubble shift in the $(\beta,u_0)$-plane.
Benchmarks~B and~C are overlaid for reference.
A few-percent late-time shift arises in a finite and natural region of
parameter space, not at a single isolated tuned point.}
\label{fig:h0_scan_main}
\end{figure}

Figure~\ref{fig:h0_scan_main} shows that the benchmark Hubble shift
is representative of a finite parameter domain rather than a fine-tuned
point, supporting the Level~B status of the present closure.

The Hubble tension, the inferred age of the Universe, and part of the
JWST early-structure tension are therefore not independent in the ECT
framework: the same late/intermediate-time $\phi$-background that shifts
$H_0$ also modifies inferred distances, cosmic ages, and the friction
term relevant for structure growth~(Level~B; see
Appendices~\ref{app:late_cosmo_background} and
\ref{app:late_cosmo_algorithm}).

A further consequence of the running $f(\phi)$ is that the galactic
critical acceleration scale becomes epoch-dependent:
\begin{equation}
g^\dagger_{\rm bg}(z)=\frac{c_*\,H(z)}{2\pi},
\label{eq:gdag_bg_z}
\end{equation}
so that $g^\dagger_{\rm bg}$ is not a universal constant but traces the
background expansion history.  Panel~(d) of
Fig.~\ref{fig:ect_hubble_jwst_background} shows both the growth proxy
$G_{\rm eff}/H^2$ and the ratio $g^\dagger_{\rm bg}(z)/g^\dagger_{\rm bg}(0)=E(z)$,
confirming that in the critical-branch picture the effective acceleration
scale at early times was much larger than today.

\begin{figure*}[htb]
\centering
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth]{figures/ect_hubble_jwst_background_bw.pdf}
\caption{Late-time ECT background solution for the benchmark
$\phi$-first cosmological closure
($\beta=0.8$, $\mu=1.5$, $\kappa=15$, $u_0=-0.12$).
\textbf{Panel~(a):} dimensionless expansion history $E(z)=H(z)/H_0^{\rm ref}$
compared to the reference $\Lambda$CDM.
\textbf{Panel~(b):} relative shift in the luminosity distance.
\textbf{Panel~(c):} lookback-time shift; the inset gives the
ECT and reference ages of the Universe.
\textbf{Panel~(d):} the growth proxy $G_{\rm eff}/H^2$ (left axis,
solid) and the ratio $g^\dagger_{\rm bg}(z)/g^\dagger_{\rm bg}(0)=E(z)$
(right axis, dash-dotted), showing that the effective galactic critical
scale $g^\dagger_{\rm bg}\propto H(z)$ was much larger in the past.
The same background drift that shifts the late inferred $H_0$ also
alters the distance and time scales entering JWST inferences.}
\label{fig:ect_hubble_jwst_background}
\end{figure*}

\label{tab:ect_hubble_jwst_summary}

\end{tabular}
\end{table}

\textit{ISW excess.}
In voids, larger $G_{\rm eff}$ in low-density regions amplifies the
ISW effect~(Level~B).  The CMB quadrupole deficit has a structural
ECT argument from horizon-scale suppression (coherent-branch boundary
conditions), but a quantitative derivation of $\delta C_2/C_2$ remains
open~(Level~Open).

\subsubsection*{Black holes and compact objects}

Compact-object implications of the macroscopic branch remain exploratory.
ECT does not yet provide a controlled numerical prediction for
the maximum neutron-star mass: the required ECT-modified equation
of state and TOV integration have not been completed.
This remains an open strong-field problem~(Level~Open).

Possible black-hole implications of the ordered condensate branch are
important, but they are not yet part of the present controlled
macroscopic derivation and should be treated as a future subsection.
For GW-related LIV effects the estimate of Section~\ref{sec:mp_gw}
applies: the expected propagation-time shift
$\Delta t_{\rm GW}\lesssim 10^{-64}$\,s is negligible for all
currently observed sources.



\subsection{Dark Sector Phenomenology in ECT}
\label{sec:dark_sector}

\textit{Status: Level~B throughout. The primary macroscopic-branch
result is that galactic mass discrepancy can be addressed by the
$\phi$-first closure without particle dark matter. Collective and
topological dark-sector candidates are structurally motivated by
P4+P5 but require the Quantum Sector for full development.}

% -------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Dark-sector interpretation at the macroscopic level}
% -------------------------------------------------------

At the macroscopic level, ECT separates two conceptually distinct
questions often conflated under the name ``dark matter''.

\textit{First,} the galactic mass-discrepancy phenomenology can be
addressed within the present $\phi$-branch closure without introducing
a standard particle-dark-matter halo~(Level~B;
Section~\ref{sec:mp_galactic}).

\textit{Second,} ECT does not exclude additional dark-sector degrees
of freedom. Collective condensate excitations, Goldstone-like modes,
and topological sectors may contribute to the cosmic dark sector.
These possibilities probe the coherent-topological branch and require
the Quantum Sector for full treatment.

Thus the macroscopic branch addresses the \emph{phenomenology} of
missing gravitational response; the deeper ontology of possible
dark-sector excitations is developed in the Quantum Sector
(Section~\ref{sec:qs_dark_sector}).

% -------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Collective excitations as possible dark-sector candidates}
% -------------------------------------------------------

\textit{Status: Level~B structural possibility. Relic abundance,
stability, and production history not yet computed from bare~P3.}

The ordered branch naturally supports soft collective excitations,
including Goldstone-like modes with masses $m\sim H_0\sim 10^{-33}$\,eV.
At the macroscopic level these may be viewed as possible dark-sector
candidates if sufficiently weakly coupled and long-lived~(Level~B).
Their relic abundance and phase-space properties are not fixed by
the present macroscopic closure; a fuller treatment requires the
coherent-topological analysis in the Quantum Sector.

% -------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Topological sectors and the dark sector}
\label{sec:ds_topological}
% -------------------------------------------------------

\textit{Status: Level~B/C structural possibility; detailed
treatment deferred to the Quantum Sector.}

ECT also admits the possibility that part of the dark sector is tied
to coherent topological configurations~(P5): winding sectors,
vortex-like structures, or instanton-like tunnelling events.
Their definition and dynamics depend on winding numbers and defect
stability beyond the coherent approximation. They are noted here
as a conceptual bridge to the Quantum Sector~(Section~\ref{sec:qs_dark_sector});
their detailed treatment is deferred.

\subsection{Mass-discrepancy phenomenology in ECT}

Within the revised ECT framework the dark-matter phenomenology
is organised into two sharply distinct levels:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Galactic mass discrepancy} (flat rotation curves,
  RAR, BTFR): attributed entirely to the nonlinear
  $\phi$-branch of the Lorentz-order field
  (Section~\ref{sec:mp_galactic}).
  No particle dark matter and no kpc-scale variation of the
  heavy condensate amplitude are invoked.

\item \textbf{Possible non-galactic dark-sector contributions}:
  ultra-light Goldstone modes and topological condensate
  configurations may exist as additional excitations,
  but they are \emph{not required} to explain galactic
  rotation curves.  Whether they contribute to cluster or
  cosmological dark-sector phenomenology remains an open
  problem.
\end{enumerate}



\subsection{Dark energy and the dark sector in ECT}
\label{sec:dark_energy_phi}

\subsubsection{Dark energy as condensate vacuum energy}

In ECT the late-time accelerated expansion is not driven by
a cosmological constant added to the action.  Instead, it
arises from the residual vacuum energy of the condensate
after $O(4)\to O(3)$ symmetry breaking:
\begin{equation}
\rho_{\rm DE} = V(\Phi_0) + \tfrac{1}{2}(\partial_w\Phi)^2
= \rho_{\rm pot} + \rho_{\rm kin}\,.
\end{equation}
The equation of state is
\begin{equation}
w = \frac{p_{\rm DE}}{\rho_{\rm DE}}
= -1 + \frac{2\rho_{\rm kin}}{3\rho_{\rm cond}}\,.
\label{eq:w_ect}
\end{equation}
Since $\rho_{\rm kin} \geq 0$, ECT \emph{predicts}
$w(z) \geq -1$ at all redshifts (no phantom crossing).
This is a falsifiable structural prediction.

\paragraph{Thawing condensate model.}
If the condensate rolls slowly toward its potential
minimum, the kinetic fraction decays:
$\rho_{\rm kin}(z)/\rho_{\rm cond} = f_0\,e^{-\kappa z}$,
giving
\begin{equation}
w(z) = -1 + \frac{2f_0}{3}\,e^{-\kappa z}\,.
\label{eq:w_thaw}
\end{equation}
This is a \emph{thawing quintessence} model: $w \to -1$
in the past (condensate near potential minimum),
$w > -1$ today (condensate rolling).

\subsubsection{Observational status: DESI BAO measurements}

The Dark Energy Spectroscopic Instrument (DESI) has
published two data releases providing the most precise
BAO distance measurements to date:

\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{DESI DR1} (April~2024~\cite{DESI2024}):
  6~million galaxy and quasar redshifts.
  Combined with Planck~CMB and type~Ia supernovae
  (Pantheon+, Union3, or DESY5), a $w_0w_a$CDM fit
  gives $w_0 \approx -0.83$, $w_a \approx -0.75$,
  disfavouring $\Lambda$CDM at $2.5$--$3.9\sigma$
  depending on the supernova dataset.

\item \textbf{DESI DR2} (March~2025~\cite{DESIDR2_2025}):
  14~million redshifts (three years of operation),
  doubling DR1.  The preference for evolving dark energy
  \emph{strengthened}: $w_0w_a$CDM is preferred over
  $\Lambda$CDM at $2.8$--$4.2\sigma$.  The best-fit
  CPL parameters indicate $w_0 > -1$ today and
  $w_0 + w_a < -1$, formally implying a phantom crossing
  near $z \approx 0.5$.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Is the phantom crossing real?}
The apparent phantom crossing ($w < -1$ at $z > 0.5$) is
a feature of the \emph{CPL parametrisation}
$w(z) = w_0 + w_a z/(1+z)$, which is a simple two-parameter
approximation --- not a physical model.  Several independent
analyses have shown~\cite{Lodha2025,Calderon2024}:

\begin{enumerate}
\item The CPL form is too rigid to correctly describe both
  low-$z$ and high-$z$ behaviour simultaneously.

\item \emph{Thawing quintessence} models (where
  $w \geq -1$ at all times) are compatible with DESI data
  at the $2\sigma$ level~\cite{Shlivko2024,Gomez2025}.

\item Non-parametric reconstructions (Gaussian processes,
  crossing statistics) also find evolving dark energy but
  with larger uncertainty on whether $w$ actually crosses
  $-1$~\cite{Calderon2024}.

\item The phantom crossing significance does not yet reach
  $5\sigma$ and depends on the choice of supernova
  dataset~\cite{Wang2025}.
\end{enumerate}

\noindent
The current observational situation can therefore be
summarised as follows:
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{lc}
\hline\hline
Statement & Status \\
\hline
$w \neq -1$ (dark energy evolves) & $2.8$--$4.2\sigma$ \\
$w$ crosses $-1$ (phantom) &
  preferred in CPL, but \\
 & $2\sigma$-compatible with $w \geq -1$ \\
$\Lambda$CDM ($w = -1$ exact) & increasingly challenged, not yet excluded \\
\hline\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\paragraph{ECT confrontation with DESI.}
The ECT thawing model~\eqref{eq:w_thaw} with
$f_0 \approx 0.26$ and $\kappa \approx 4.3$ (calibrated,
not derived from first principles) is consistent with
DESI data at the $2\sigma$ level
(Fig.~\ref{fig:w_z}).  It reproduces the key observational
feature --- $w > -1$ today, evolving toward $w = -1$
in the past --- while predicting that the phantom crossing
is \emph{apparent}, not real.

If future data (DESI Year~5, Euclid, Vera Rubin/LSST)
confirm the phantom crossing at $>3\sigma$, ECT would be
falsified or require fundamental modification.  If
$w \geq -1$ is confirmed, $\Lambda$CDM would be further
challenged and ECT remains viable.


\subsubsection{Mass discrepancy: $\phi$-modification vs.\ particle dark matter}

The galactic mass-discrepancy phenomenology (flat rotation
curves, RAR, BTFR) is explained in ECT by the nonlinear
response of the Lorentz-order field $\phi$
(Section~\ref{sec:mp_galactic}).  This mechanism does
\emph{not} require new particles.

\paragraph{Predictions for direct detection experiments.}
Since the galactic mass discrepancy arises from the
$\phi$-branch rather than from weakly interacting massive
particles, ECT predicts that direct dark-matter-particle detection
experiments (XENON, LZ, PandaX, DARWIN) will find
\emph{no WIMP signal} for the galactic mass discrepancy.
A robust detection of a particle species accounting for
the galactic mass discrepancy would falsify the
$\phi$-branch interpretation.  By contrast, the mere
existence of additional dark condensate excitations on
non-galactic scales would not.



\paragraph{Cosmological fractions.}
ECT does not yet derive the cosmological fractions
$\Omega_b$, $\Omega_{\rm DM}$, and $\Omega_\Lambda$ from
first principles.  What it presently offers is a
reinterpretation: the galactic mass discrepancy is attributed
to the nonlinear $\phi$-branch rather than to particle dark
matter, while the late-time dark-energy sector is interpreted
as residual condensate vacuum energy.  A first-principles
derivation of the effective cosmological fractions remains
an open problem.

\paragraph{Distinction from the fifth force.}
The galactic $\phi$-modification and the ECT fifth force
($\mathcal{L}_5 = \beta\bar\Psi\gamma^A n_A\Psi$,
$\beta \sim m_f/M_{\rm Pl}$) are \emph{different}
manifestations of the same condensate:
the $\phi$-branch operates on kpc scales;
the fifth force is Planck-suppressed and detectable at
laboratory scales through spin precession
($\omega_5 \sim 10^{-10}$\,rad\,s$^{-1}$) and
E\"otv\"os-type experiments ($\eta \sim 10^{-15}$).
Neither is a consequence of the other.

\bigskip
\noindent
\textbf{Transition to Part~III.}
Part~II has established the macroscopic observable predictions of ECT:
galactic rotation curves from the Lorentz-order field $\phi$,
the baryonic Tully--Fisher relation as an exact algebraic consequence
of the critical infrared branch, cosmological inflation, dark energy,
and dark-matter candidates from the condensate spectrum.
All of these emerge from the variation of the condensate
amplitude $v_0(r)$ and the anisotropy parameter $\chi = \alpha-\beta$
on astrophysical and cosmological scales.

Part~III returns to the microscopic quantum structure.
Whereas Part~I derived key results of quantum mechanics from the condensate
(Schrödinger equation and CCR strictly; influence functional and second law
with Gaussian--Markov assumptions), Part~III examines
what the condensate \emph{additionally} predicts about the foundational
principles of physics: the uncertainty principle as a theorem,
the principle of extremal action from saddle-point condensate paths,
a structural route toward quantum statistics and the Pauli exclusion
principle via $SO(4)$ representation theory (sign structure compatible
with fermionic antisymmetry in the quadratic limit;
full PLZ theorem not yet derived),
and the structural organization of three quantum vacuum phenomena---Casimir
(at condensate boundaries), Unruh, and environmental decoherence---as
three observables controlled by related limits of the condensate
two-point function $N(\tau,\mathbf{r})$ (organizing proposition).

%==============================================================



% ============================================================

\paragraph{Bridge to the Quantum Sector.}
The macroscopic branch addresses gravitational phenomenology. Whenever
the discussion turns to coherent collective excitations, winding sectors,
or topological dark-sector configurations, the analysis enters the domain
of the coherent-topological branch~(P5). Those aspects are developed in
Section~\ref{sec:qs_dark_sector} of the Quantum Sector.
