% ============================================================
\subsection{Uncertainty principle in the coherent branch}
\label{sec:qs_uncertainty}
% backward-compatibility alias:
\label{sec:uncertainty}
% ============================================================

\textit{Status: Level~A for the mathematical uncertainty inequality
once the canonical commutator structure of the smooth coherent branch
is admitted; Level~B for the physical normalisation of that inequality
by the observed $\hbar$, which depends on
Eq.~\eqref{eq:qs_S0_identification}.}

\medskip
The uncertainty principle is not introduced in ECT as an independent
axiom.
If the coherent branch already admits (i)~a wave-dynamical
representation, (ii)~a canonical organisation, and (iii)~a commutator
candidate normalised by the intrinsic action scale $S_0$
(Section~\ref{sec:qs_ccr}), then the uncertainty relation follows as
a standard mathematical consequence.

\subsubsection*{Operator input}

From Section~\ref{sec:qs_ccr}, the natural commutator candidate of the
coherent branch is~\eqref{eq:qs_commutator_candidate}:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:qs_unc_comm}
  [\hat q,\hat p]
  = i\,S_0.
\end{equation}
After the final empirical identification~\eqref{eq:qs_S0_identification},
this becomes the observed canonical commutator:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:qs_unc_comm_hbar}
  [\hat q,\hat p]
  = i\,\hbar
\end{equation}
This is the observationally identified form~(Level~B):
it requires the final identification~\eqref{eq:qs_S0_identification}.

\subsubsection*{Robertson--Schr\"odinger inequality}

For any pair of self-adjoint operators $\hat A$, $\hat B$ and any
state $|\psi\rangle$, the Cauchy--Schwarz inequality gives
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:qs_robertson}
  \Delta A\,\Delta B
  \;\ge\;
  \tfrac{1}{2}\bigl|\langle[\hat A,\hat B]\rangle\bigr|.
\end{equation}
Setting $\hat A=\hat q$ and $\hat B=\hat p$ with~\eqref{eq:qs_unc_comm}
gives the coherent-branch uncertainty relation
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:qs_uncertainty_S0}
  \Delta q\,\Delta p
  \;\ge\;
  \frac{S_0}{2}
\end{equation}
Equation~\eqref{eq:qs_uncertainty_S0} is Level~A once the coherent
canonical structure~\eqref{eq:qs_unc_comm} is admitted.
After the $S_0=\hbar$ identification this reduces to the standard
Heisenberg form
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:qs_uncertainty_hbar}
  \Delta q\,\Delta p
  \;\ge\;
  \frac{\hbar}{2}
\end{equation}
This is a Level~B observational form~(Heisenberg inequality),
since it requires the final identification~\eqref{eq:qs_S0_identification}.

\subsubsection*{Interpretation}

ECT does not postulate uncertainty at the foundation.
Uncertainty appears only after the coherent branch has already
developed the structures that ordinary quantum theory usually assumes:
wave amplitudes, canonical variables, and commutator normalisation.
The uncertainty relation is therefore not primitive; it is derivative.

\paragraph{Status summary.}
\textit{Level~A:} given the canonical structure~\eqref{eq:qs_unc_comm},
the inequality~\eqref{eq:qs_uncertainty_S0} is pure mathematics.
\textit{Level~B:} the physical Heisenberg form
$\Delta q\,\Delta p\ge\hbar/2$ depends on the completion of
$S_0=\hbar$~\eqref{eq:qs_S0_identification}.

\paragraph{Summary.}
In ECT the uncertainty principle is not an axiom of nature imposed from
the outset.
It is the mathematical consequence of the canonical organisation of the
smooth coherent branch.

% ============================================================
\subsection{Principle of extremal action and saddle dominance}
\label{sec:qs_extremal_action}
% ============================================================

\textit{Status: Level~A for the saddle-point principle inside the
coherent amplitude language; Level~B for the physical interpretation
of finite-$S_0$ corrections as the source of quantum fluctuations in
specific reduced systems.}

\medskip
The principle of extremal action is not an independent postulate in
ECT.
It follows directly from the coherent amplitude structure already
established in Sections~\ref{sec:qs_phase_dynamics}
and~\ref{sec:qs_wave}.

\subsubsection*{Coherent amplitude weighting}

The coherent branch is weighted by amplitudes of the
form~\eqref{eq:qs_weight_S0}:
\[
  \mathcal{A}[q] \sim \exp\!\bigl(i\,S[q]/S_0\bigr).
\]
In the Euclidean preparatory language the corresponding weight is
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:qs_extremal_weight_E}
  \mathcal{W}[q]
  \sim
  \exp\!\left(-\frac{S_E[q]}{S_0}\right).
\end{equation}
When the relevant action satisfies $S[q]\gg S_0$ (or $S_E[q]\gg S_0$),
the path weight is dominated by saddle configurations.

\subsubsection*{Saddle-point conditions}

In the Lorentzian branch the dominant contributions satisfy
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:qs_saddle}
  \delta S[q] = 0;
\end{equation}
in the Euclidean preparatory branch:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:qs_saddle_E}
  \delta S_E[q] = 0.
\end{equation}
This is the emergent principle of extremal action~(Level~A).

\subsubsection*{Why this matters}

Classicality does not require a second independent principle.
Classical extremal trajectories and finite-$S_0$ coherent fluctuations
are two limits of a single ordered-branch framework: the large-action
saddle regime and the near-$S_0$ quantum regime respectively.

\subsubsection*{Finite-$S_0$ corrections}

When $S[q]$ is not large compared with $S_0$, saddle-point dominance
fails and neighbouring histories contribute appreciably.
Finite-$S_0$ corrections are therefore the origin of the coherent
non-classical regime in ECT.

\paragraph{Status.}
The saddle principle is Level~A.
Its detailed implementation in specific reduced coherent systems is
Level~B, depending on the wave-dynamical and $S_0=\hbar$ programme.

\paragraph{Summary.}
In ECT the principle of extremal action is not an additional law.
It is the saddle-dominance limit of the coherent amplitude weighting
already present in the Quantum Sector.

% ============================================================
\subsection{Conservation laws in the coherent sector}
\label{sec:qs_conservation}
% ============================================================

\textit{Status: Level~A for the existence of Noether currents inherited
from the variational structure of the ordered condensate; Level~B for
their full interpretation in reduced coherent-sector language.
Connection to ECT basics and Macroscopic Physics:
Section~\ref{sec:noether}, Appendix~\ref{app:noether_full}, and
Section~\ref{sec:mp_noether}.}

\medskip
The Quantum Sector does not introduce conservation laws from outside.
They are inherited from the same variational condensate structure that
already produced conserved quantities in ECT basics and Macroscopic
Physics.
What changes in QS is not the existence of the currents, but their
interpretation inside the coherent-topological branch.

This subsection is also the QS-side development of the shared
deferred Noether material~(Section~\ref{sec:noether}):
the same variational foundation that generated source currents in
Macroscopic Physics must, in the coherent-topological branch,
organise phase-sector charges, winding-sector bookkeeping, and
ultimately topological current algebra.

\subsubsection*{Translational Noether current}

From translational invariance of the underlying action, the condensate
admits the conserved Noether tensor
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:qs_noether_T}
  \partial_A T^{AB} = 0
\end{equation}
(Level~A; follows from P1--P3 and the Noether procedure,
Appendix~\ref{app:noether_full}).
This holds regardless of which effective branch is studied.

\subsubsection*{Rotational and topological sector}

Likewise, the ordered condensate carries conserved rotational currents,
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:qs_noether_J}
  \partial_C J^{C,AB} = 0,
\end{equation}
already developed in Appendix~\ref{app:noether_full}.
In the coherent-topological sector these currents acquire an additional
interpretive rôle: they organise how loop sectors, winding sectors, and
defect sectors are embedded into the same ordered medium.

\subsubsection*{Why conservation laws look different in QS}

In the geometric branch the natural observables are stress-energy,
source tensors, and large-scale response.
In the Quantum Sector the natural observables are amplitudes, reduced
phase variables, winding sectors, and coherent histories.
The same underlying conserved structures are therefore seen through a
different coarse-graining.

\subsubsection*{Open point: topological currents}

A fully explicit development of topological Noether currents in the
coherent branch has not yet been completed.
The deferred Noether material~(Section~\ref{sec:noether}) flagged this
as a shared MP/QS target.
The coherent branch clearly suggests a conserved topological
organisation, but its final current algebra remains open.

\paragraph{Summary.}
Conservation laws are not missing from the Quantum Sector; they are
inherited from the same variational foundation as ECT basics and MP.
Their specifically coherent-topological interpretation is still only
partially developed.

% ============================================================
\subsection{Quantum statistics: exchange sectors and spinorial compatibility}
\label{sec:qs_statistics}
% ============================================================

\textit{Status: Level~B throughout.
This subsection provides a structural route to bosonic/fermionic
classification inside the coherent-topological branch.
It does not yet constitute a first-principles derivation of the full
spin-statistics theorem or of second-quantised anticommutation
relations from bare~P3.}

\medskip
If the Quantum Sector of ECT is to reproduce more than one-particle
coherent kinematics, it must also explain why exchange sectors split
into bosonic and fermionic classes.
At the present stage the strongest justified result is structural: ECT
naturally reproduces the topological dichotomy of exchange sectors and
shows its compatibility with the representation content of the ordered
branch.

\subsubsection*{Exchange topology}

For two identical excitations in three spatial dimensions, the reduced
configuration space is
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:qs_exchange_space}
  \mathcal{M}_2
  =
  \bigl(\mathbb{R}^3\times\mathbb{R}^3\setminus\Delta\bigr)/S_2,
\end{equation}
whose fundamental group is
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:qs_exchange_pi1}
  \pi_1(\mathcal{M}_2) = \mathbb{Z}_2.
\end{equation}
This yields exactly two topological exchange classes: symmetric and
antisymmetric~(Level~A as a topological fact; the connection to
specific condensate sectors is Level~B).

\subsubsection*{Representation-theoretic compatibility}

After $O(4)\to O(3)$ breaking, excitations of the ordered sector fall
into representations of the residual rotational structure.
Integer-spin tensorial sectors are compatible with symmetric exchange;
half-integer spinorial sectors are compatible with antisymmetric
exchange.
This is not yet the full Pauli--L\"uders--Zumino theorem, but it is
the correct structural compatibility statement: exchange topology and
representation sign fit together naturally in the ordered branch.

\subsubsection*{What is and is not claimed}

ECT at the present stage does \emph{not} yet derive:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
  \item the full relativistic spin-statistics theorem;
  \item the full operator anticommutation algebra
    $\{\hat a_i,\hat a_j^\dagger\}=\delta_{ij}$;
  \item the complete many-body fermionic Fock-space construction
    from bare condensate dynamics~(Open; OP-Q11).
\end{enumerate}
What it does provide is a structurally natural route from
coherent-topological exchange sectors to the bosonic/fermionic
dichotomy.

\paragraph{Summary.}
Quantum statistics in ECT is presently a Level~B structural result:
exchange topology and ordered-branch representation theory already
point toward the standard bosonic/fermionic classification, but the
full spin-statistics theorem remains open~(OP-Q11).

% ============================================================
\subsection{Representation-theoretic route to Dirac structure}
\label{sec:qs_dirac}
% ============================================================

\textit{Status: Level~A for the emergence of the Lorentz algebra
$\mathfrak{so}(1,3)$ from $O(4)\to O(3)$ SSB combined with Wick
rotation, and for the representation-theoretic route to Clifford
structure.
This gives a conditional structural theorem: if the coherent sector
contains physical spinorial excitations, then their unique local
Lorentz-covariant first-order dynamics is Dirac-type.
Level~B for the physical realisation of a Dirac field in ECT.
Open: mass generation and gauge couplings from condensate microdynamics.}

\medskip
The exchange-sector analysis of Section~\ref{sec:qs_statistics}
established that the ECT broken phase naturally admits both bosonic
and fermionic sectors.
The present subsection shows that the symmetry structure of the broken
condensate provides a natural representation-theoretic route to
the Dirac structure.

\subsubsection*{From $O(4)\to O(3)$ to the Lorentz algebra~(Level~A)}

The Lie algebra $\mathfrak{so}(4)$ has 6 generators $J_{AB}$.
Under $O(4)\to O(3)$ with the condensate direction $n^A=\delta^A_4$:
\begin{itemize}
  \item \textbf{Unbroken} ($O(3)$ subgroup): $J_{ij}$,
    $i,j\in\{1,2,3\}$ --- spatial rotation generators.
  \item \textbf{Broken} (coset $O(4)/O(3)$): $J_{i4}$,
    $i\in\{1,2,3\}$.
\end{itemize}
After the Wick rotation $w\to-ic_*t$~\eqref{eq:qs_wick},
the broken generators become boost generators:
$K_i\equiv-i\,J_{i4}$.
A direct calculation then confirms that $J_{ij}$ and $K_i$ satisfy
the Lorentz algebra $\mathfrak{so}(1,3)$,
with $[K_i,K_j]=-i\,J_{ij}$.
Thus the Lorentz algebra emerges from the broken-phase structure
and the Wick rotation.~(Level~A: follows from P4+P5+\eqref{eq:qs_wick}.)

\subsubsection*{Representation-theoretic route to Clifford structure~(Level~A)}

The spinor representation of $\mathfrak{so}(1,3)$ is
$(\tfrac{1}{2},0)\oplus(0,\tfrac{1}{2})$~(Dirac spinor).
Within that representation, the Lorentz generators take the form
$J^{\mu\nu}=\frac{i}{4}[\gamma^\mu,\gamma^\nu]$, which forces
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:qs_clifford}
  \bigl\{\gamma^\mu,\gamma^\nu\bigr\}
  = 2\,g^{\mu\nu}\,\mathbf{1}_4,
\end{equation}
where $g^{\mu\nu}$ is the emergent Lorentzian metric from the broken
condensate phase.
The Clifford algebra~\eqref{eq:qs_clifford} is therefore a
representation-theoretic consequence of the broken-phase Lorentz
structure, not an independent postulate.~(Level~A.)

\subsubsection*{Conditional structural theorem: unique first-order covariant dynamics}

For a spinorial field in the $(\tfrac{1}{2},0)\oplus(0,\tfrac{1}{2})$
representation, the most general local Lorentz-covariant first-order
differential equation takes the form
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:qs_dirac_conditional}
  \bigl(i\,S_0\,\gamma^\mu\partial_\mu - m_\psi\,c_*\bigr)\psi = 0,
\end{equation}
because $i\gamma^\mu\partial_\mu$ is the unique first-order operator
consistent with~\eqref{eq:qs_clifford}.
This is a conditional statement:
\begin{quote}
\textbf{Conditional structural theorem.}
\textit{If the coherent-topological sector of ECT contains physical
spinorial excitations realising the
$(\frac{1}{2},0)\oplus(0,\frac{1}{2})$ representation of the
emergent Lorentz group, then their local Lorentz-covariant
first-order dynamics is uniquely Dirac-type~\eqref{eq:qs_dirac_conditional}.}
\end{quote}

\paragraph{What this theorem does and does not establish.}
\textit{It does establish:} the representation-theoretic uniqueness
of the Dirac operator, given the Lorentz algebra and the spinor
representation.
\textit{It does not establish:} that spinorial excitations actually
exist in the ECT spectrum; their mass generation or gauge couplings;
the complete quantisation of the Dirac field from bare~P3.

\paragraph{Pauli exclusion.}
Exchange topology gives bosonic and fermionic sectors at Level~A
(Section~\ref{sec:qs_statistics}).
The Dirac structure, once admitted, makes the standard spin-statistics
argument available: a spin-$\tfrac{1}{2}$ field quantised with
commutators yields an energy spectrum unbounded below, so
anticommutators are required.
Pauli exclusion is therefore a Level~B structural consequence
conditional on the realisation of the spinorial sector and on
$S_0=\hbar$~(OP-Q2, OP-Q11).

\paragraph{Status summary.}
\begin{itemize}
  \item Level~A: Lorentz algebra from broken phase + Wick rotation;
    Clifford algebra as spinor-representation consequence.
  \item Level~B~(conditional): Dirac-type first-order dynamics,
    given spinorial excitations.
  \item Level~B: Pauli exclusion, conditional on spinorial sector
    and $S_0=\hbar$.
  \item Open~(OP-Q3, OP-Q11): physical spinorial spectrum,
    mass generation, gauge couplings, full second-quantisation.
\end{itemize}

% ============================================================
\subsection{Quantum vacuum structure of the ordered condensate}
\label{sec:qs_vacuum_intro}
% backward-compatibility alias:
\label{sec:quantum_vacuum}
% backward-compatibility alias:
\label{sec:unified_correlator}
% ============================================================

\textit{Status: Level~A for the statement that the ordered condensate
defines a nontrivial coherent vacuum sector.
Level~B for quantitative identifications of vacuum stiffness scales
with observed Planck-scale quantities and for specific vacuum-response
phenomena discussed in the following subsections.}

\medskip
The Quantum Sector of ECT does not describe particles placed on top of
an otherwise empty vacuum.
Its more basic claim is that the vacuum itself is a structured ordered
medium.
The coherent-topological branch is therefore simultaneously a theory of
phase-sensitive excitations and a theory of the physical vacuum.

\subsubsection*{Vacuum as an ordered medium}

Once the condensate enters the ordered phase, the background is no
longer featureless.
It possesses:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
  \item a nontrivial order parameter~$\Phi_{\rm eff}=\rho e^{i\theta}$;
  \item a phase-sensitive coherent sector with winding structure;
  \item stiffness scales controlling deformations of the ordered state;
  \item topological sectors and loop actions weighted by $S_0$;
  \item nontrivial vacuum correlators of coherent observables.
\end{enumerate}
Thus the ECT vacuum is already a dynamical object before one introduces
particles or measurement.

\subsubsection*{Unified vacuum viewpoint}

This is one of the central unifying features of ECT.
What standard physics often treats as separate domains---quantum vacuum
structure, wave dynamics, action quantisation, and part of
gravitational stiffness---are, in ECT, different manifestations of one
and the same ordered condensate background.
The geometric branch probes its phase-insensitive response;
the Quantum Sector probes its phase-sensitive and topological response.

\subsubsection*{Vacuum stiffness and Planck-scale interpretation}

The ordered condensate resists deformation.
In the geometric branch this appears as gravitational stiffness
(Section~\ref{sec:mp_matching}).
In the coherent branch it appears as phase stiffness~$K_\theta^{\rm eff}$,
loop action cost $S_0$, and the nontrivial energetic structure of the
ordered vacuum.
A full first-principles derivation relating all these stiffness notions
to one common microscopic set of condensate parameters remains open,
but the structural unity is already clear from the two-branch
architecture.

\paragraph{Status.}
That the vacuum is a structured ordered medium is Level~A.
That its stiffness parameters can be identified quantitatively with
all observed Planck-scale quantities is Level~B/open, depending on
the completion of the matching programme in both MP and QS.

\paragraph{Summary.}
The vacuum in ECT is the ordered condensate itself, seen through the
coherent branch.
This provides the natural setting for Casimir-like effects,
particle-production phenomena, and Unruh-type vacuum response.

% ============================================================
\subsection{Boundary sensitivity of the ordered vacuum and the Casimir effect}
\label{sec:qs_casimir}
% backward-compatibility alias:
\label{sec:casimir}
% ============================================================

\textit{Status: Level~B.
ECT naturally predicts that the ordered coherent vacuum should be
sensitive to boundary conditions.
A full quantitative Casimir calculation from the completed coherent
EFT remains to be carried out.}

\medskip
A nontrivial ordered vacuum should respond to boundaries.
This is the essential conceptual content of the Casimir effect in ECT:
placing boundaries modifies the allowed coherent fluctuation spectrum
of the ordered condensate and therefore changes the vacuum energy.

\subsubsection*{Why a Casimir-type effect is expected}

If the ordered vacuum supports coherent fluctuation modes, then
imposing boundary conditions changes the allowed mode spectrum.
Schematically,
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:qs_casimir_modes}
  E_{\rm vac}^{\rm(boundary)}
  \neq
  E_{\rm vac}^{\rm(free)}.
\end{equation}
The resulting energy difference induces an observable force between
boundaries.
This is not an extra hypothesis; it is the generic consequence of
having a nontrivial ordered vacuum with mode structure.

\subsubsection*{ECT interpretation}

In ordinary QFT the Casimir force is often phrased as a consequence of
zero-point mode subtraction.
In ECT the interpretation is more direct: the effect reflects the
response of the ordered coherent vacuum to a change in admissible
boundary-compatible fluctuation sectors.
The language of ``zero-point'' energy is replaced by the language of
boundary-constrained coherent vacuum stiffness.

\subsubsection*{Status and future derivation}

ECT supports the \emph{structural existence} of a Casimir-type
phenomenon.
What is not yet completed is the explicit calculation of the force
coefficient for realistic geometries from the final reduced coherent
action~(OP-Q12).

\paragraph{Summary.}
The Casimir effect fits naturally into ECT as a boundary-sensitivity
phenomenon of the ordered vacuum.
Its quantitative derivation remains part of the future
coherent-vacuum programme.

% ============================================================
\subsection{Cosmological particle production and time-dependent ordered backgrounds}
\label{sec:qs_particle_production}
% ============================================================

\textit{Status: Level~B.
ECT is structurally compatible with cosmological particle production
in time-dependent ordered backgrounds.
A completed first-principles derivation of all production rates from
the coherent EFT is not yet available.}

\medskip
If the ordered condensate background changes in time, the notion of
``particle'' defined relative to one coherent vacuum slicing need not
coincide with that defined relative to another.
This is the natural setting for cosmological particle production in ECT,
complementary to the macroscopic phase-transition discussion
of Section~\ref{sec:mp_cosmo}.

\subsubsection*{Time-dependent ordered branch}

In a nonstationary background, the effective coherent vacuum is itself
time-dependent.
Mode decomposition at early and late times therefore differs.
Schematically, the early-time and late-time mode operators are related
by a Bogoliubov transformation,
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:qs_bogoliubov}
  a_k^{\rm(out)}
  =
  \alpha_k\,a_k^{\rm(in)}
  +
  \beta_k\,a_{-k}^{\rm(in)\dagger},
\end{equation}
with $|\beta_k|^2$ measuring the produced excitation density.
This structural form is Level~B: the actual $\alpha_k$, $\beta_k$
coefficients require the completed time-dependent coherent-vacuum
calculation.

\subsubsection*{ECT interpretation}

Particle production here is not ``creation from nothing''.
It is a reorganisation of excitation content relative to a changing
ordered background.
In that sense, cosmological particle production is another
manifestation of the dynamical vacuum nature of the ECT condensate.

\subsubsection*{Relation to MP cosmology}

Macroscopic Physics describes the large-scale evolution of the ordered
branch (Section~\ref{sec:mp_cosmo}).
The present QS subsection gives the coherent-vacuum interpretation of
how such time dependence can populate excitation sectors.
The two descriptions are complementary: MP governs the background
evolution; QS governs the excitation production against that background.

\paragraph{Summary.}
ECT naturally accommodates cosmological particle production whenever
the ordered vacuum changes in time.
Quantitative production rates remain Level~B/open~(OP-Q12).

% ============================================================
\subsection{Accelerated observers and the Unruh-type response}
\label{sec:qs_unruh}
% backward-compatibility alias:
\label{sec:unruh}
% ============================================================

\textit{Status: Level~B.
ECT is structurally compatible with an Unruh-type response of the
ordered coherent vacuum to accelerated observers.
A completed detector-response derivation from the reduced coherent
action is still open.}

\medskip
If the ordered vacuum is genuinely physical, then observer-dependent
mode decomposition should matter.
An accelerated observer need not decompose the coherent vacuum into the
same excitations as an inertial observer.
This is the structural origin of an Unruh-type effect in ECT.

\subsubsection*{Kinematic expectation}

For uniform acceleration $a$, the standard QFT result gives
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:qs_unruh_temp}
  T_U
  =
  \frac{\hbar\,a}{2\pi\,c\,k_B}.
\end{equation}
This formula uses the observed $\hbar$; within ECT, $\hbar$ is to be
understood as $S_0$ after the identification
$S_0=\hbar$~\eqref{eq:qs_S0_identification}~(Level~B).
The structural statement is that an accelerated detector coupled to the
coherent branch should register a thermal-like response of the ordered
vacuum.

\subsubsection*{ECT status}

The ordered-vacuum framework makes an Unruh-type effect natural and
expected.
What is not yet in place is the explicit detector-response calculation
from the completed ECT coherent EFT~(OP-Q12).

\paragraph{Summary.}
The Unruh effect is naturally compatible with ECT because the vacuum is
an ordered coherent medium, not an empty background.
Its fully explicit derivation remains Level~B/open.

% ============================================================
\subsection{Unified response logic and analogue-gravity continuity}
\label{sec:qs_vacuum_unified}
% ============================================================

\textit{Status: Level~B throughout.}

\medskip

\subsubsection*{Unified response logic of the ordered vacuum}

The ordered-vacuum effects discussed in the preceding subsections
should not be read as a collection of unrelated phenomena.
From the ECT viewpoint, Casimir response, particle production in
time-dependent backgrounds, Unruh-type detector response, and
Hawking-like horizon thermality are different manifestations of one
underlying structure: the coherent vacuum of the ordered condensate
responds nontrivially to boundaries, acceleration, time dependence,
and strong-field causal interfaces.

The logic can be organised as follows:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
  \item \textbf{Boundary sensitivity:}
    boundaries reshape the coherent vacuum mode spectrum, producing
    Casimir-type effects~(Section~\ref{sec:qs_casimir}).
  \item \textbf{Time-dependent background sensitivity:}
    nonadiabatic variation of the ordered background leads to
    Bogoliubov-type mode mixing and particle-production
    effects~(Section~\ref{sec:qs_particle_production}).
  \item \textbf{Observer sensitivity:}
    accelerated detectors probe the coherent vacuum differently
    from inertial ones, giving rise to Unruh-type
    response~(Section~\ref{sec:qs_unruh}).
  \item \textbf{Horizon/interface sensitivity:}
    strong-field causal interfaces generate reduced-state
    thermality in black-hole
    settings~(Section~\ref{sec:qs_black_holes}).
\end{enumerate}
In all four cases the vacuum is not trivially empty: it is an
ordered coherent medium whose fluctuation structure depends on
how it is probed.

\paragraph{Why this matters.}
This unified viewpoint prevents the Quantum Sector from fragmenting
into separate phenomenological anecdotes.
Vacuum response is one of the principal outputs of the
coherent-topological branch, with a single underlying mechanism
expressed in four different physical settings.

\paragraph{Status.}
The unified reading of Casimir response, particle production,
Unruh-type detector response, and horizon thermality as manifestations
of one ordered coherent vacuum is Level~B.
It is a coherent interpretive closure supported by the structure of
the Quantum Sector, but the detailed first-principles derivation of
each effect is not yet complete at the same level.

\subsubsection*{Analogue-gravity continuity of the QS vacuum picture}

ECT does not introduce this vacuum-response logic in isolation.
There is a strong continuity with the analogue-gravity lesson:
effective horizons, mode conversion, and thermal detector response
can arise in emergent media without requiring spacetime geometry
itself to be fundamental.

This does not mean ECT is merely an analogue model.
The point is more precise: ECT uses the analogue-gravity lesson as
evidence that horizon thermality and vacuum response need not be
interpreted as proofs of a fundamental microscopic spacetime
ontology.
They can instead emerge from the response structure of an ordered
medium---exactly as the coherent-topological branch provides.

\paragraph{Interpretive consequence.}
This continuity strengthens the ECT reading of Hawking and Unruh
phenomena: it becomes more plausible that black-hole thermality,
accelerated detector response, and boundary-sensitive vacuum effects
all belong to the same emergent-vacuum family rather than to
unrelated mechanisms.

\paragraph{Status.}
The analogue-gravity continuity argument is Level~B: a conceptual
strengthening of the ECT interpretation, not a standalone derivation.

\begin{figure}[h]
\centering
\begin{tikzpicture}[
  node distance=1.0cm and 1.0cm,
  box/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center, minimum width=3.0cm,
    minimum height=0.95cm, font=\small},
  arrow/.style={->, thick}
]
\node[box] (vac) {ordered coherent\\vacuum};
\node[box, below left=of vac] (casimir) {boundary response\\(Casimir)};
\node[box, below=of vac] (prod) {time-dependent response\\(particle production)};
\node[box, below right=of vac] (unruh) {observer response\\(Unruh)};
\node[box, below=2.2cm of prod] (bh) {strong-field interface\\response (Hawking/horizon)};
\node[box, right=2.0cm of bh] (ag) {analogue-gravity\\continuity};
\draw[arrow] (vac) -- (casimir);
\draw[arrow] (vac) -- (prod);
\draw[arrow] (vac) -- (unruh);
\draw[arrow] (casimir) -- (bh);
\draw[arrow] (prod) -- (bh);
\draw[arrow] (unruh) -- (bh);
\draw[arrow] (bh) -- (ag);
\draw[arrow] (vac) to[bend left=40] (ag);
\end{tikzpicture}
\caption{Unified response logic of the ordered coherent vacuum
in the Quantum Sector of ECT~(Level~B).
Boundary conditions, time-dependent backgrounds, accelerated observers,
and strong-field causal interfaces probe one and the same ordered vacuum
in different ways.
The analogue-gravity continuity shows that none of these effects requires
a fundamental spacetime ontology; they emerge from the coherent-vacuum
response structure.
This is a structural interpretation map, not a quantitative derivation.}
\label{fig:qs_vacuum_unified}
\end{figure}

For a detailed discussion of the unified vacuum-response logic,
see Appendix~\ref{app:qs_vacuum_response}.

\paragraph{Summary.}
The four vacuum-response effects discussed above are best understood
not as separate phenomena, but as different probes of the same ordered
coherent vacuum~(Section~\ref{sec:qs_vacuum_unified}).
The vacuum in ECT is not an auxiliary stage on which dynamics is later
placed.
It is part of the ordered condensate itself.
This gives a unified conceptual home to Casimir-like effects,
particle-production phenomena, and accelerated-vacuum response, while
keeping all quantitative overclaims under control.

% ============================================================
\subsection{Influence functional, decoherence, and the arrow of time}
\label{sec:qs_decoherence}\label{sec:influence_functional}\label{sec:second_law}
% ============================================================

\textit{Status: Level~A for the causal retarded kernel in the
quadratic broken-phase sector; Level~A for nonnegative spectral
density in the quadratic sector; Level~B for the low-entropy initial
coherent sector, the effective ohmic regime, the Markov approximation,
and the explicit entropy-production formula.
Connection to ECT basics: Section~\ref{sec:arrow_of_time},
Appendix~\ref{app:ohmic_markov}, and Appendix~\ref{app:retarded_kernel}.}

\medskip
The previous subsections established the coherent branch as a
phase-sensitive sector with a distinguished action scale, a
Schr\"odinger-type reduction, and a natural canonical organisation.
However, none of this yet explains why macroscopic coherent
superpositions are not generically observed, why effective
irreversibility appears, or why a preferred thermodynamic arrow of
time emerges.
These questions belong to decoherence.
In ECT they must be addressed inside the coherent branch itself,
rather than imported from an external quantum framework.

\subsubsection*{Why decoherence belongs to the coherent branch}

Decoherence in ECT is not a correction to the geometric branch.
It is a process internal to the coherent-topological sector:
a smooth coherent subsystem interacts with the rest of the ordered
condensate, whose unresolved modes act as an effective environment.
The ``system'' is the low-dimensional coherent sector tracked
explicitly; the ``environment'' is the large set of unresolved
condensate modes that are integrated out.
The system--environment split is not fundamental, but branch-dependent
and scale-dependent.

\subsubsection*{Influence-functional form of the effective description}

After integrating out the unresolved bath modes, the reduced coherent
sector is described by a reduced effective weight.
Following the notation of ECT basics (Section~\ref{sec:arrow_of_time}),
where $q$ and $q'$ label forward and backward coherent histories, the
influence functional takes the schematic form
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:qs_influence}
  \mathcal{F}[q,q']
  =
  \exp\!\left\{
    \frac{i}{S_0}\,\Gamma[q,q']
    - \frac{1}{S_0}\,\Gamma_{\rm irr}[q,q']
  \right\},
\end{equation}
where $\Gamma[q,q']$ is the coherent-sector decoherence functional
(already prepared in ECT basics; Section~\ref{sec:arrow_of_time})
and $\Gamma_{\rm irr}[q,q']\ge 0$ is the irreversible suppression
part. Consistency requires
\[
  \Gamma_{\rm irr}[q,q] = 0,
\]
so that no decoherence penalty is assigned on the diagonal.
By contrast, the phase-sensitive part $\Gamma[q,q']$ need not
vanish on the diagonal and may remain nontrivial away from the
diagonal as well.
The normalisation by $S_0$---rather than a postulated $\hbar$---is
required by internal consistency:
$S_0$ is the only available action scale at this stage.

\paragraph{Status.}
The existence of a reduced influence-functional description is Level~B:
it is the natural EFT organisation of the coherent branch once a
subset of condensate modes is integrated out.
What is structural is the system--environment logic itself;
what remains open is the exact microscopic derivation of
the full nonlinear decoherence functional $\Gamma[q,q']$
for the complete coherent sector.

\subsubsection*{Causal retarded kernel: the Level~A result}

A crucial ingredient of the arrow-of-time argument is already
established at Level~A in the quadratic broken-phase sector.
The retarded Green kernel satisfies
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:qs_retarded_zero}
  K(\tau<0) = 0.
\end{equation}
This follows from the hyperbolic Lorentzian operator of the broken
phase: both poles lie in the lower half-plane, so closing the contour
above for $\tau<0$ gives zero~(Appendix~\ref{app:retarded_kernel}).
The coherent branch therefore inherits a genuinely causal retarded
kernel from the same broken-phase structure that underlies macroscopic
causality in the geometric branch.

\paragraph{Physical meaning.}
This is one of the structurally strongest points of the Quantum Sector.
The arrow-of-time analysis does not begin with an arbitrary
irreversibility rule.
It begins with a kernel that is already causally retarded in the
underlying broken-phase EFT.
Irreversibility is therefore built on top of a causal ordered
background, not inserted by hand.

\subsubsection*{Low-entropy coherent initial sector}

The second ingredient is the assumption that the initial coherent
sector is highly ordered and therefore of low effective entropy.
This should not be overstated.
The claim is not that $S_{\rm ent}(w_0)=0$ has been proved in the
full quantum-mechanical sense.
Rather: P4 selects an ordered vacuum branch and P5 restricts attention
to the smooth coherent topological sector.
Together with the non-tachyonic quadratic spectrum, this strongly
motivates a highly ordered low-entropy initial coherent sector.

\paragraph{Structure of the initial sector.}
The key point is not that vanishing initial entropy has already been
derived as a theorem from bare~P3.
Rather, the ordered condensate together with the coherent-topological
restriction strongly motivates an initially low-entropy sector:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
  \item the ordered branch selects a non-generic vacuum structure;
  \item the coherent sector restricts attention to phase-correlated
    configurations rather than arbitrary mixtures;
  \item the quadratic fluctuation spectrum is non-tachyonic, so this
    sector is dynamically viable.
\end{enumerate}
The natural QS starting point is therefore not a maximally disordered
state but a highly ordered coherent one---exactly the initial condition
needed for an emergent arrow of time.

\paragraph{Status.}
The existence of an ordered coherent sector is structural~(Level~A).
Its interpretation as a low-entropy initial condition is Level~B:
strongly motivated by P4--P5 and the ordered vacuum, but not yet a
first-principles microscopic entropy theorem.

\subsubsection*{Positive spectral density and dissipative kernel}

The third ingredient is positivity of the spectral density in the
quadratic sector.
As prepared in ECT basics and detailed in Appendix~\ref{app:ohmic_markov},
the relevant linear effective sector admits a nonnegative spectral
density:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:qs_rho_positive}
  \rho(\mu^2) \ge 0.
\end{equation}
This is Level~A in the quadratic sector.
It implies a nonnegative dissipative part of the retarded response
kernel in the linearised effective description and is the input that
makes monotonic entropy growth plausible once the coherent subsystem
is coupled to an unresolved environment.

\subsubsection*{Effective ohmic regime and Markov approximation}

At this point one reaches the main Level~B closure assumptions of the
decoherence program.
The scale analysis of Appendix~\ref{app:ohmic_markov} shows that the
standard 3D Goldstone-like derivative coupling gives a super-ohmic
spectral density,
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:qs_super_ohmic}
  J(\omega) \propto N_{\rm eff}\,\omega^2\,|g(\omega/c_*)|^2
  \;\sim\; N_{\rm eff}\,\omega^4
  \qquad (\text{standard 3D bath}),
\end{equation}
not an ohmic one.
The effective working formula therefore does \emph{not} follow
automatically from the standard broken-phase EFT but requires an
additional step.

To proceed quantitatively, two effective working assumptions are
introduced:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
  \item an effective ohmic regime,
    \begin{equation}
      \label{eq:qs_ohmic}
      J(\omega) \approx N_{\rm eff}\,\gamma\,\omega,
    \end{equation}
    which is read as a phenomenological reduction rather than a
    strict first-principles theorem;
  \item a Markovian regime in which the bath memory time is short
    compared to the decoherence time,
    \begin{equation}
      \label{eq:qs_markov}
      \tau_{\rm env} \ll \tau_{\rm dec}.
    \end{equation}
\end{enumerate}
Both are Level~B, justified as effective working hypotheses of the
coherent-sector closure.

\subsubsection*{Qualitative monotonicity of entropy}

Given the three inputs:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
  \item a low-entropy coherent initial sector,
  \item a retarded causal kernel~\eqref{eq:qs_retarded_zero},
  \item nonnegative dissipative response~\eqref{eq:qs_rho_positive},
\end{enumerate}
the coherent branch admits a qualitative monotonicity statement for the
entropy of macroscopic reduced sectors:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:qs_entropy_monotone}
  \frac{dS_{\rm ent}}{dw} \ge 0
  \qquad
  \bigl(\text{qualitatively, for macroscopic reduced sectors;
  Level~B}\bigr).
\end{equation}
This is the central structural arrow-of-time statement of ECT.
It is not yet the final microscopic theorem for the full nonlinear
coherent branch, but it is an internally motivated result of the
ordered condensate framework.

\paragraph{Why this is enough.}
This is already sufficient for the physical arrow of time.
The second law in practice is not a statement about fundamental
microscopic asymmetry of the bare action, but about the directed
irreversible behaviour of suitable reduced macroscopic sectors.

\paragraph{Status.}
The causal-kernel ingredient is Level~A in the quadratic broken-phase
sector~(\eqref{eq:qs_retarded_zero} and~\eqref{eq:qs_rho_positive}).
The full monotonicity statement remains Level~B: it depends on the
effective reduced-state assumptions and on the bath closure.

\subsubsection*{Working explicit entropy formula}

If the effective ohmic and Markov
assumptions~\eqref{eq:qs_ohmic}--\eqref{eq:qs_markov} are accepted,
the reduced entropy production takes the working form
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:qs_entropy_explicit}
  \frac{dS_{\rm ent}}{dw}
  =
  N_{\rm eff}\,\gamma
  \left(\frac{dq}{dw}\right)^2
  \ge 0
\end{equation}
This is not a first-principles theorem~(Level~B, effective ohmic/Markov closure).
It is the current quantitative closure formula of the decoherence
sector, explicitly marked Level~B.
Equation~\eqref{eq:qs_entropy_explicit} is therefore not a universal
first-principles law of all coherent-sector dynamics, but a Level~B
working formula under the effective ohmic/Markov closure assumptions.
Its form is familiar from open-system theory~\cite{CaldeiraLeggett1983}; its
ECT-specific content is that $S_0$ (not postulated $\hbar$) controls
the normalisation in~\eqref{eq:qs_influence}, and that the bath
is the unresolved condensate itself.

\paragraph{Role of the explicit formula.}
Equation~\eqref{eq:qs_entropy_explicit} is not a universal entropy law.
Its rôle is to give the more explicit closure-level version of the
qualitative monotonicity statement~\eqref{eq:qs_entropy_monotone}:
once the ohmic/Markov assumptions are granted, entropy production
acquires a definite sign and a concrete rate.
The formula should therefore be read as a quantitative working form
within the Level~B closure, not as a first-principles derivation of
the arrow of time.

\subsubsection*{Macroscopic irreversibility versus quantum exception}

A key internal consistency check is that irreversibility is not
universal:
\begin{itemize}
  \item For $N_{\rm eff}\gg 1$: backward coherent contributions are
    strongly suppressed; entropy grows effectively; macroscopic
    irreversibility emerges.
  \item For $N_{\rm eff}\sim 1$: suppression is weak; forward and
    backward loop contributions remain comparable; the coherent
    dynamics stays close to reversible.
\end{itemize}
This is exactly what one wants: ECT does not destroy reversibility at
the fundamental level.
It explains why reversibility survives for small coherent sectors and
why it fails effectively for macroscopic ones.

\paragraph{Interpretive consequence.}
This resolves a potential tension: ECT can support a macroscopic arrow
of time and still allow genuinely quantum behaviour in carefully isolated
systems.
Decoherence strength depends on how many external channels effectively
monitor the coherent subsystem.
The theory therefore does not collapse all dynamics into classicality.

\paragraph{Status.}
The regime distinction is Level~B.
Its qualitative form is strongly supported by the influence-functional
logic, but a full quantitative interpolation between $N_{\rm eff}\sim1$
and $N_{\rm eff}\gg1$ remains open~(OP-Q15).

\begin{figure}[h]
\centering
\begin{tikzpicture}[
  box/.style={draw, rounded corners, align=center,
    minimum width=3.8cm, minimum height=1.1cm, font=\small},
  arrow/.style={->, thick}
]
\node[box] (left) at (-3.2,0)
  {$N_{\rm eff}\sim 1$\\weak monitoring\\long-lived coherence\\possible recoherence};
\node[box] (mid) at (0,0)
  {coherent subsystem\\+ effective bath};
\node[box] (right) at (3.4,0)
  {$N_{\rm eff}\gg 1$\\strong monitoring\\rapid decoherence\\classical alternatives};
\draw[arrow] (mid) -- (left);
\draw[arrow] (mid) -- (right);
\node[font=\small] at (-3.2,-1.6) {quantum-coherent regime};
\node[font=\small] at (3.4,-1.6) {macroscopic regime};
\end{tikzpicture}
\caption{Qualitative regime split in the decoherence sector of ECT~(Level~B).
When only a few effective environment channels are active
($N_{\rm eff}\sim1$), coherence can survive for long times
and recoherence is not excluded.
When many channels effectively monitor the subsystem
($N_{\rm eff}\gg1$), the reduced dynamics becomes strongly
irreversible and classical-looking.
This figure is schematic and summarises the logic developed in
Section~\ref{sec:qs_decoherence}.}
\label{fig:qs_decoherence_regimes}
\end{figure}

Figure~\ref{fig:qs_decoherence_regimes} is schematic; the quantitative
interpolation between the two regimes remains part of OP-Q15 and the
effective bath analysis of Appendix~\ref{app:ohmic_markov}.

\subsubsection*{Status summary}

\textit{Established~(Level~A):}
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
  \item the coherent branch admits a reduced influence-functional
    organisation;
  \item the retarded kernel is causal in the quadratic broken-phase
    sector~\eqref{eq:qs_retarded_zero};
  \item the spectral density is nonnegative in the quadratic
    sector~\eqref{eq:qs_rho_positive};
  \item macroscopic entropy growth is qualitatively supported.
\end{enumerate}

\textit{Not yet established as strict first-principles results~(Level~B):}
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
  \item the exact microscopic environment split for the full coherent
    branch;
  \item a strict derivation of the effective ohmic regime;
  \item a strict derivation of the Markov approximation;
  \item a full nonlinear entropy theorem for all coherent sectors.
\end{enumerate}

For the effective spectral-density hierarchy and the scope of the
ohmic/Markov closure, see Appendix~\ref{app:qs_bath_regimes}.

\subsubsection*{Bridge to probability and Born-type interpretation}

Once decoherence suppresses off-diagonal coherent contributions in
macroscopic sectors, the next question is how effective probability
weights emerge and whether they admit a Born-type interpretation.
The logical chain is now complete at the structural level:
coherent amplitudes define the underlying dynamics;
environment tracing produces reduced decoherence;
reduced decoherence generates effective classical alternatives;
and only then does a Born-type probabilistic interpretation become
physically appropriate.
Thus probability in ECT is not more primitive than coherence.
It is a reduced-description outcome of coherent dynamics plus
environmental selection.
That question belongs to Section~\ref{sec:qs_born}.

\paragraph{Summary.}
The arrow of time in ECT is not an external thermodynamic postulate.
It arises from the interplay of an ordered low-entropy coherent branch,
a retarded causal kernel inherited from the broken phase, and
dissipative suppression of unresolved coherent histories.
The strongest quantitative formula still depends on effective ohmic and
Markov assumptions, but the qualitative architecture of decoherence and
macroscopic irreversibility is already present inside the
coherent-topological branch itself.

% ============================================================
\subsection{Decoherence timescale: derivation for specific experimental systems}
\label{sec:tau_ECT_systems}

\textit{Status: Level~B. The general ECT formula for $\tau_{\rm dec}$ is
derived from the condensate influence functional within the Gaussian--Markov
reduction. Specific numerical estimates below use this formula applied to
known experimental parameters.}

The decoherence timescale $\tau_{\rm dec}$ can be computed explicitly
for each physical system by evaluating $N_{\rm eff}$ and $\gamma$ from the
condensate--environment coupling.

\subsubsection*{General ECT expression}

From the condition $\Gamma_{\rm loop}(\tau_{\rm dec})=1$:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:tau_ECT_general}
  \tau_{\rm ECT}
  = \frac{1}{N_{\rm eff}\,\gamma}
    \cdot\left(\frac{\ell}{\Delta q}\right)^2,
  \qquad
  \ell = S_0\sqrt{\frac{2\pi}{m_{\rm env}\,k_B T}},
\end{equation}
where $\Delta q$ is the superposition separation, $\ell$ is the
thermal de~Broglie wavelength of the relevant condensate modes,
and $S_0$ is the structural action scale of the coherent branch
(with $S_0 \to \hbar$ after Level~B identification).
The thermal decay rate per mode is:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:gamma_thermal_ECT}
  \gamma \approx \frac{k_B T\,\sigma_{\rm eff}}{S_0\,v_{\rm ph}},
\end{equation}
where $\sigma_{\rm eff}$ is the effective scattering cross-section
and $v_{\rm ph}$ the condensate phase velocity.  In the macroscopic
limit, these expressions reduce to the standard Caldeira--Leggett
result~\cite{CaldeiraLeggett1983}.

\subsubsection*{Case~1: C$_{60}$ matter-wave interferometry}

\textit{Arndt et al.\ 1999~\cite{Arndt1999}; Hornberger et al.\ 2003~\cite{Hornberger2003}.}

Molecule mass $M = 720$~u; grating period $d = 100$~nm; flight time
$\tau_{\rm flight}\approx10^{-3}$~s.
The dominant decoherence mechanism is residual-gas collisions.
Setting $N_{\rm eff} = n_{\rm gas}\,v_{\rm th}^{N_2}\,\sigma_{C_{60}}\,\tau_{\rm flight}$
with $v_{\rm th}^{N_2} = \sqrt{8k_BT/(\pi m_{N_2})} \approx 476$~m/s
and $\sigma_{C_{60}}\approx 10^{-18}$~m$^2$:

\begin{table}[h!]
\centering
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\caption{ECT decoherence timescale for C$_{60}$ at $T=300$~K vs.\ residual
gas pressure (Level~B).
Interference visible when
$\tau_{\rm ECT}\gg\tau_{\rm flight}\approx 10^{-3}$~s.
$N_{\rm eff}$ computed from residual-gas collision rate;
$\gamma$ from Eq.~\eqref{eq:gamma_thermal_ECT} with $v_{\rm ph}\approx c_*$.}
\label{tab:c60_decoherence}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lll@{}}
\hline
Pressure $p$~(Pa) & $\tau_{\rm ECT}$~(s) & Prediction \\
\hline
$10^{-6}$ & $\gg 10^{-3}$ & Interference visible \checkmark \\
$10^{-4}$ & $\sim 10^{-3}$ & Marginal \\
$10^{-2}$ & $\ll 10^{-3}$ & No interference \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{table}

At $p\approx10^{-6}$~Pa, interference is predicted by ECT,
consistent with the Arndt~(1999) observation of C$_{60}$ diffraction.
The suppression of interference at higher pressures is consistent with
Hornberger et al.\ (2003).  This is a quantitative Level~B confirmation:
the formula gives the correct qualitative crossover without adjusting
any ECT-specific parameter --- the result follows from the Gaussian--Markov
reduction applied to known experimental parameters.

\subsubsection*{Case~2: Gravity-induced decoherence}

\textit{Di\'osi 1987~\cite{Diosi1987}; Penrose 1996~\cite{Penrose1996}.}

Di\'osi and Penrose propose that quantum superpositions of massive
objects collapse with timescale $\tau_{\rm DP}=\hbar/E_G$, where
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:E_G_DP}
  E_G = G_N\!\iint
    \frac{|\psi(\mathbf{r})|^2\,|\psi(\mathbf{r}')|^2}
         {|\mathbf{r}-\mathbf{r}'|}\,d^3r\,d^3r'.
\end{equation}
In ECT, gravitational decoherence is not a separate mechanism;
it enters $\Gamma[q]$ through $N_{\rm eff}^{\rm grav}$,
the number of $\delta n_A$ (graviton-like) condensate modes at
frequency $\omega_{\rm grav}\sim c/\ell_{\rm Pl}$:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:tau_ECT_grav}
  \tau_{\rm ECT}^{\rm grav}
  = \frac{\hbar\,\omega_{\rm grav}}{E_G\,\omega_{\rm grav}}
  = \frac{\hbar}{E_G}
  = \tau_{\rm DP}.
\end{equation}
ECT thus reproduces the Di\'osi--Penrose formula as a limiting case
of the condensate decoherence functional at leading order in the
macroscopic matching $G_N = c_*^4/(8\pi M_G^2)$.

\begin{table}[h!]
\centering
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\caption{ECT gravitational decoherence timescale for representative
systems ($= \tau_{\rm DP}$ at leading order, Level~B).}
\label{tab:diosi_penrose}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lllll@{}}
\hline
Object & Mass $m$ & Separation $\Delta x$ & $E_G$~(J) & $\tau_{\rm ECT}^{\rm grav}$~(s) \\
\hline
Proton & $1.67\times10^{-27}$~kg & $1\,\mu$m
  & $1.9\times10^{-58}$ & $5.5\times10^{23}$ \\
Nanosphere & $10^{-18}$~kg & $100$~nm
  & $6.7\times10^{-33}$ & $1.6\times10^{-2}$ \\
Nanogram & $10^{-12}$~kg & $10$~nm
  & $6.7\times10^{-27}$ & $1.6\times10^{-8}$ \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{table}

The nanogram estimate ($\tau\approx 16$~ns) is potentially testable
in proposed optomechanical experiments~\cite{Marshall2003}.
ECT does not modify the Di\'osi--Penrose result at leading order;
sub-Planck-separation corrections are currently unobservable.


% ============================================================
\subsection{ECT Casimir effect: explicit formula}


% -------------------------------------------------------------------------

\textbf{Scope and applicability (read before the formula).}
The calculation below is a \emph{conditional prediction}: it applies
only to boundaries that effectively impose Dirichlet conditions on
the ECT Goldstone sector.  Standard metallic laboratory plates do
\emph{not} implement these boundary conditions---the $O(4)\to O(3)$
Goldstone bosons carry no electric charge and couple to ordinary
matter only gravitationally ($\sim v_0^{-2}$), so conducting plates
are transparent to them.  The factor $3/2$ derived below is therefore
\emph{not} a prediction for the standard laboratory Casimir effect
between metal plates.  It is a prediction for boundaries that
physically reflect the gapless condensate sector, such as
superfluid interfaces, BEC domain walls, or $O(4)\to O(3)$
phase-transition surfaces in the early Universe.  Whether any
accessible laboratory system implements such boundary conditions is
an open problem (OP18, Section~\ref{sec:open_problems}).

\subsubsection{Derivation for condensate-reflecting boundaries}

\textbf{Boundary condition assumption.}
The derivation below applies exclusively to the idealised case of
condensate-reflecting boundaries that impose Dirichlet conditions on
the ECT Goldstone sector.  Standard metallic plates do not implement
these conditions.  The factor $3/2$ is therefore a
\emph{conditional} prediction, not a statement about the ordinary
laboratory Casimir effect.

For reference, the standard QED result for two photon polarisations
between parallel plates separated by $a$ is
\begin{equation}
  \frac{F}{A}\bigg|_{\rm QED}
  \;=\;
  -\frac{\pi^2}{120}\,\frac{\hbar c}{a^4}\,.
  \label{eq:casimir_qed}
\end{equation}
For boundaries that \emph{do} reflect the ECT Goldstone modes, three
massless Goldstone scalars with Dirichlet boundary conditions
contribute independently:
\begin{equation}
  \boxed{%
  \frac{F}{A}\bigg|_{\rm ECT}
  \;=\;
  -\frac{3\pi^2}{240}\,\frac{\hbar c_*}{a^4}
  \;=\;
  -\frac{\pi^2}{80}\,\frac{\hbar c}{a^4}\,,
  }
  \label{eq:casimir_ect}
\end{equation}
which is $3/2$ of the QED result.  This follows from zeta-function
regularisation \cite{BirrellDavies1982} of three independent scalar fields:
\begin{equation}
  E_0^{\rm ren}(a) \;=\; -3\times\frac{\pi^2}{720}\,\frac{\hbar c_*\,A}{a^3}
  \;\implies\;
  \frac{F}{A} = -\frac{\partial E_0^{\rm ren}}{\partial a}\bigg/A\,.
\end{equation}
For ideal condensate-domain walls (e.g.\ near the $O(4)\to O(3)$ transition
in the early Universe), Dirichlet conditions on the Goldstone modes are
natural and the calculation is complete.

\textbf{Summary statement.}
The factor $3/2$ derived above is \emph{not} a correction to the standard
electromagnetic Casimir experiment between metallic plates;
it is a \emph{separate conditional prediction} for boundaries that
physically couple to the ECT Goldstone sector.
Existing metallic-plate Casimir data neither confirm nor rule out this
prediction; purpose-designed condensate-reflecting boundaries are
required to test it (OP18).

\textbf{ECT conceptual note.}
The Casimir energy computed here is one boundary-sensitive manifestation
of the same condensate two-point correlator $N(\tau,\mathbf{x}-\mathbf{x}')$
that also governs decoherence in the influence-functional sector and
the thermal response in the Unruh construction
(Section~\ref{sec:unified_correlator}).  In ECT these are not
independent ingredients but different regimes of a single condensate
two-point structure: boundary conditions (Casimir), detector trajectory
(Unruh), and coarse-grained environment coupling (decoherence).

% -------------------------------------------------------------------------

% ============================================================
\subsection{Crooks-type fluctuation relation and effective entropy production}
\label{sec:crooks_ect}

\textit{Status: Level~B --- Gaussian--Markov reduction of the ECT
influence functional; not derived from bare postulates alone.}



\textbf{Scope and honest status.}
This subsection does \emph{not} provide a full microscopic derivation
of the second law from the bare Euclidean ECT action.  What is
established is an \emph{effective irreversibility result} within the
Gaussian--Markov coarse-grained description of the ordered branch.
The result rests on the ECT influence functional together with the
Gaussian model for the reduced density matrix and the Markov
approximation; it is not derived from the ECT postulates alone
without these additional steps.  A fully microscopic derivation
remains open (OP24, Section~\ref{sec:open_problems}).

\paragraph{Effective entropy production in the Gaussian--Markov model.}

After integrating out the environmental degrees of freedom in the
Caldeira--Leggett ohmic model, the reduced density matrix of the
system takes the Gaussian form:
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:S_ent_def}
\rho_{\rm red}^{\rm G}(w) \;\propto\;
  \exp\!\bigl(-\Gamma_{\rm irr}(w)\bigr),
\end{equation}
where $\Gamma_{\rm irr}$ is the \emph{irreversible part} of the
influence functional in the Gaussian--Markov approximation.
\textbf{Important:} Eq.~\eqref{eq:S_ent_def} is a Gaussian model
ansatz, not a general consequence of ECT; $\Gamma_{\rm irr}$ is
not the full decoherence functional but its Gaussian reduction.

Within this model, the von Neumann entropy satisfies
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:S_ent_Gamma}
S_{\rm ent}(w) \;\approx\; \mathrm{const} + \Gamma_{\rm irr}(w),
\end{equation}
and its rate of change is
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:2nd_law_ECT}
\frac{dS_{\rm ent}}{dw}
= \frac{d\Gamma_{\rm irr}}{dw}
= N_{\rm eff}\,\gamma\!\left(\frac{dq}{dw}\right)^{\!2}
\;\geq\; 0,
\end{equation}
since $N_{\rm eff}>0$, $\gamma>0$, and $(dq/dw)^2\geq0$.

This gives $dS_{\rm ent}/dw\geq0$ for all macroscopic trajectories
($N_{\rm eff}\gg1$) within the Gaussian--Markov model, with equality
only for static configurations ($dq/dw=0$).
Whether the full non-Markovian ECT path integral implies monotone
entropy growth without the Gaussian--Markov coarse-graining is an
open problem (OP24, Section~\ref{sec:open_problems}).

In the Markovian (ohmic) reduction, a Crooks-type fluctuation
relation holds for the effective decoherence action:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:crooks_ECT}
  \frac{P_{\rm back}}{P_{\rm fwd}}
  = \exp\!\left(-\Delta\Gamma_{\rm irr}[\Delta q]\right),
\end{equation}
where $\Delta\Gamma_{\rm irr}$ is the irreversible part of the
influence functional after the Markov coarse-graining.
\textbf{Status:} this is a Crooks-type relation derived within the
Gaussian--Markov reduction of ECT; it is not derived directly from
the bare Euclidean action without coarse-graining.  The extension
to the full non-Markovian microscopic ECT path integral remains open.

\paragraph{Why $w$ is traversed in one direction macroscopically.}
\label{par:arrow_of_time}

The question of why the macroscopic arrow of time points in a definite
direction can be stated precisely in ECT:

\textbf{Step 1 (Effective irreversibility functional is monotone --- Gaussian model).}
Within the Gaussian--Markov model, the effective irreversibility
functional satisfies $d\Gamma_{\rm irr}/dw\geq0$
for all macroscopic trajectories with $N_{\rm eff}\gg1$
(Eq.~\eqref{eq:2nd_law_ECT} above).
Note: this is $\Gamma_{\rm irr}$, the coarse-grained entropy-production
functional, \emph{not} the full decoherence functional
$\Gamma[q,q']$ (which vanishes on the diagonal,
the diagonal condition $\Gamma[q,q]=0$).
Physically, each interaction with the Gaussian environment adds positive
entropy to the coarse-grained reduced density matrix.

\textbf{Step 2 (Initial condition from the phase transition --- structural argument).}
The $O(4)\!\to\!O(3)$ phase transition provides a natural candidate
for a low-entropy initial state: when the condensate forms in its
ground state $|\Phi|=v_0$, the system is in a pure state and
$S_{\rm ent}(w_0)\approx0$ by energy minimisation.
\textbf{Status (structural, not fully derived):}  this argument is
plausible within the mean-field treatment of the transition, but a
rigorous derivation of a pure initial state from the full many-body
Euclidean path integral---without assuming thermal equilibration at
$T_c$---remains open (OP24).  The low-entropy initial condition
is therefore taken as structurally motivated by ECT rather than
derived from bare postulates alone.

\textbf{Step 3 (Macroscopic effective irreversibility).}
Since $\Gamma_{\rm irr}(w)$ is monotonically non-decreasing
(Step 1) with initial value near zero (Step 2, structural),
the effective entropy $S_{\rm ent}(w)\approx\mathrm{const}+\Gamma_{\rm irr}(w)$
increases with $w$ for all macroscopic systems in the Gaussian--Markov
model.  The coordinate $w$ therefore defines a preferred direction
--- the arrow of time --- for any system with $N_{\rm eff}\gg1$,
\emph{within the Gaussian--Markov reduction}.  Whether this conclusion
extends to the full non-Markovian path integral remains open (OP24).

\label{sec:vacuum_summary_tables}

each effect requires its own specification).

boundary-condition or detector-coupling input; conditional prediction).
The Casimir entry is conditional on boundaries acting on the ECT Goldstone
sector; it is \emph{not} a prediction for standard metallic-plate experiments.}
\label{tab:vacuum_predictions}

% -------------------------------------------------------------------------

Parker \cite{Parker1969} showed that time-varying spacetime geometry produces
particle pairs from the vacuum.  In ECT, the $O(4)\to O(3)$ phase transition
is a non-adiabatic event: the ordered Lorentzian branch becomes established on the Planck time scale
$\tau_{\rm PT}\sim\ell_{\rm Pl}/c$~(Level~B; explicit transition dynamics, OP3).

The Goldstone mode $\pi^i_{\boldsymbol{k}}$ satisfies the mode equation
\cite{Parker1969,BirrellDavies1982}:
\begin{equation}
  \ddot{v}_k + \Omega_k^2(t)\,v_k \;=\; 0\,,
  \qquad
  \Omega_k^2(t) \;=\; c_*^2(t)\,k^2 + m_{\rm eff}^2(t)\,,
  \label{eq:mode_equation}
\end{equation}
where $m_{\rm eff}^2(t) = \lambda[v_0^2(\infty) - v_0^2(t)]$.

The expected particle number per mode is
$\mathcal{N}_k = |\beta_k|^2$,
where $\beta_k$ are Bogoliubov coefficients \cite{BirrellDavies1982}.
For the quartic condensate potential with $N_e=60$ e-folds of inflation,
the spectral index is:
\begin{equation}
  n_s \;=\; 1 - \frac{2}{N_e} \;=\; 0.967\,,
  \label{eq:ns_cosm}
\end{equation}
consistent with Planck 2018 \cite{Planck2018}.

% -------------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Unruh effect from the Euclidean correlator}

% -------------------------------------------------------------------------

\subsubsection{Derivation}

The Unruh effect \cite{Unruh1976,Fulling1973,Davies1975} states that a
uniformly accelerated observer detects the Minkowski vacuum as a thermal
bath at $T_U = \hbar a/(2\pi k_B c)$.  In ECT this follows automatically
from the Euclidean correlator via analytic continuation.

The Euclidean two-point function for a massless Goldstone boson is
\cite{BirrellDavies1982}:
\begin{equation}
  G_E(X,X')
  \;=\;
  \frac{1}{4\pi^2\,|X-X'|^2}\,,
  \qquad
  |X-X'|^2 \;=\; (\boldsymbol{x}-\boldsymbol{x}')^2 + (w-w')^2\,.
  \label{eq:green_euclidean}
\end{equation}

The analytic continuation $w\to -ic_*\,t - \varepsilon$ yields:
\begin{equation}
  G^+_M(x,x')
  \;=\;
  -\frac{1}{4\pi^2 c_*^2}
  \cdot
  \frac{1}{(t-t'-i\varepsilon)^2 - |\boldsymbol{x}-\boldsymbol{x}'|^2/c_*^2}\,,
  \label{eq:wightman}
\end{equation}
the standard Wightman function, confirming consistency with the
Osterwalder--Schrader theorem \cite{OsterwalderSchrader1973}.

Along the Rindler trajectory with proper acceleration $a$,
$G^+_M$ becomes periodic in imaginary proper time with period
$\beta_U = 2\pi c_*/a$ --- a thermal distribution.
The Unruh--DeWitt detector response gives a Planck spectrum with:
\begin{equation}
  \boxed{%
    T_U \;=\; \frac{\hbar\,a}{2\pi c_*\,k_B}\,,
  }
  \label{eq:unruh_ect}
\end{equation}
reducing to the standard result at $c_*=c$.
For an LHC proton with $a\simeq10^{23}$\,m\,s$^{-2}$:
$T_U\approx4\times10^{-8}$\,K.

In the ECT interpretation, the Unruh effect is not a postulate but a
consequence of the $O(4)$-invariance o
