\paragraph{Open problems of the Quantum Sector.}
\begin{description}[leftmargin=2.2em]
  \item[OP-Q1] Explicit reduced loop calculation yielding the
    first-principles value of $S_0$
    (Appendix~\ref{app:Sloop_calc}).
  \item[OP-Q2] Final identification of the pre-quantum action scale
    with the observed $\hbar$~\eqref{eq:qs_S0_identification}.
  \item[OP-Q3] Full derivation of the effective coherent Hamiltonian
    $\hat H_{\rm coh}$ for the relevant physical sectors.
  \item[OP-Q4] Rigorous derivation of quantum commutators from the
    coherent branch beyond canonical plausibility
    arguments~\eqref{eq:qs_commutator_candidate}.
  \item[OP-Q5] Exact microscopic derivation of the full nonlinear
    influence functional $\Gamma[q,q']$~\eqref{eq:qs_influence}.
  \item[OP-Q6] Derivation of the effective ohmic regime and of the
    Markov limit from the condensate bath without auxiliary closure
    assumptions~\eqref{eq:qs_ohmic}.
  \item[OP-Q7] Full first-principles emergence of the Hilbert-space
    projector and probability-measure structure from bare P1--P5,
    which would close the Gleason argument and ground the Born rule
    as more than a conditional Level~B uniqueness statement.
  \item[OP-Q8] Completed measurement theory: branch update, pointer
    stability, and record formation.
  \item[OP-Q9] Dynamical classification, production, and stability of
    topological defect sectors outside the smooth P5 branch
    (Section~\ref{sec:qs_defects}).
  \item[OP-Q10] Quantitative link between coherent-topological dark
    candidates and observed dark-sector phenomenology.
  \item[OP-Q11] Physical realisation of spinorial excitations in ECT
    and the complete second-quantised fermionic structure from bare~P3.
    Note: the Lorentz-to-Clifford route is Level~A and the conditional
    Dirac structure is Level~B~(Section~\ref{sec:qs_dirac});
    what remains open is the proof that such excitations exist in
    the ECT spectrum.
  \item[OP-Q12] Quantitative derivation of coherent-vacuum response
    effects (Casimir force, particle production rates, Unruh detector
    response) from the completed reduced coherent
    EFT~(Sections~\ref{sec:qs_casimir}--\ref{sec:qs_unruh}).
  \item[OP-Q13] Global nonlinear completion of the black-hole
    evaporation problem in the presence of a critical Lorentz-order
    shell, including
    (i) explicit shell dynamics and profile,
    (ii) generalized-entropy evolution~\eqref{eq:qs_generalized_entropy},
    and (iii) a Page-curve-type computation for the reduced radiation
    sector~(Section~\ref{sec:qs_black_holes}).
  \item[OP-Q14] Derivation of compact-object and near-horizon
    observables (ringdown frequency shifts, late-time transfer
    structure, primordial-black-hole evaporation constraints) from
    the completed critical-shell dynamics;
    fixing the closure parameters $\eta_1,\eta_2$ in
    Eq.~\eqref{eq:qs_bh_dispersion} from first principles.
  \item[OP-Q15] Quantitative interpolation between the weakly
    monitored quantum-coherent regime $N_{\rm eff}\sim1$ and the
    strongly monitored macroscopic regime $N_{\rm eff}\gg1$,
    including a first-principles derivation of the effective bath
    structure beyond the simple ohmic/Markov closure.
\end{description}

\paragraph{What has been achieved.}
Even with these open problems, the Quantum Sector has already gone far
beyond a generic statement that ``quantum mechanics might emerge''.
ECT now contains:
a coherent phase-sensitive branch,
loop quantisation structure,
a candidate action quantum~$S_0$,
a wave-dynamical reduction,
a canonical kinematic framework,
a decoherence architecture,
a Born-type probability candidate,
and a wider defect ontology connected to the dark sector.
That is already a coherent research programme rather than a loose
speculation.

\paragraph{Methodological status.}
The correct overall status of the Quantum Sector is neither ``fully
derived quantum mechanics'' nor ``purely conjectural''.
It is an intermediate but substantial result: ECT has identified the
correct structural location inside the theory where quantum kinematics,
decoherence, and probability can emerge, and has developed a large
fraction of that architecture explicitly.
What remains open is the final closure of the programme.

\paragraph{Bridge to the rest of the paper.}
With this status map in place, the role of the Quantum Sector inside
the full ECT paper becomes clear.
ECT basics establishes that a coherent-topological branch exists.
Macroscopic Physics develops the phase-insensitive geometric branch.
The present section develops the phase-sensitive coherent branch.
Later comparison and outlook sections can therefore assess ECT as a
two-branch theory with one common ordered-condensate foundation.

\paragraph{What ECT does and does not establish in the Quantum Sector.}
The Quantum Sector of ECT should not be read as a complete derivation
of all standard quantum laws from the bare postulates.
Its present strength lies elsewhere: it organises the
coherent-topological branch into a unified structure, clarifies which
results are already structural, which are closure-dependent, and which
remain open, and substantially narrows the space of admissible
interpretations.
In several places the gain is not a full derivation, but a strong
exclusion result: some options that would remain logically possible
in a looser framework are no longer compatible with ECT once its
postulate structure is taken seriously.

\paragraph{Summary.}
The Quantum Sector is now structurally complete enough to stand beside
Macroscopic Physics as the second major developed branch of ECT.
It is not yet finished in the strongest first-principles sense, but it
is already sufficiently articulated, internally organised, and
self-critical to support the later comparison, prediction, and outlook
sections of the paper.

\part{Summary, Comparisons, and Outlook}
\label{part:summary}
%==============================================================

\section{Discussion}
\label{sec:discussion}

We now discuss the conceptual interpretation, limitations,
and future directions of the ECT framework.

\subsection{Conceptual interpretation of the framework}

ECT proposes that Lorentzian spacetime, quantum dynamics, and
gravitational interactions can all be obtained from a single
underlying structure: a scalar condensate in four-dimensional
Euclidean space with spontaneously broken $O(4)$ symmetry.
This is a working hypothesis supported by the results presented
here at varying levels of rigour, as classified in
Table~\ref{tab:ect-levels}.

This perspective inverts the conventional logic of quantum gravity.
Rather than attempting to quantise an existing spacetime geometry, ECT
starts from a fundamentally Euclidean arena where no distinction
between space and time exists, and recovers the Lorentzian structure
as an effective property of the symmetry-broken vacuum.  The
Lorentzian metric, the causal cone, and the arrow of time all arise
from the same condensate background that provides a common
parameter-matching framework for $G_N$, $\hbar$, and $c_*$
(internal consistency relations; non-circular derivation open, OP-$\Lambda$).

This framework should not be interpreted as claiming that time is
``unreal''.  Rather, it suggests that the distinction between temporal
and spatial coordinates---encoded in the metric signature---is a
collective, emergent property of the vacuum state, much as superfluidity
is a collective property of helium-4 below the $\lambda$-point.

\subsection{Emergence of physical frameworks from the condensate}
\label{subsec:emergence_chains}

A central claim of ECT is that several major physical frameworks can be
recovered as limiting descriptions or organised sectors of one ordered
condensate structure.
In the present article this claim must be stated with explicit status
discipline: some recoveries are structural, some are effective, and some
remain incomplete.

\paragraph{General relativity.}
The ordered broken phase generates an effective Lorentzian propagation
sector and a macroscopic tensor branch.
At linear level the tensor sector admits a Fierz--Pauli-like structure;
in the frozen-order pure-metric limit the Einstein--Hilbert form is the
unique two-derivative closure in four dimensions.
The full $\phi$-first nonlinear macroscopic closure remains effective.
\emph{Status: structural Level~A for the ordered Lorentzian branch and
for the pure-metric uniqueness statement; Level~B for the completed
macroscopic closure used observationally.}

\paragraph{Quantum coherent dynamics.}
The coherent branch supports a structural action scale $S_0$, winding
sectors, canonical phase dynamics, and a Schr\"odinger-type reduction in
which $S_0$ plays the role of the quantum action scale.
However, the final physical identification $S_0=\hbar$, the completed
observational Schr\"odinger equation, and the full canonical quantum
interpretation remain below unconditional Level~A.
\emph{Status: structural Level~A for the existence of the coherent
action scale and the phase/canonical framework; Level~B for the final
physical $\hbar$ identification and completed observational quantum
laws.}

\paragraph{Decoherence and the macroscopic arrow of time.}
ECT provides a subsystem--environment logic in which reduced-state
decoherence and effective entropy growth arise naturally once many bath
modes are traced out.
This supports a macroscopic arrow of time without postulating a
fundamental microscopic irreversibility.
The fully quantitative entropy law remains closure-dependent.
\emph{Status: Level~A for the structural reduced-state logic;
Level~B for explicit monotonic entropy growth laws under effective
bath assumptions.}

\paragraph{Galactic weak-field phenomenology.}
The present critical $\phi$-branch closure captures BTFR/RAR-type
behaviour, environmentally sensitive acceleration scales, and flat
rotation-curve phenomenology without introducing a standard
particle-dark-matter halo at the level of the current closure.
\emph{Status: Level~B effective macroscopic closure.}

\paragraph{Gauge and matter sectors.}
ECT provides a condensate framework in which gauge and matter sectors can
be embedded consistently, but the exact Standard Model gauge group,
fermion-generation structure, and full coupling hierarchy are not yet
derived uniquely from the bare postulates.
\emph{Status: partial structural embedding with major open problems.}

\paragraph{Interpretive conclusion.}
The correct claim is therefore not that every established theory has
already been rederived as a completed Level~A theorem.
Rather, ECT organises general relativity, coherent quantum dynamics,
decoherence, vacuum-response effects, and dark-sector phenomenology
inside one common ordered-medium picture while making explicit which
parts are structural, which are effective, and which remain open.


\subsection{Limitations of the present formulation}

Several important limitations should be noted.

(i)~The Standard Model gauge group $SU(3) \times SU(2) \times U(1)$ is
embedded within the condensate structure but not derived from it.
The colour group $SU(3)$ has no identified origin in the $O(4)$
breaking pattern.

(ii)~The galactic weak-field sector is currently implemented
through an exploratory algebraic closure of the Lorentz-order
field $\phi$, not yet through a full boundary-value solution
of the $\phi$-equation.  The deep-IR critical form
$\mathcal{F} \propto Y_\phi^{3/2}$ is a hypothesis motivated
by 3D scale invariance, not yet a full nonperturbative
derivation.  The present closure captures the screened and
deep-critical asymptotics but does not yet reproduce the
full inner morphology of all observed rotation curves.

(iii)~The critical acceleration scale $g_\dagger$ is not
treated as a universal fundamental constant in ECT.
In the current implementation it is controlled by the
ambient Lorentz-order background $\phi_{\rm env}$.
The observed galaxy-to-galaxy scatter should therefore be
interpreted as part of the physics to be explained, not
as a failure of universality.

(iv)~Three fermion generations, the Yukawa coupling hierarchy, and
the fine structure constant $\alpha_{\rm fs} = 1/137$ are not
explained.

(v)~A rigorous power-counting analysis of graviton loops on the
Euclidean background has not been performed; the claim of potential
UV safety remains a conjecture.

(vi)~The derivation of thermodynamic irreversibility required a
causal response kernel $K(\tau < 0) = 0$, which is structurally motivated
by the Lorentzian causal structure of ECT (Section~\ref{sec:second_law}).
The effective second law holds within the Gaussian--Markov approximation;
a full microscopic derivation remains open (OP24).

\subsection{Future directions}

The most important open problems for future work include:

(i)~Replacing the algebraic $\phi$-closure model by a full
spherical boundary-value solver for $\phi(r)$, with explicit
environmental boundary conditions, realistic baryonic
components (including SPARC gas profiles), and eventually
full axisymmetric disk geometry.

(ii)~A full two-loop RG analysis connecting the condensate
scales ($v_0 \sim M_{\rm Pl}$, $v_2 = 246$~GeV, galactic
$\phi$-sector) through the running of $\lambda(\mu)$.

(iii)~Numerical simulations of condensate evolution during cosmological
phase transitions, including predictions for the primordial power
spectrum beyond the slow-roll approximation.

(iv)~A systematic comparison of ECT predictions with the full SPARC
database (175 galaxies), including the $\phi_{\rm env}$--environment
correlation test.

(v)~Derivation of the Standard Model gauge structure from the internal
symmetries of the condensate, rather than embedding it by hand.

\paragraph{The Great Attractor and large-scale flows.}
The Great Attractor region (distance $\sim 60\,$Mpc,
peculiar velocity $\sim 600\,$km\,s$^{-1}$) is a
large-scale gravitational anomaly usually attributed to a
dark-matter overdensity.  In the $\phi$-framework, an
overdense supercluster region has high $\phi_{\rm env}$
(deeply Lorentzian, screened), but the surrounding
intermediate-density regions through which infalling
galaxies move have \emph{lower} $\phi_{\rm env}$ and
therefore enhanced $G_{\rm eff}$.  This amplification of
the apparent gravitational pull from the transition zone
could contribute to the observed infall pattern without
requiring a dark-matter halo as massive as the $\Lambda$CDM
estimate.  A quantitative prediction requires solving the
$\phi$-equation on Mpc scales, which is part of the
full recalculation programme (OP21).

(v)~Derivation of the Standard Model gauge structure from the internal
symmetries of the condensate, rather than embedding it by hand.

(vi)~Exploration of whether additional fundamental constants
(Boltzmann constant, fine structure constant) can be related to
condensate parameters.

\paragraph{The Lorentz-order field as an organising principle.}
A recurring theme of the present work is that the
Lorentz-order field $\phi = \ln(\chi/\chi_{\rm vac})$
provides a single variable that organises multiple
aspects of the theory:
the effective gravitational regime (Newtonian, MOND-like,
or quantum/Planckian) is controlled by the local value and
gradient of $\phi$;
screening in dense environments, the BTFR, environmental
modulation of $g_\dagger$, and the cosmological acceleration
scale all follow from the $\phi$-dynamics;
the transition between GR and modified gravity is not
merely a matter of curvature or distance but of the local
degree of Lorentzian ordering of the vacuum.
A central next step is to promote the galactic order field
to a cosmological background $\phi_{\rm bg}(t)$ plus
inhomogeneous perturbations, unifying late-time acceleration,
the redshift evolution of $g_\dagger$, lensing and
gravitational slip, and galactic dynamics within one
vacuum-order framework (OP-new-4, OP21).

\paragraph{Gauge interactions and the vacuum-order hierarchy.}
At present the Lorentz-order field should not be interpreted
as a derivation of the electromagnetic, weak, or strong
interactions: these emerge from the phase symmetries of the
condensate (Section~\ref{sec:gauge}), not from $\phi$.
However, $\phi$ may play an indirect role: as the order
parameter controlling the macroscopic phase of the vacuum,
it may determine \emph{in which regime} certain effective
low-energy sectors are realised.  A deeper question for
future work is whether the emergence of gauge sectors can
also be organised relative to this vacuum-order hierarchy.

\paragraph{The cleanest tests.}
The most informative empirical tests of the
Lorentz-order-field mechanism are expected not in the
highest-mass systems, but in the most weakly screened
low-density environments---void dwarfs, diffuse groups,
outer disks---where the vacuum sits closest to the critical
Lorentzian boundary.  Environment-dependent transition
morphologies (the detailed shape of the Newtonian-to-MOND
transition, not just the asymptotic $g_\dagger$) may provide
a further high-quality diagnostic.


%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\section{Conclusion}
\label{sec:conclusion}

\paragraph{Overview of the framework.}

In this work we have developed the Euclidean Condensate Theory (ECT), in
which spacetime and gravitational dynamics arise from a condensate
structure of the vacuum.
The complete theoretical identity of the framework is captured by four
fundamental laws (Section~\ref{sec:laws_ect}) and six signature
equations (Section~\ref{sec:signature_eqs}).
The derivational chain running from the postulates to the observational
predictions is mapped in Table~\ref{tab:ect_structure}, while the full
classification of results by derivation level is given in
Table~\ref{tab:ect-levels}.
All phenomenological inputs are listed explicitly in
Section~\ref{sec:ssb}. Starting from a small set of basic principles
— Euclidean symmetry, spontaneous symmetry breaking, and condensate
dynamics — we have shown how several key elements of relativistic and
quantum physics can emerge within a unified framework.

The central hypothesis is that the vacuum corresponds to a condensate
field possessing an underlying $O(4)$ symmetry. A spontaneous symmetry
breaking

\[
O(4)\rightarrow O(3)
\]

selects a preferred direction which appears as the time dimension of the
emergent spacetime. Perturbations propagating in this condensate
experience an effective Lorentzian geometry while the microscopic
description remains fundamentally Euclidean.

Within this framework several fundamental constants acquire structured
roles inside the ordered condensate description, but not all of them are
already obtained as unconditional first-principles derivations.
The speed of light is identified with the propagation velocity of the
ordered low-energy sector.
The observed gravitational coupling enters through geometric EFT matching
in the macroscopic tensor branch~(Level~B).
The coherent sector contains a structural pre-quantum action scale~$S_0$,
while the final physical identification $S_0=\hbar$ remains a
Level~B/open step rather than a completed Level~A theorem.

\paragraph{Quantum vacuum structure.}

A distinctive feature of ECT, developed in Section~\ref{sec:quantum_vacuum},
is that three quantum vacuum phenomena --- the conditional Goldstone-sector
Casimir-type vacuum shift, the Unruh temperature, and cosmological particle
production --- are all controlled
by related limits of the condensate two-point function
$G_E=(4\pi^2|X-X'|^2)^{-1}$ (organizing proposition;
each effect still requires its own boundary, detector, or
coarse-graining specification).
The Casimir pressure ratio $3/2$ is derived for condensate-reflecting
boundaries (\emph{not} predicted for standard metallic plates;
see Section~\ref{sec:casimir}).
The Unruh temperature $T_U=\hbar a/(2\pi c_* k_B)$ is derived by
continuing the $O(4)$-invariant correlator onto the Rindler trajectory.
Time-dependent ordered backgrounds naturally admit Bogoliubov-type mode
mixing, while inflationary benchmark values such as
$n_s \simeq 1-2/N_e \approx 0.967$ belong to the effective cosmological
ordering closure developed in the macroscopic branch~(Level~B) rather than
to a standalone first-principles vacuum theorem.

\paragraph{Observational validation.}

The galactic weak-field sector of ECT is interpreted through
the nonlinear response of the Lorentz-order field $\phi$, not
through a kpc-scale variation of the heavy condensate amplitude.
This response is modelled by the algebraic closure
introduced in Section~\ref{sec:galactic_dynamics}, parameterised
by the effective galactic critical scale $g^\dagger_{\rm eff}$.

Within this framework, flat rotation curves, the RAR, and the
BTFR are interpreted as manifestations of a critical $\phi$-branch
rather than as evidence for particle dark matter.  The full SPARC
sample analysis (165 galaxies, fixed and free $M/L$ modes)
yields median reduced $\chi^2$ competitive with MOND and lower
than MOND on the clean sub-sample; see Table~\ref{tab:sparc_summary_main}.
The preferred baseline scale clusters around $cH_0/(2\pi)$,
with galaxy-to-galaxy scatter that may reflect genuine environment
dependence or residual modelling systematics.  These results should
be viewed as proof-of-principle tests of the $\phi$-branch closure
rather than as final self-consistent field solutions.

\paragraph{Emergent galactic acceleration scale.}

A central result is that the theory \emph{admits} a
characteristic acceleration scale $g^\dagger_{\rm eff}$
controlled by the ambient Lorentz-order background.
This scale is not imposed as a universal constant
(as in MOND) but may vary with environment through
$g^\dagger_{\rm eff} = g^\dagger_0\,Z_{\rm env}$,
where $g^\dagger_0 \sim cH_0/(2\pi)$ is the cosmological baseline.
Observationally, $g^\dagger_{\rm eff} \approx 10^{-10}\,$m\,s$^{-2}$
governs the RAR, BTFR, and the flattening of rotation curves.

These phenomena all follow from the nonlinear response of the
Lorentz-order field $\phi$ in the critical weak-field branch,
without requiring particle dark matter.

An important aspect is that $g_\dagger$ is not inserted as an
independent MOND-like constant in the present formulation, but arises
within the current critical $\phi$-branch closure as a secondary scale
associated with the ordered vacuum background.  The characteristic galactic acceleration
scale arises as a secondary consequence of this framework. The agreement
between the predicted and observed magnitude of $g_\dagger$ therefore
provides a nontrivial consistency test of the theory.


\paragraph{Near-horizon critical shell.}

A noteworthy output of the present ECT strong-field closure is the
appearance of a characteristic near-horizon shell scale
\begin{equation}
  \rho_c = \frac{\ell_{\rm Pl}}{\sqrt{3\pi}},
  \label{eq:rho_c_conclusion}
\end{equation}
obtained within the current Tolman-heating / critical-shell ansatz.
In the present article this scale should be read as a
closure-level result~(Level~B), not as a universal first-principles theorem.
Its role is to provide a concrete interface scale at which the
macroscopic Lorentzian description may cease to remain complete and the
coherent-topological sector may become dynamically relevant.

This is physically suggestive and potentially useful for organising
strong-field phenomenology, but the full shell dynamics, the associated
generalised entropy evolution, and the explicit Page-curve computation
remain open problems.
The correct status is therefore Level~B:
the shell picture substantially weakens the traditional information
paradox, but does not yet amount to a completed constructive solution.

\paragraph{Dark-sector implications.}

An important conceptual consequence of the ECT framework is that both
phenomena commonly attributed to the cosmological dark sector are
\emph{interpretable within} the condensate structure of the vacuum
(Level~B/C; see open problems).

First, the late-time accelerated expansion can be interpreted as the
residual vacuum energy associated with the condensate background. In
this sense dark energy can be interpreted as the macroscopic energy density
of the condensate within the effective late-time order-field closure,
without requiring a separate fundamental cosmological constant
(Level~B; full first-principles derivation remains open).

Second, the gravitational phenomena usually attributed to dark matter
are reinterpreted in ECT as manifestations of the nonlinear
Lorentz-order-field branch: in dilute galactic environments the
$\phi$-sector activates a critical regime that enhances the effective
gravitational pull, reproducing flat rotation curves, the radial
acceleration relation, and the baryonic Tully--Fisher relation without
invoking collisionless particle dark matter.

In addition to this effective mechanism, the condensate sector may
support further degrees of freedom such as Goldstone-like modes or
topological configurations. These excitations could behave as extremely
weakly interacting or ultra-light components and therefore contribute to
dark-sector phenomenology. Determining whether such excitations are
observable or effectively hidden requires a detailed analysis of the
microscopic condensate dynamics.


\paragraph{Detectability of the ECT mass-discrepancy mechanism.}

In ECT, the dominant mass-discrepancy phenomenology on galactic scales is not
due to a new collisionless particle component but arises from the
nonlinear response of the Lorentz-order field $\phi$ in the
critical weak-field branch.  There is therefore \emph{no} additional
local particle flux to be detected in laboratory experiments, and
standard direct-detection strategies are not expected to observe
a signal.

Instead, the appropriate detection channel is gravitational: precision
tests of kinematics and lensing as a function of environment and scale.
In particular, ECT can be constrained by joint rotation-curve and
lensing analyses, by tests of the external-field effect in systems such
as satellites and ultra-diffuse galaxies, and by cluster-merger lensing
geometries (e.g.\ Bullet-like systems), where the condensate
redistribution can decouple the lensing potential from the gas
distribution.

If the condensate sector supports additional weakly coupled excitations
(Goldstone-like modes or topological configurations), these would behave
as an ultra-light and extremely feebly interacting component. Their most
promising observational signatures would then be astrophysical
structure effects (core sizes, interference patterns, small-scale
suppression, or characteristic oscillatory signals), rather than
terrestrial scattering events.


\paragraph{Detectability of the ECT dark-energy mechanism.}

In ECT, dark energy corresponds to residual condensate vacuum energy and
possible slow evolution of condensate parameters at late times. Unlike a
pure cosmological constant, this scenario generically allows mild
time-dependence, which is best tested through precision constraints on
the expansion history and growth of structure, e.g.\ via the
combination of BAO+SNe, weak lensing, and redshift-space distortions.
A key target is the redshift dependence of the effective equation of
state $w(z)$ and potential correlations between late-time acceleration
and quantities controlling the condensate background.

If the condensate parameters are effectively frozen on cosmological
timescales, the model becomes observationally close to $\Lambda$CDM at
the background level, and the discriminating power shifts to combined
constraints on growth, lensing, and consistency relations.


\paragraph{Observational prospects.}

The ECT framework therefore suggests two complementary observational
strategies.

The first is precision tests of the predicted modifications of gravity
on galactic and cluster scales, including the radial acceleration
relation, the external-field effect, and the baryonic Tully--Fisher
relation. These effects provide direct falsifiable predictions of the
theory.

The second is the search for additional condensate excitations. If such
modes exist, they would be expected to couple extremely weakly to
ordinary matter and could appear as ultra-light dark-sector degrees of
freedom. Conversely, it is also possible that the condensate dynamics
suppresses these excitations so strongly that they remain effectively
undetectable.


\subsection*{Final assessment, comparative status, and future strengthening}

The most accurate final assessment is that ECT is not yet a completed
exact theory deriving all standard physical laws from bare postulates
alone, but neither is it a loose speculative hypothesis.
Its present status is stronger and more precise:
ECT has matured into a unified research framework in which both
macroscopic geometry and coherent quantum dynamics are organised as two
branches of one ordered condensate description.
This does not yet close all open problems, but it provides a common
ontological language in which a wide range of previously disconnected
structures can now be expressed, compared, and constrained inside one
theoretical architecture.

The main achievement of the revised postulate structure is not that it
automatically converts every important physical law into an
unconditional Level~A theorem.
Its achievement is that it sharply separates what is already
structurally proved, what is closure-dependent but highly constrained,
and what remains genuinely open.
In that sense, the gain is methodological as well as physical:
the framework no longer hides phenomenological assumptions behind
theorem-like language, and it makes explicit which statements belong to
Level~A, which belong to Level~B, and which still require additional
microscopic completion.
That explicit discipline is itself a major strengthening of the theory.

ECT is also not unique merely because it attempts to unify
microphysics and macrophysics.
Other major programmes---including string-theoretic, loop-based,
pregeometric, causal, analogue-gravity, induced-gravity, and related
emergent-spacetime approaches---also aim to connect quantum structure
and gravitational or spacetime physics.
The distinctive feature of ECT lies elsewhere:
it attempts to connect, in one continuous chain, Euclidean microscopic
starting data, spontaneous ordering, emergent Lorentzian structure,
gravitational dynamics, coherent phase kinematics, decoherence,
vacuum-response phenomena, dark-sector logic, and horizon thermality.
The correct claim is therefore not that ECT has already exceeded all
competing approaches in formal completion or empirical precision, but
that it offers an unusually broad and internally linked architecture
with explicit status control across both micro- and macrophysics.

Several results are already genuinely nontrivial.
Among the strongest are:
the emergence of the ordered Lorentzian branch;
the unique macroscopic rank-2 tensor compatible with the broken
symmetry pattern;
the existence of a coherent phase branch with winding sectors;
the structural existence of a pre-quantum action scale;
the canonical organisation of coherent dynamics;
the subsystem--environment logic of decoherence;
the unified interpretation of vacuum-response effects;
and the incompatibility of fundamental non-unitary information
destruction with the ECT postulate structure.
These results do not yet constitute a final derivation of all known
physics, but they already exclude classes of interpretation that would
otherwise remain admissible.
Such exclusion results are scientifically meaningful:
a theory becomes stronger not only by computing numbers, but also by
narrowing the space of logically possible explanations.

At the same time, several central outputs remain Level~B or Open:
the physical identification $S_0=\hbar$,
the completed observational Schr\"odinger equation,
the full physical Dirac sector beyond the structural spinor route,
the full spin--statistics/Pauli theorem,
the Born rule as an unconditional bare-postulate theorem,
and the constructive strong-field shell/interface mechanism needed for
an explicit Page-curve computation.
These limitations are real and should not be minimised.
They mark the current frontier of the theory.
But they do not reduce ECT to a mere guess.
Rather, they show that the framework has reached a scientifically
useful stage: the unfinished steps are now localised, named, and
technically attackable instead of remaining vague conceptual gaps.

An important future question is whether some of these Level~B results
can be promoted to Level~A.
In some cases this may require only further derivation from the present
postulates; in other cases it may require one or more additional
microscopic assumptions that constrain the condensate more tightly.
Natural candidates for such strengthening assumptions could include:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*),noitemsep]
\item a \emph{spectral-normalisation postulate} fixing the absolute
normalisation of the minimal coherent action cycle and thereby
potentially determining $S_0$ rather than merely proving its existence;
\item a \emph{coherent-Hamiltonian closure postulate} selecting a unique
real-time generator of the ordered branch compatible with the same
action scale $S_0$;
\item a \emph{spinorial-sector postulate} specifying which condensate
representation sector realises physical fermionic excitations;
\item a \emph{projector/probability completeness postulate} sharpening
the route from decohered alternatives to a probability assignment;
\item a \emph{strong-field shell regularity postulate} sufficient to
derive near-horizon purification dynamics and Page-curve behaviour
constructively.
\end{enumerate}
Whether such additions would be elegant consequences of the ordered
medium picture or merely ad hoc repairs must be judged carefully.
But the important point is that the present framework now makes this
question precise:
it identifies not only which results remain below Level~A, but also
what kind of additional input would be needed to push them upward.

The fairest conclusion is therefore this:
ECT is not yet a finished final theory, but it is already a serious and
unusually broad unification programme.
Its strength lies in the combination of a common ontological language
for quantum and gravitational/macroscopic physics, a growing set of
Level~A structural results, explicit observational and falsifiability
targets, and an honest map of what remains closure-dependent or open.
That is already a substantial scientific achievement, and it defines a
clear route for the next stage of development.
