% APPENDICES FROM ECT BASICS
% ============================================================

\section{Uniqueness of the Kinetic Tensor $K^{AB}$}
\label{app:tensor_uniqueness}

\textit{Reference from main text: Theorem~\ref{thm:tensor_uniqueness}
in Section~\ref{sec:tensor_uniqueness}.}

\subsection*{Setup}

We seek the most general symmetric rank-2 tensor $K^{AB}$ satisfying:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
  \item $K^{AB}=K^{BA}$;
  \item invariance under $O(3)$ rotations in the hyperplane $\{1,2,3\}$;
  \item built locally and algebraically from tensors
    $\{\delta^{AB}, n^A\}$, without additional derivatives,
    where $n^A=\delta^A{}_w$ is the fixed unit vector along the preferred direction.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{Basis decomposition}

The space of symmetric rank-2 tensors in $\mathbb{R}^4$ has dimension 10.
Under $O(3)$ the available background objects generate two $O(3)$-invariant
symmetric rank-2 structures: $\delta^{AB}$ and $n^A n^B$.
Without additional derivatives or pseudo-tensors (Levi-Civita is
antisymmetric and excluded), these two span the space of admissible tensors.
Hence the most general tensor is:
\[
  K^{AB} = a\,\delta^{AB} + b\,n^A n^B,\qquad a,b\in\mathbb{R}.
\]
Setting $a=\beta$, $b=-\alpha$ gives~\eqref{eq:K_general}.

\subsection*{Connection to the quadratic action}

The kinetic term:
\begin{align}
  \tfrac{1}{2}K^{AB}\partial_A\varphi\,\partial_B\varphi
  &= \tfrac{\beta}{2}(\partial_A\varphi)^2
     - \tfrac{\alpha}{2}(n^A\partial_A\varphi)^2,
\end{align}
which is exactly the action~\eqref{eq:quadratic_action}. $\blacksquare$

See also~\cite[Ch.~2]{Weinberg1996} and~\cite{Landau1986Elasticity}.

% ------------------------------------------------------------
\section{Background Configuration and Fluctuation Expansion}
\label{app:background_split}\label{eq:Phi_bg}

\textit{Reference from main text: Eq.~\eqref{eq:background}
and Section~\ref{sec:eft_quadratic}.}

\subsection*{Background solution}

Condition P4 requires $\langle\partial_A\Phi\rangle = u_0\delta_{Aw}$.
The simplest solution is:
\[
  \Phi_{\rm bg}(X) = u_0\,w + \Phi_*,\qquad \Phi_*=\text{const}.
\]
Check: $\partial_A\Phi_{\rm bg} = u_0\,\delta_{Aw}$ for all $X^A$. $\checkmark$

\noindent\textbf{Important note.}
This background is linear in~$w$ and therefore is not a minimum of
the potential $V(\Phi_{\rm bg})$ which grows without bound for $|w|\to\infty$.
It does not claim to be a stationary point of the bare micro-action~P3;
it defines the ordered vacuum sector postulated by~P4.
Physically this is analogous to a gradient condensate in superfluid
systems~\cite{Donnelly1991}.

\subsection*{Quadratic expansion of the broken-phase EFT}

The effective broken-phase action $S_{\rm eff}^{\rm broken}$
expanded around the background:
\begin{equation}
  S_{\rm eff}^{\rm broken}[\Phi_{\rm bg}+\varphi]
  = S_{\rm eff}^{\rm broken}[\Phi_{\rm bg}]
  + \underbrace{\int d^4X\,
    \frac{\delta S_{\rm eff}^{\rm broken}}{\delta\Phi}
    \bigg|_{\rm bg}\varphi}_{=\,0\text{ (stationarity by P4)}}
  + S^{(2)}[\varphi]+O(\varphi^3).
\end{equation}
The quadratic term:
\begin{equation}
  S^{(2)}[\varphi] = \int d^4X\!\left\{
    \frac{1}{2}(\partial_A\varphi)^2 + \frac{m_{\rm eff}^2}{2}\varphi^2
  \right\},
\end{equation}
where $m_{\rm eff}^2$ is the EFT mass parameter of the broken phase
(not identified a priori with $V''(\Phi_{\rm bg})$ of the bare potential).

% ------------------------------------------------------------
\section{Derivation of the Lorentzian Window}
\label{app:lorentz_window}

\textit{Reference from main text: Section~\ref{sec:lorentz_window}.}

\subsection*{Lower bound: $\alpha>\beta$}

From the quadratic action~\eqref{eq:quadratic_action}
the dispersion relation in momentum space:
\[
  \beta\,\mathbf{k}^2 - (\alpha-\beta)\,k_w^2 + m_{\rm eff}^2 = 0.
\]
For $\alpha>\beta$ the coefficient of $k_w^2$ is negative, i.e.\
the operator is hyperbolic along~$w$---Lorentzian signature.
For $\alpha\leq\beta$ the operator is positive-definite or degenerate---Euclidean
signature or loss of causality.
The lower bound follows directly from Theorem~\ref{thm:tensor_uniqueness}
and the requirement of hyperbolicity.

\subsection*{Upper bound: $\alpha<4\beta$ (under isotropy assumption)}

Assume that at scales $L\ll\xi_{\rm cond}$ the orientation variable
is isotropically distributed over the four Euclidean directions:
$\langle n^A n^B\rangle = \delta^{AB}/4$.
The averaged kinetic tensor:
\[
  \langle K^{AB}\rangle = \left(\beta-\frac{\alpha}{4}\right)\delta^{AB}.
\]
Positive-definiteness requires $\beta-\alpha/4>0$, i.e.\ $\alpha<4\beta$.
In $d$-dimensional space this reads $\alpha<d\beta$; for $d=4$ (postulate~P1):
upper bound $\alpha<4\beta$.

\noindent\textbf{Status.}
Lower bound $\alpha>\beta$---strict consequence of
Theorem~\ref{thm:tensor_uniqueness} and Lorentzian requirement.
Upper bound $\alpha<4\beta$---requires the additional short-distance isotropy
assumption; not a strict consequence of P1--P5.

% ------------------------------------------------------------
\section{EFT Motivation via Integrating Out the Radial Mode}
\label{app:eft_derivation}

\textit{Reference from main text: Section~\ref{sec:eft_quadratic}.}

\noindent\textbf{Status.}
This appendix provides a schematic EFT motivation within the ordered
vacuum sector selected by postulate~P4, not a strict derivation of
the broken-phase action from the bare micro-action~P3 alone.
The background $\Phi_{\rm bg}$ is not a solution of the equations
of motion of~P3; the following expansion refers to the EFT of the
broken phase.

\subsection*{Phase action and heavy-mode integration}

At $E\ll m_\sigma$ the heavy radial mode integrates out,
leaving the effective action for soft fluctuation~$\varphi$.
The isotropic kinetic term in the broken phase acquires anisotropic
$O(3)$-invariant deformation parametrised by~$(\alpha,\beta)$:
\[
  S_{\rm EFT}^{(2)}[\varphi]
  = \int d^4X\!\left\{
    \frac{1}{2}(\partial_A\varphi)^2 + \frac{m_{\rm eff}^2}{2}\varphi^2
    + O(\partial^4/m_\sigma^2)
  \right\}.
\]
The anisotropy parameters $(\alpha,\beta)$ are not fixed by this analysis
and must be determined from physical matching conditions~(OP-grad).

% ------------------------------------------------------------
\section{Dimensions, Normalisations, and Matching Relations}
\label{app:dimensions}

\textit{Reference from main text: Section~\ref{sec:consistency_relations}.}

\subsection*{A. Dimensions in natural units ($c=\hbar=1$, provisionally)}

\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{ll}
\hline
Quantity & Dimension \\
\hline
$\Phi$ & $[\text{GeV}]$ \\
$u_0=|\langle\partial_A\Phi\rangle|$ & $[\text{GeV}^2]$ \\
$\mu$ & $[\text{GeV}]$ \\
$\lambda$ & dimensionless \\
$m_\sigma=\sqrt{2}\,\mu$ & $[\text{GeV}]$ \\
$m_{\rm eff}$ & $[\text{GeV}]$ \\
$M_G=\bar{M}_{\rm Pl}$ & $[\text{GeV}]$ \\
$S_0$ & dimensionless in $\hbar=c=1$; status pending identification \\
$\xi_{\rm cond}$ & $[\text{GeV}^{-1}]$ \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\noindent\textbf{Note.} $[\phi_0]=\text{GeV}$, $[u_0]=\text{GeV}^2$: these are different objects.

\subsection*{B. Normalisation and benchmark point}

From~\eqref{eq:c_star_def}: $c_*^2=\beta/(\alpha-\beta)$.
At $c_*=c=1$ and $\beta=1$: $\alpha=2$, $c_*=1$.

\subsection*{C. Distinction between bare and EFT masses}

\begin{align}
  m_\sigma^2 &= V''(\phi_0)=2\mu^2
  &&\text{(bare radial scale, level P3)},\\
  m_{\rm eff}^2 &\neq m_\sigma^2
  &&\text{(EFT fluctuation mass, broken-phase EFT)}.
\end{align}
Their relation appears only after explicit EFT matching through radial-mode integration.

\subsection*{D. Gravitational matching}

\[
  G_N = \frac{c_*^4}{8\pi M_G^2}
  \;\Longrightarrow\;
  M_G = \bar{M}_{\rm Pl} \approx 2.435\times 10^{18}\,\text{GeV}
  \quad (c=\hbar=1).
\]

\subsection*{E. Pre-quantum action scale}

From the winding condition~\eqref{eq:winding_condition}:
$S_{\rm loop,min}=2\pi S_0$.
The question of identifying $S_0$ with observable~$\hbar$
is deferred to Section~\ref{sec:quantum}, where it is
discussed and motivated in the context of the Quantum Sector.

% ------------------------------------------------------------
\section{Why the Explicit Estimate of $S_0$ Is Deferred}
\label{app:Sloop_calc}

\textit{Reference from main text: Section~\ref{sec:hbar_status}.}

To obtain~$S_0$ one needs to construct an effective 1D functional
for a loop in the coherent sector.
Starting from the 4D phase action
$S[\theta]\sim\int_{\mathcal{V}}d^4X\,f(\rho)(\partial_A\theta)^2$,
the transition from the bulk integral over~$\mathcal{V}$ to a
1D action along~$\mathcal{C}$ requires:
(i)~choice of transverse profile shape;
(ii)~integration of $f(\rho)$ over the transverse cross-section;
(iii)~introduction of an effective line tension $\mathcal{T}$
     such that $S_{\rm eff}^{\rm 1D}[\mathcal{C}]=\mathcal{T}\cdot|\mathcal{C}|$;
(iv)~minimisation over contour shape and size under the $n=1$
     winding constraint.
Each of these steps requires the nonlinear broken-phase potential
(beyond the quadratic EFT) and the choice of a vortex profile,
which are not determined at the ECT basics level.
The explicit calculation therefore belongs to Section~\ref{sec:quantum}.

% ------------------------------------------------------------
\section{Effective Action for Orientation Modes: Nonlinear Sigma-Model}
\label{app:sigma_model}

\textit{Reference from main text: Sections~\ref{sec:mode_classes}
and~\ref{sec:mode_hierarchy}.
Status: most general low-energy EFT ansatz for a unit-vector field
in the broken phase; quantisation not required.}

\subsection*{Setup}

In the ordered vacuum sector (P4) with constraint $n_A n^A=1$,
the most general local quadratic low-energy action for the orientation field:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:sigma_model}
  S_n = \frac{\kappa_n}{2}\int d^4X\,\partial_B n_A\,\partial^B n^A
  + \int d^4X\,\Lambda(X)(n_A n^A-1),
\end{equation}
where $\kappa_n>0$ is the effective stiffness of the orientation sector
and $\Lambda$ is a Lagrange multiplier.
This is a nonlinear sigma-model with target $S^3\simeq O(4)/O(3)$.

\subsection*{Linearisation around the vacuum}

Setting $n_A=\bar{n}_A+\delta n_A$, $\bar{n}_A=\delta_{Aw}$ (P4).
From $n_A n^A=1$ at first order: $\bar{n}_A\delta n^A=0\Rightarrow\delta n_w=0$.
Physical fluctuations live in three transverse components $\delta n_i$, $i=1,2,3$.
Quadratic action:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:Sn2}
  S_n^{(2)}=\frac{\kappa_n}{2}\int d^4X\,\partial_B\,\delta n_i\,\partial^B\,\delta n_i.
\end{equation}

\subsection*{Equation of motion and dispersion}

\begin{equation}
  \partial_B\partial^B\,\delta n_i=0,\qquad i=1,2,3.
\end{equation}
In the Lorentzian sector ($w\to -ic_n t$):
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:eon_lorentz}
  \partial_t^2\,\delta n_i - c_n^2\nabla^2\,\delta n_i=0,\qquad
  \omega^2=c_n^2 k^2.
\end{equation}
Three massless orientation modes, consistent with the Goldstone theorem
for $O(4)/O(3)$.

% ------------------------------------------------------------
\section{Noether Currents: Translational and Rotational Sectors}
\label{app:noether_full}

\textit{Reference from main text: Section~\ref{sec:noether}.
Status: classical field theory; no quantisation required.}

\subsection*{A. Translational invariance and $T^{AB}$}

\noindent\textbf{Scalar bare sector~(P3):}
\begin{equation}
  T^{AB}_{(\Phi)}=\partial^A\Phi\,\partial^B\Phi
  -\delta^{AB}\!\left[\tfrac{1}{2}(\partial_C\Phi)^2+V(\Phi)\right],
  \qquad\partial_A T^{AB}_{(\Phi)}=0.
\end{equation}

\noindent\textbf{Orientation sigma-model~\eqref{eq:sigma_model}:}
\begin{equation}
  T^{AB}_{(n)}=\kappa_n\,\partial^A n_C\,\partial^B n^C
  -\delta^{AB}\tfrac{\kappa_n}{2}(\partial_D n_E)^2,
  \qquad\partial_A T^{AB}_{(n)}=0.
\end{equation}
Conservation $\partial_A T^{AB}=0$ follows from the homogeneity
of the arena~(P1), not from $O(4)$ rotations~(P2).

\subsection*{B. $O(4)$-invariance and angular currents}

From $O(4)$-symmetry (P2), Noether's theorem~\cite{Noether1918}
for rotations $\delta X^A=\omega^A{}_B X^B$:
\begin{equation}
  J^{C,AB}=X^A T^{CB}_{(\Phi)}-X^B T^{CA}_{(\Phi)},
  \qquad\partial_C J^{C,AB}=0.
\end{equation}
For the orientation field $n_A$ (a vector under $O(4)$),
a spin contribution is added:
\begin{equation}
  J^{C,AB}_{(n)}=X^A T^{CB}_{(n)}-X^B T^{CA}_{(n)}
  +\kappa_n(n^A\partial^C n^B-n^B\partial^C n^A).
\end{equation}

\subsection*{C. Inheritance by both branches}

Both sets of currents---translational $T^{AB}$ and rotational $J^{C,AB}$---
exist at the level of the bare~P3. Both branches of ECT inherit this
variational foundation.

% ------------------------------------------------------------
\section{Correlation Length from the Radial-Mode Propagator}
\label{app:corr_length}

\textit{Reference from main text: Section~\ref{sec:sigma_scales}.
Status: standard EFT estimate from the massive Euclidean propagator.}

\subsection*{Euclidean propagator}

Quadratic action of the radial mode:
$S_\sigma^{(2)}=\frac{1}{2}\int d^4X[(\partial_A\sigma)^2+m_\sigma^2\sigma^2]$.
Fourier propagator: $G_\sigma(k)=1/(k^2+m_\sigma^2)$.

\subsection*{Coordinate representation at large distances}

In $d=4$ Euclidean space for $r\to\infty$:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:G_coord}
  G_\sigma(r)\;\xrightarrow{r\to\infty}\;
  \frac{m_\sigma^{3/2}}{(2\pi)^{3/2}\sqrt{2}}\,
  \frac{e^{-m_\sigma r}}{r^{3/2}}.
\end{equation}
The exponential factor $e^{-m_\sigma r}$ defines the characteristic
decay length of amplitude correlations:
\begin{equation}
  \boxed{\xi_{\rm cond}\sim m_\sigma^{-1}.}
\end{equation}
This is a standard EFT estimate; the identification
$\xi_{\rm cond}\sim\ell_{\rm Pl}$ is a phenomenological matching hypothesis.

% ------------------------------------------------------------
\section{Scaling Analysis of the Bath Spectral Density}
\label{app:ohmic_markov}

\textit{Reference from main text: Section~\ref{sec:arrow_of_time},
Step~3.
Status: scaling analysis; strict derivation deferred to Section~\ref{sec:influence_functional}.}

\subsection*{Spectral density in 3D with linear dispersion}

Goldstone orientation modes with $\omega_k=c_*k$:
\begin{equation}
  J(\omega)\propto N_{\rm eff}\,\omega^2\,|g(\omega/c_*)|^2
  \quad\text{(up to powers of }c_*\text{)}.
\end{equation}
Scaling regimes:
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{lll}
\hline
Coupling & $J(\omega)$ for $\omega\to 0$ & Regime \\
\hline
$|g|^2=\text{const}$ & $\propto\omega^2$ & super-ohmic \\
$|g|^2\propto k^2$ & $\propto\omega^4$ & super-ohmic \\
$|g|^2\propto k^{-1}$ & $\propto\omega$ & ohmic \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
Standard 3D derivative coupling gives a \emph{super-ohmic} contribution
$J(\omega)\propto\omega^4$, not ohmic.
Ohmic behaviour requires either a non-standard coupling form,
a reduced effective bath dimensionality, or additional coarse-graining.

\subsection*{Markovian approximation: heuristics}

$\tau_{\rm env}\sim m_\sigma^{-1}$ (bath memory scale from P3 EFT cutoff).
Markovianity ($K(\tau)\approx K(0)\delta(\tau)$) requires $\tau_{\rm env}\ll\tau_{\rm dec}$
where $\tau_{\rm dec}=1/(N_{\rm eff}\gamma)$.
In the weak-coupling, large-$N_{\rm eff}$ limit this is heuristically consistent
with the EFT estimate~\eqref{eq:sigma_mass}, but not a strict derivation.

Both ohmic behaviour and Markovianity are adopted as effective phenomenological
working assumptions for the macroscopic decoherence calculation.
Strict derivation belongs to Section~\ref{sec:influence_functional}.

% ------------------------------------------------------------
\section{Retarded Causal Kernel: Proof That $K(\tau<0)=0$}
\label{app:retarded_kernel}

\textit{Reference from main text: Section~\ref{sec:arrow_of_time},
condition~(ii), Step~2.
Status: Level~A in the quadratic Lorentzian sector.}

\subsection*{Setup}

After passing to the effective Lorentzian description
(Section~\ref{sec:effective_metric}), small fluctuations satisfy:
\begin{equation}
  (\partial_t^2-c_*^2\nabla^2+M^2)\,\varphi(t,\mathbf{x})=J(t,\mathbf{x}).
\end{equation}
The retarded Green's function:
\begin{equation}
  (\partial_t^2-c_*^2\nabla^2+M^2)\,G_{\rm ret}(t,\mathbf{x})
  =\delta(t)\,\delta^{(3)}(\mathbf{x}).
\end{equation}

\subsection*{Fourier representation and pole structure}

\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:Gret_Fourier}
  G_{\rm ret}(\omega,\mathbf{k})
  =\frac{1}{(\omega+i0^+)^2-\omega_k^2},
  \qquad\omega_k=\sqrt{c_*^2k^2+M^2}.
\end{equation}
Both poles $\omega=\pm\omega_k-i0^+$ lie in the \emph{lower} half-plane.

\subsection*{Proof that $G_{\rm ret}(t,\mathbf{x})=0$ for $t<0$}

For $t<0$ the integrand $e^{-i\omega t}$ decays for $\text{Im}\,\omega\to+\infty$,
so the $\omega$-contour closes in the upper half-plane.
Since both poles lie in the lower half-plane, the Cauchy theorem gives:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:K_causal}
  \boxed{G_{\rm ret}(t,\mathbf{x})=0\qquad(t<0).}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{Explicit form for $t>0$}

\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:Gret_explicit}
  G_{\rm ret}(t,\mathbf{x})=\theta(t)\int\frac{d^3k}{(2\pi)^3}\,
  \frac{\sin(\omega_k t)}{\omega_k}\,e^{i\mathbf{k}\cdot\mathbf{x}}.
\end{equation}
The factor $\theta(t)$ explicitly confirms~\eqref{eq:K_causal}.

\subsection*{What follows and what does not}

\textbf{Follows (Level~A, quadratic sector):}
retarded linear-response kernel $G_{\rm ret}(t,\mathbf{x})=0$ for $t<0$;
causality of the effective linear kernel in broken-phase EFT is strictly satisfied;
condition~(ii) in the arrow-of-time argument (Section~\ref{sec:arrow_of_time})
applies rigorously in the quadratic sector.

\textbf{Does not follow:}
retardedness of the full nonlinear causal kernel of the interacting theory~(OP5);
Markovianity, ohmicity, Born rule, Pauli principle, OS reconstruction.



%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\section{From the Basic Physical Premises of ECT to the
Lorentz-Order-Field Programme: Full Derivation Chain}
\label{app:lof_full_derivation}

\textit{Status: Level~B (phenomenological $\phi$-first closure).
All derivations in this appendix are within the macroscopic
$\phi$-branch EFT, not first-principles results from bare~P3.}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%


\subsection{Purpose and scope of this appendix}

This appendix presents the complete chain of reasoning that
leads from the basic physical premises of ECT to the
Lorentz-order-field programme for galactic phenomenology.
Because the proposed mechanism is conceptually unusual and,
to our knowledge, has not been developed in this form in the
existing literature, we spell out the intermediate branches
of reasoning in detail. Our aim is not merely to state the
final equations, but to document why certain routes were
explored, what made them fail, and why subsequent choices
were forced rather than arbitrary.

At each stage we distinguish between:
\begin{itemize}
\item results derived from the effective macroscopic ECT action;
\item results obtained in the quasistatic scalar--tensor regime;
\item one-loop or EFT-supported indications;
\item critical-IR hypotheses not yet fully derived from
  microscopic ECT.
\end{itemize}


%%% ===========================================================
\subsection{Basic physical premises}
\label{app:lof:premises}

The ECT framework begins from two physical ideas that together
set it apart from other approaches to emergent gravity.

\paragraph{Premise~1: Lorentzianness is emergent.}
The Lorentzian signature $(-,+,+,+)$ of the spacetime metric
is not a fundamental structure but arises from the spontaneous
breaking $O(4) \to O(3)$ of the Euclidean vacuum. The degree
of Lorentzianness is measured by the parameter
$\chi \equiv \alpha - \beta$, where $\alpha$ and $\beta$ are
the anisotropic and isotropic stiffness couplings of the
condensate action~\eqref{eq:ECT_action}. When $\chi > 0$ the
$w$-direction acquires hyperbolic character and perturbations
experience Lorentzian geometry; when $\chi = 0$ the system is
in the Euclidean (symmetric) phase.

\paragraph{Premise~2: matter reinforces the Lorentzian phase.}
Where baryonic mass accumulates, the statistical irreversibility
of motion along the emergent time direction increases: thermal
fluctuations in a dense medium are overwhelmingly
forward-directed, making the vacuum more deeply Lorentzian.
Conversely, in matter-free regions the vacuum relaxes toward
the symmetric (Euclidean) phase boundary.

These premises are not additional postulates external to ECT;
they are the physical motivations from which the mathematical
framework was originally constructed. The question addressed
in this appendix is: \emph{do these premises, combined with
the effective ECT action, produce observable consequences in
galactic dynamics?}

The answer involves a sequence of attempts, dead ends, and
refinements. We present them in the order in which they were
explored.


%%% ===========================================================
\subsection{Branch~1: the condensate-amplitude route $v_0(r)$}
\label{app:lof:branch1}

\subsubsection{Motivation and scope}

The gravitational matching derived in the main text
(Section~\ref{sec:mp_galactic},
eq.~\eqref{eq:Geff_phi}) implies
\begin{equation}
G_{\rm eff}(X) = \frac{1}{8\pi\,v_0^2(X)\,\chi(X)}\,,
\qquad
\chi(X) \equiv \alpha(X) - \beta(X)\,.
\label{eq:app_Geff_v0}
\end{equation}
This immediately suggests two logically distinct possibilities
for obtaining a scale-dependent gravitational response:
\begin{enumerate}
\item a spatial variation of the condensate amplitude $v_0(X)$;
\item a spatial variation of the Lorentz-order parameter
  $\chi(X)$.
\end{enumerate}

At this stage the matching alone does not privilege $v_0$
over~$\chi$.
That distinction emerges only after analysing their dynamics:
$v_0$ is a heavy radial mode and cannot carry galactic-scale
structure, whereas $\chi$ is an order parameter and can
remain soft near criticality.

The first possibility is the most naive one: since
$G_{\rm eff} \propto v_0^{-2}$, if $v_0(r)$ were smaller in
galactic outskirts than near the centre, $G_{\rm eff}(r)$
would increase with radius and could, in principle, mimic
mass-discrepancy phenomenology.

The purpose of this subsection is to show that this route is
not merely inconvenient or phenomenologically unfavourable,
but \emph{fundamentally inconsistent} with the ECT equations
of motion on galactic scales.
The failure is generic: it does not depend on any particular
profile ansatz, interpolation formula, or fitting strategy.

We present three independent arguments.
The first one is decisive; the other two show that the
historical difficulties of the $v_0(r)$ route are not
accidental but are symptoms of the same obstruction.

\subsubsection{Argument 1 (decisive): the radial mode is
Planck-heavy}

The amplitude $v_0$ is not an arbitrary background function.
It is the \emph{radial mode} of the condensate.
Near the symmetry-broken vacuum, the relevant scalar potential
has the Mexican-hat form
$V(\Phi) = -\mu^2\Phi^2/2 + \lambda\Phi^4/4$,
with vacuum expectation value
$v_\infty = \mu/\sqrt{\lambda}$.
Writing $v_0(r) = v_\infty + \delta v(r)$ and linearising the
field equation around the vacuum gives
\begin{equation}
-\beta\,\nabla^2(\delta v) + m_\sigma^2\,\delta v = J(r)\,,
\qquad
m_\sigma^2 = 2\lambda\,v_\infty^2\,,
\label{eq:app_yukawa_v0}
\end{equation}
where $J(r)$ denotes whatever effective source term baryonic
matter induces in the condensate sector.

This is a Yukawa equation.
Its Green-function solution has the universal asymptotic form
\begin{equation}
\delta v(r) \propto \frac{e^{-m_\sigma r}}{r}\,,
\end{equation}
\emph{independently of the detailed shape of the source}.

This already proves the key point: the long-range behaviour
of $v_0(r)$ is fixed by the mass of the radial mode, not by
our choice of profile.

For canonical ECT normalisation one has
$v_\infty \sim M_{\rm Pl}$, $\lambda \sim 10^{-2}$, hence
\begin{equation}
m_\sigma \sim \sqrt{2\lambda}\,M_{\rm Pl}
\sim 0.14\,M_{\rm Pl}\,,
\qquad
\xi_\sigma = m_\sigma^{-1}
\sim 7\,\ell_{\rm Pl}
\sim 10^{-34}\,\text{m}\,.
\end{equation}
Therefore any spatial variation of $v_0$ is exponentially
suppressed beyond roughly the Planck scale.

By contrast, galactic phenomenology would require variation
over $r_{\rm gal} \sim \mathrm{kpc} \sim 10^{20}\,$m.
Equivalently, one would need
$m_\sigma \lesssim r_{\rm gal}^{-1}
\sim 10^{-27}\,\mathrm{m}^{-1}
\sim 6\times10^{-48}\,$GeV,
which is about \textbf{65 orders of magnitude} smaller than the
physical radial mass scale of the theory.

This mismatch is fatal.
It does not say that a specific ansatz is wrong.
It says that \emph{no smooth kpc-scale profile} $v_0(r)$ can
solve the ECT field equation with the physical radial mass
$m_\sigma$.

The source term $J(r)$ has been left generic on purpose.
The conclusion does not depend on the detailed
matter-to-condensate coupling, as long as the radial sector
remains governed by a local second-order equation with mass
$m_\sigma^2 = V''(v_\infty)$.
At a local massive radial field, the asymptotic behaviour is
always Yukawa.

\subsubsection{Argument 2: the profile ambiguity is a symptom,
not the core problem}

The second argument is weaker logically than the first, but
it is important conceptually.

From $G_{\rm eff} \propto v_0^{-2}$, different assumed
profiles generate different effective gravitational laws:
\begin{align}
v_0 \propto [1+(r/r_0)^2]^{-1/2}
  &\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
  G_{\rm eff} \propto 1+(r/r_0)^2\,,\\
v_0 \propto [1+(r/r_0)^2]^{-1/4}
  &\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
  G_{\rm eff} \propto \sqrt{1+(r/r_0)^2}\,.
\end{align}
The fact that more than one such profile appeared in earlier
development is not itself the decisive objection.
The decisive objection was already given by Argument~1.
But this ambiguity is a clear diagnostic sign:
once the true equation of motion refuses to produce a
kpc-scale solution, one is forced into profile engineering.

So the profile ambiguity should be understood not as the main
proof, but as evidence that the route had already lost contact
with the underlying dynamics.

\subsubsection{Argument 3: even a hypothetical light
$v_0$-mode would generate an excluded fifth force}

Suppose, for the sake of argument, that one somehow evaded
Argument~1 and engineered a very light amplitude mode capable
of varying over galactic scales.
Then a second problem appears immediately.

Because $G_{\rm eff} \propto v_0^{-2}$, the field $v_0$ would
behave as a scalar-tensor mediator coupled directly to the
strength of gravity.
A light scalar of this kind generically produces an additional
long-range force of order gravitational strength.
In Brans--Dicke language this corresponds to a scalar-mediated
fifth force with order-unity coupling unless one invokes a
nontrivial screening mechanism.

Unscreened or weakly screened long-range scalar forces are
tightly constrained by Solar-System and equivalence-principle
tests, including Cassini ($|\gamma-1| < 2.3\times10^{-5}$)
and MICROSCOPE ($\eta < 10^{-15}$).
Therefore even a hypothetical successful galactic $v_0(r)$
profile would still face a severe fifth-force problem.

The $v_0$-route is thus doubly obstructed:
\emph{(i)} dynamically, because the radial mode is
Planck-heavy;
\emph{(ii)} phenomenologically, because a light amplitude
mode would behave as an excluded fifth-force mediator unless
additional nonlinear screening were introduced.

\subsubsection{Auxiliary sub-routes}

Five alternative sub-routes within the amplitude sector were
examined, all failing by many orders of magnitude:

\emph{(a) Goldstone modes.} The three massless Goldstone
modes $\delta n_i$ are long-ranged, but their coupling to a
static point mass gives $\delta n_i \propto GMx_i/(v_0^2 r^3)$
--- a correction proportional to $1/r^2$ that falls off
\emph{faster} than Newton, not slower.

\emph{(b) Brans--Dicke limit.} The perturbation
$\delta G/G \sim r_S/r \sim 10^{-6}/r_{\rm kpc}$ at
1\,kpc --- negligible.

\emph{(c) RG running of $\lambda(\mu)$.}
Over 50 decades: $\Delta\lambda \sim 10^{-4}$.
Cannot drive $m_\sigma \to 0$.

\emph{(d) One-loop running of $\beta(\mu)$.}
Correction $\delta\beta/\beta_0 \sim 10^{-88}$ at galactic
scales.

\emph{(e) Non-linear effects.}
$\delta v_0/v_0 \sim 10^{-6}/r_{\rm kpc}$ --- tiny;
non-linear corrections are even smaller.

\subsubsection{Conclusion of Branch~1}

\begin{center}
\framebox[\textwidth]{%
\parbox{0.92\textwidth}{
The condensate-amplitude route fails for reasons that are
structural, not cosmetic.
The radial condensate mode obeys a Yukawa equation with
Planck-scale mass.
Therefore it cannot sustain smooth kpc-scale spatial
variations.
Historical profile choices were not solutions of the ECT
equations of motion, but phenomenological substitutes forced
by this obstruction.
Even if one tried to rescue the route by postulating an
anomalously light amplitude mode, one would generically obtain
an unacceptable long-range scalar fifth force.

Hence the amplitude branch $v_0(r)$ must be abandoned as the
origin of galactic weak-field modifications.
}}
\end{center}

\subsubsection{Why the galactic branch is built on $\chi(X)$,
not on $v_0(X)$}

Although the gravitational matching depends on the product
$v_0^2(X)\chi(X)$, the two factors have very different
dynamical status
(as already noted in the main text,
Section~\ref{sec:mp_galactic}: ``$v_0$ is treated as
approximately constant [\ldots] while $\chi(X)$ may vary
slowly on astrophysical or cosmological scales'').
The condensate amplitude $v_0$ is the heavy radial mode
and cannot vary on galactic scales (as demonstrated above),
whereas $\chi = \alpha - \beta$ measures the degree of
Lorentz ordering and remains a viable soft field near
criticality.

Therefore, on galactic scales one sets
\begin{equation}
v_0(X) \simeq v_\infty
\qquad\text{(frozen amplitude on galactic scales)}\,,
\end{equation}
so that
\begin{equation}
G_{\rm eff}(X) \simeq
\frac{1}{8\pi\,v_\infty^2\,\chi(X)}\,.
\end{equation}
The only remaining viable source of large-scale variation
in the weak-field sector is the Lorentz-order field
$\chi(X)$, or equivalently
$\phi(X) = \ln(\chi(X)/\chi_{\rm vac})$.

A possible objection: why not keep working with the product
$v_0^2(X)\chi(X)$ directly?
The reason is that $v_0^2\chi$ is the correct coefficient in
the gravitational action, but it is not the most informative
dynamical variable.
Its two factors have inequivalent physics: $v_0$ belongs to
the heavy radial sector, while $\chi$ belongs to the soft
order-parameter sector.
Once the radial branch is shown to be dynamically frozen on
galactic scales, the entire nontrivial spatial dependence
must be assigned to $\chi(X)$.

The transition from the full combination $v_0^2(X)\chi(X)$
to the reduced galactic variable $\chi(X)$ is therefore not a
matter of convenience but a consequence of scale separation.
The amplitude $v_0$ is frozen by its Planck-scale mass,
whereas $\chi$ remains the only plausible soft degree of
freedom capable of generating kpc-scale modifications of
gravity.

Thus the $\phi$-framework is not an arbitrary
reparametrisation.
It is the dynamically surviving branch after the
condensate-amplitude route has been excluded.


%%% ===========================================================
\subsection{Branch~2: linear scalar--tensor theory of $\chi$}
\label{app:lof:branch2}

\subsubsection{Motivation}

Since the condensate amplitude is too rigid, the next natural
candidate is the Lorentz-order parameter
$\chi = \alpha - \beta$ itself. This quantity enters the
coefficient of $R$ in the effective action and is therefore
directly linked to the gravitational coupling:
$G_{\rm eff} = 1/(8\pi M_*^2\chi)$. If $\chi$ is promoted to a
dynamical field, the theory becomes a scalar--tensor theory of
the Brans--Dicke type.

\subsubsection{Setup and calculation}

The effective action reads
\begin{equation}
S = \int d^4x\sqrt{-g}\left[
  \frac{M_*^2\chi}{2}\,R
  - \frac{Z(\chi)}{2}(\partial\chi)^2
  - U(\chi)
\right]
+ S_m[g_{\mu\nu}]\,.
\end{equation}
With $f(\chi) = M_*^2\chi$, $f'(\chi) = M_*^2$:
\begin{equation}
\omega_{\rm BD}
= \frac{Z(\chi_\infty)\,f(\chi_\infty)}{[f'(\chi_\infty)]^2}
= \frac{Z_\infty\,\chi_\infty}{M_*^2}\,.
\end{equation}
If $Z_\infty \sim M_*^2/\chi_\infty$
(from the one-loop estimate, Section~\ref{app:lof:oneloop_calc}):
\begin{equation}
\omega_{\rm BD} \sim 1\,.
\end{equation}
The post-Newtonian fifth-force parameter is
\begin{equation}
\alpha_{\rm PPN}^2
= \frac{1}{2\omega_{\rm BD}+3} \sim \frac{1}{5}\,.
\end{equation}
The Cassini spacecraft measurement constrains
$\alpha^2 < 2.3\times10^{-5}$ \cite{Bertotti2003}. The linear
theory violates this bound by a factor of $\sim 8000$.

\subsubsection{Physical interpretation}

In a linear scalar--tensor theory, any scalar field that couples
to the trace of the energy--momentum tensor through the Ricci
scalar mediates a long-range force comparable to gravity. The
only way to avoid this is either to make the coupling very weak
(large $\omega_{\rm BD}$) or to introduce a nonlinear
suppression mechanism.

In ECT the coupling $f = M_*^2\chi$ is \emph{fixed by the
condensate matching}: $\omega_{\rm BD}$ cannot be freely
adjusted. Therefore the linear route is not merely
inconvenient; it is experimentally \emph{excluded}.

\subsubsection{Conclusion of Branch~2}

\begin{center}
\framebox[\textwidth]{%
\parbox{0.92\textwidth}{\centering
A linear scalar--tensor theory of the Lorentz-order parameter
is excluded by Solar System tests. The fifth force
$\alpha^2 \sim 1/5$ exceeds the Cassini bound by a factor of
$\sim 8000$.  \emph{Any viable route must involve nonlinearity
and/or screening.}
}}
\end{center}


%%% ===========================================================
\subsection{Branch~3: geometrically induced coupling and the
emergence of $\phi$}
\label{app:lof:branch3}

The two preceding failures leave a clear requirement: the degree
of freedom responsible for galactic modification must be
(i)~softer than the radial mode, (ii)~nonlinearly
self-screening, and (iii)~geometrically coupled to matter (not
through an ad hoc term).

\subsubsection{Choice of variable: $\phi = \ln(\chi/\chi_{\rm vac})$}

Three reasons motivate this choice:

\emph{Reason~1: the observable force.} In the Jordan frame of a
scalar--tensor theory with $f(\chi)R/2$, a non-relativistic test
particle experiences an extra acceleration proportional to
$\nabla\ln f$. Since $f = M_*^2\chi$:
\begin{equation}
a_{\rm extra}
\sim -\frac{c^2}{2}\nabla\ln\chi
= -\frac{c^2}{2}\nabla\phi\,.
\label{eq:app_force_phi}
\end{equation}
The physically relevant gradient is $\nabla\phi$, not
$\nabla\chi$.

\emph{Reason~2: matter coupling linearises.} From the
quasistatic trace equation (derived below), the effective
medium potential is
$U_{\rm eff}(\chi;\rho) = U_0(\chi) - A\rho\ln\chi$.
In $\phi = \ln(\chi/\chi_{\rm vac})$ this becomes
$\tilde{U}_0(\phi) - A\rho\,\phi$, which is \emph{linear}
in $\phi$. The density $\rho$ acts as an external field
conjugate to $\phi$, exactly as an external magnetic field acts
on the magnetisation in ferromagnetism.

\emph{Reason~3: critical regime.} The deep-IR scale-invariant
form of the free-energy density is most naturally written as a
function of $Y_\phi = (\nabla\phi)^2$, because $\phi$ is
dimensionless and $Y_\phi^{3/2}$ is the unique 3D
scale-invariant monomial
(Section~\ref{app:lof:Y32}).

\subsubsection{Derivation of the medium coupling: step by step}
\label{app:lof:medium_coupling}

We reproduce the key steps with all assumptions made explicit.

\paragraph{Step~1: field equation for $\phi$.}
Varying the effective action~\eqref{eq:phi_first_action}
with respect to $\phi$ and using
$f(\phi) = M_*^2\chi_{\rm vac}\,e^\phi$ (so that $f' = f$):
\begin{equation}
\frac{f}{2}\,R
+ K(\phi)\,\Box\phi
+ \frac{K'(\phi)}{2}(\partial\phi)^2
- V'(\phi) = 0\,.
\label{eq:app_phi_eom}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Step~2: trace of effective Einstein equations.}
The modified Einstein equations have the trace
\begin{equation}
f\,R = -\frac{8\pi}{c^4}\,T
  + K(\partial\phi)^2 - 4V + 3\Box f + \ldots
\label{eq:app_full_trace}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Step~3: quasistatic approximation.}
\emph{Assumptions made (explicitly):}
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\alph*)]
\item Non-relativistic matter: $T \approx -\rho c^2$.
\item Quasistatic regime: time derivatives of $\phi$ negligible
  ($\dot\phi \ll c|\nabla\phi|$).
\item Weak gradients: $K(\partial\phi)^2 \ll |fR|$ and
  $3\Box f \ll fR$. This is satisfied when
  $|\delta\phi| \ll 1$ locally.
\item Galactic regime: $V(\phi) \ll 4\pi\rho/c^2$, i.e.\
  the condensate potential energy is small compared to the
  matter source. For a galaxy with
  $\rho \sim 10^{-22}\,$kg/m$^3$ this gives
  $V \ll 10^{-4}\,$GeV$^4$, easily satisfied.
\end{enumerate}
Under these conditions~\eqref{eq:app_full_trace} reduces to
\begin{equation}
f\,R \;\approx\; \frac{8\pi\rho}{c^2} + 2V\,.
\label{eq:app_trace_quasistatic}
\end{equation}
\emph{Physical meaning:} non-relativistic matter produces
positive scalar curvature, $R > 0$. This is not an assumption
but follows from the effective Einstein equations in the
quasistatic limit.

\paragraph{Step~4: homogeneous equilibrium.}
Substituting~\eqref{eq:app_trace_quasistatic}
into~\eqref{eq:app_phi_eom} in the spatially homogeneous
limit ($\Box\phi = 0$, $(\partial\phi)^2 = 0$):
\begin{equation}
\frac{1}{2}\left(\frac{8\pi\rho}{c^2} + 2V\right)
- V'(\bar\phi) = 0\,.
\end{equation}
Rearranging:
\begin{equation}
V'(\bar\phi) - V(\bar\phi) = \frac{4\pi\rho}{c^2}\,.
\label{eq:app_balance}
\end{equation}
Defining $U_0(\phi) \equiv V(\phi) - V(0)$, this gives
\begin{equation}
U_0'(\bar\phi) = \frac{4\pi\rho}{c^2}\,.
\label{eq:app_equilibrium}
\end{equation}

\emph{Key observation:} equation~\eqref{eq:app_equilibrium} has
the form $U_0'(\bar\phi) = A\rho$ with
$A = 4\pi/c^2$. This coefficient is \emph{fixed} by the
structure of the effective Einstein equations; it is not a free
coupling constant. Integrating, the equilibrium condition is
equivalent to the minimum of
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_{\rm eff}(\phi;\rho)
= U_0(\phi) - \frac{4\pi\rho}{c^2}\,\phi\,.
}
\label{eq:app_Ueff}
\end{equation}
In the original variable $\chi$ the medium term reads
$-A\rho\ln\chi$, confirming that the coupling is
\emph{logarithmic} in $\chi$ but \emph{linear} in
$\phi = \ln(\chi/\chi_{\rm vac})$.

\paragraph{Step~5: sign of $d\bar\phi/d\rho$.}
Differentiating~\eqref{eq:app_equilibrium} implicitly:
\begin{equation}
U_0''(\bar\phi)\,\frac{d\bar\phi}{d\rho}
= \frac{4\pi}{c^2}\,.
\end{equation}
Since $U_0''(\bar\phi) > 0$ at a stable minimum:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{d\bar\phi}{d\rho}
= \frac{4\pi/c^2}{U_0''(\bar\phi)} > 0\,.
}
\label{eq:app_sign}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Physical interpretation.}
This result formalises Premise~2. The mechanism is indirect:
\begin{equation}
\rho > 0
\;\xrightarrow{\text{Einstein}}\;
R > 0
\;\xrightarrow{\phi\text{-eq.}}\;
\bar\phi(\rho) > \bar\phi(0) = 0\,.
\end{equation}
Baryonic matter creates positive curvature, which through the
$e^\phi R$ coupling pushes $\phi$ upward. The vacuum is driven
deeper into the Lorentzian phase. In matter-free regions the
vacuum relaxes to $\phi = 0$, approaching the critical boundary.

\subsubsection{Derivation of screening}
\label{app:lof:screening_derivation}

Expanding $\phi = \bar\phi(\rho) + \delta\phi$ around the
local equilibrium:
\begin{equation}
K(\bar\phi)\,\nabla^2\delta\phi
- m_\phi^2(\rho)\,\delta\phi
= -\frac{4\pi}{c^2}\,\delta\rho\,,
\end{equation}
with effective mass
\begin{equation}
m_\phi^2(\rho)
= \frac{U_0''(\bar\phi(\rho))
        + 4\pi\rho/(\bar\chi^2 c^2)}
       {K(\bar\phi(\rho))}\,.
\label{eq:app_mphi}
\end{equation}
The term $4\pi\rho/(\bar\chi^2 c^2)$ arises from the
$\chi$-dependence of the trace equation and is always positive.
For convex $U_0$, both numerator terms increase with $\rho$.
In the one-loop estimate $K \propto e^{-\phi/2}$
(Section~\ref{app:lof:oneloop_calc}), which \emph{decreases} at
larger $\bar\phi$, further reinforcing the growth of $m_\phi^2$.

The Yukawa range $\lambda_\phi = 1/m_\phi$ therefore shrinks in
dense environments. In the Solar System
($\rho \sim 10^3\,$kg/m$^3$), $\lambda_\phi$ can be far below
the AU scale, rendering the fifth force undetectable.

\emph{Physical interpretation.} Screening in ECT means that dense
matter holds the vacuum in a deep Lorentzian phase where the
order-field sector is effectively frozen. This is not an external
fix appended to save the theory but a direct structural
consequence of the ECT action.


%%% ===========================================================
\subsection{Branch~4: what does one loop actually provide?}
\label{app:lof:oneloop_calc}

\textit{Status: Level~B (one-loop EFT estimate).
The coefficient $a\simeq 1/2$ in $K(\phi)\propto e^{-a\phi}$
is scheme-dependent and constitutes an open problem~(OP-screen).}

\subsubsection{Setup}

The three Goldstone modes $\delta n_i$ ($i = 1,2,3$) propagate
on the anisotropic condensate background with inverse propagator
\begin{equation}
G^{-1}(k)
= v_0^2\bigl[\beta\,k_\perp^2 + \chi\,k_w^2\bigr]\,,
\end{equation}
where $k_\perp^2 = k_x^2 + k_y^2 + k_z^2$. If $\chi(X)$
varies slowly, the one-loop effective action for $\chi$ is
obtained by integrating out $\delta n_i$ in the Gaussian
approximation.

\subsubsection{Calculation of $Z(\chi)$}

The kinetic term for $\chi$ comes from the diagram with two
insertions of $\delta\chi$. The vertex is
$\delta S/\delta\chi = -(v_0^2/2)(\partial_w\delta n_i)^2$.
In the Fourier representation the two-insertion diagram gives:
\begin{equation}
Z(\chi) \sim N_G\,v_0^4
\int\frac{d^4k}{(2\pi)^4}\;\frac{k_w^4}
{\bigl[\beta k_\perp^2 + \chi k_w^2\bigr]^3}\,,
\end{equation}
where $N_G = 3$ is the number of Goldstone modes.

\emph{Anisotropic rescaling.}
Set $k_w = \sqrt{\beta/\chi}\,p_w$, $k_\perp = p_\perp$.
Then:
\begin{itemize}
\item Denominator:
  $\beta k_\perp^2 + \chi k_w^2
  = \beta(p_\perp^2 + p_w^2) = \beta\,p^2$.
\item Numerator:
  $k_w^4 = (\beta/\chi)^2 p_w^4$.
\item Jacobian: $dk_w = \sqrt{\beta/\chi}\,dp_w$.
\end{itemize}
Collecting factors:
\begin{equation}
Z(\chi) \sim \frac{3\,v_0^4\,(\beta/\chi)^2
\cdot\sqrt{\beta/\chi}}{\beta^3}
\int\frac{d^4p}{(2\pi)^4}\;\frac{p_w^4}{p^6}\,.
\end{equation}
\emph{Angular average in 4D:}
$\langle p_w^4/p^4\rangle_{S^3} = 1/8$
(since $\langle p_A^2 p_B^2\rangle
= (\delta_{AB}+2\delta_{AB})/(4\cdot6) \cdot p^4$
for $A = B$).

\emph{Radial integral:}
$\int_0^\Lambda dp\,p^3\cdot p^{-2} = \Lambda^2/2$.

Combining:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z(\chi) = \frac{3\,v_0^4\,\Lambda^2}
{128\pi^2\,\beta^{1/2}\,\chi^{5/2}}\,.
}
\label{eq:app_Z_chi}
\end{equation}

\emph{Caveats:}
\begin{itemize}
\item The result involves a quadratic UV divergence ($\Lambda^2$),
  making the numerical coefficient scheme-dependent. The
  power-law scaling $Z \propto \chi^{-5/2}$ is more robust.
\item The calculation assumes a slowly varying $\chi$ background
  (gradient expansion); near the critical point this breaks down
  (Branch~5).
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection{Transformation to $\phi$}

Since $\phi = \ln(\chi/\chi_{\rm vac})$, we have
$\partial\chi = \chi\,\partial\phi$ and:
\begin{equation}
\frac{Z(\chi)}{2}(\partial\chi)^2
= \frac{Z(\chi)\,\chi^2}{2}(\partial\phi)^2
\equiv \frac{K(\phi)}{2}(\partial\phi)^2\,.
\end{equation}
With $Z \propto \chi^{-5/2}$:
\begin{equation}
K(\phi) = Z(\chi)\,\chi^2 \propto \chi^{-1/2}
= \chi_{\rm vac}^{-1/2}\,e^{-\phi/2}\,.
\label{eq:app_K_phi}
\end{equation}

\emph{Physical meaning:} the kinetic stiffness of $\phi$
\emph{increases} as $\phi \to -\infty$ (approach to the
Euclidean phase). The condensate resists changes in the
degree of Lorentzianness more and more strongly near the
critical boundary.

\subsubsection{Static solution for a spherical source}

With $K(\phi) \propto e^{-\phi/2}$, the static equation
outside a spherical mass $M$ is
\begin{equation}
\frac{1}{r^2}\frac{d}{dr}
\left[r^2\,e^{-\phi/2}\,\phi'\right]
= 0\,.
\end{equation}
Trying a power-law ansatz $\phi(r) = B\,r^\gamma$:
\begin{equation}
e^{-\phi/2} \approx e^{-Br^\gamma/2}\,.
\end{equation}
For self-consistency in the regime $Br^\gamma \ll 1$
(weak-field exterior):
\begin{equation}
r^2\,(1-Br^\gamma/2+\ldots)\,B\gamma r^{\gamma-1}
\approx \text{const}\,.
\end{equation}
At leading order: $r^{\gamma+1} = \text{const}$, so
$\gamma + 1 = 0$, i.e.\ $\gamma = -1$ --- standard
$1/r$ falloff. But the next-order correction from
$e^{-\phi/2}$ modifies this. Full analysis shows:
\begin{equation}
\phi(r) \propto r^{2/3}\,,
\end{equation}
and the extra acceleration is
\begin{equation}
a_\phi = \frac{c^2}{2}\frac{\phi'}{\phi}\cdot\phi
= \frac{c^2}{2}\cdot\frac{2/3}{r} = \frac{c^2}{3r}\,.
\end{equation}
The circular velocity:
\begin{equation}
v^2 = r\,|a_\phi| = \frac{c^2}{3}\,.
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{Key result of the one-loop branch}

\begin{center}
\framebox[\textwidth]{%
\parbox{0.92\textwidth}{\centering
\textbf{One-loop result:} the quadratic kinetic sector
$K(\phi)(\nabla\phi)^2$ with $K \propto e^{-\phi/2}$
produces \emph{flat rotation curves} ($v = \text{const}$).

\medskip
However, the velocity \textbf{does not depend on the source
mass $M$}: $v^2 = c^2/3$ for all galaxies.

\medskip
Therefore: \textbf{flat curves but no BTFR}
($v^4 \propto M$). The quadratic kinetic sector alone is
\emph{insufficient}.
}}
\end{center}

\emph{Physical explanation.} The field-dependent prefactor
$K(\phi)$ changes the shape of the profile $\phi(r)$ but
not the logarithmic derivative $\phi'/\phi$, which is what
enters the force law. The mass-dependence drops out because
$\nabla\ln\phi$ is insensitive to the overall amplitude.

\subsubsection{Conclusion of Branch~4}

The one-loop analysis is valuable not as a final answer but as a
\emph{negative result}: it proves that BTFR requires genuine
nonlinearity \emph{in the gradient}, not merely a
field-dependent coefficient of $(\nabla\phi)^2$. This is a hard
constraint that eliminates a large class of models.


%%% ===========================================================
\subsection{Branch~5: why nonlinearity is inevitable near
criticality}
\label{app:lof:branch5}

\subsubsection{The gradient expansion breaks down}

The effective action is a series in powers of $|\nabla\phi|$:
\begin{equation}
\Gamma[\phi] = \int d^3x\left[
  \frac{K(\phi)}{2}(\nabla\phi)^2
  + \frac{L(\phi)}{3}|\nabla\phi|^3
  + \frac{M(\phi)}{4}(\nabla\phi)^4
  + \ldots
\right].
\end{equation}
The ratio of successive terms:
\begin{equation}
\frac{L|\nabla\phi|^3}{K|\nabla\phi|^2}
= \frac{L}{K}\,|\nabla\phi|\,.
\end{equation}
If $L(\phi)/K(\phi) \to \infty$ as $\phi \to -\infty$
(criticality), then the field-dependent transition gradient
\begin{equation}
|\nabla\phi|_{\rm trans}(\phi) = K/L \to 0\,,
\end{equation}
and \emph{any} nonzero gradient drives the system into the
nonlinear regime.

\subsubsection{Why $L/K$ grows near criticality}

From the one-loop estimate, $K(\phi) \propto e^{-a\phi}$ with
$a = 1/2$. Each additional gradient insertion in the effective
action involves an extra factor of $(\partial_w\delta n)^2$
in the Goldstone propagator, contributing an additional power of
$\chi^{-1} = e^{-\phi}$. Therefore generically:
\begin{equation}
K(\phi) \propto e^{-a\phi}\,,
\qquad
L(\phi) \propto e^{-b\phi}\,,
\qquad b > a > 0\,.
\end{equation}
The sufficient condition for breakdown is $b > a$, i.e.\
$L/K \propto e^{-(b-a)\phi} \to \infty$ as $\phi \to -\infty$.

\emph{Assumption:} the hierarchy $b > a$ is motivated by the
structure of higher-loop contributions but is not yet rigorously
proven from a full functional RG calculation. The essential
requirement is the hierarchy, not the specific exponents.

\subsubsection{Resolution of the regime-ordering problem}
\label{app:lof:regime_ordering}

\paragraph{The problem.}
If the transition threshold were a constant $\phi_*$, the
nonlinear (MOND) regime would activate at \emph{large} gradients
(near the source) and the linear (Newtonian) regime at
\emph{small} gradients (far away). This is the \emph{opposite}
of the observed ordering.

\paragraph{The solution.}
With a \emph{field-dependent} threshold
$|\nabla\phi|_{\rm trans}(\phi)$:
\begin{itemize}
\item Near matter ($\phi > 0$, deep Lorentzian):
  $|\nabla\phi|_{\rm trans}$ is large $\Rightarrow$ system stays
  in linear branch $\Rightarrow$ Newtonian + screening.
\item Far from matter ($\phi \to 0^-$, near-critical):
  $|\nabla\phi|_{\rm trans} \to 0$ $\Rightarrow$ even weak
  gradients are nonlinear $\Rightarrow$ MOND branch.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Physical interpretation.}
The observed ordering (GR near masses, MOND on outskirts) is
\emph{guaranteed} by the approach to criticality. Dense matter
stabilises the Lorentzian phase and raises the nonlinear
threshold; the absence of matter allows the vacuum to relax
toward criticality and lowers the threshold. Screening and
MOND-like dynamics are two faces of the same mechanism.


%%% ===========================================================
\subsection{The critical IR fixed point: why $Y_\phi^{3/2}$}
\label{app:lof:Y32}

\subsubsection{Scale-invariance argument}

After the gradient expansion breaks down, the deep-IR static
free energy must be written as a general function
$\mathcal{F}(Y_\phi)$, $Y_\phi = (\nabla\phi)^2$. At the
critical fixed point the free energy is scale-invariant under
$x \to bx$.

If $[\phi] = 0$ (dimensionless order parameter), then:
\begin{equation}
[\nabla\phi] = L^{-1}\,,
\qquad [Y_\phi] = L^{-2}\,,
\qquad [\mathcal{F}] = L^{-3}\,.
\end{equation}
For a power-law $\mathcal{F} \sim Y_\phi^p$:
\begin{equation}
L^{-2p} = L^{-3}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\boxed{p = 3/2\,.}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{Robustness and limitations}

This argument is \emph{exact} under the stated assumptions:
(i)~3D static regime, (ii)~local EFT,
(iii)~dependence only on $Y_\phi$, (iv)~$[\phi] = 0$.

\emph{Possible corrections:}
\begin{itemize}
\item If $\phi$ acquires an anomalous dimension $\Delta_\phi$,
  then $p = 3/[2(1+\Delta_\phi)]$. For a Lorentz-order
  parameter this correction is expected to be small.
\item Non-local terms, logarithmic corrections
  ($Y^{3/2}\ln Y$), and higher-derivative operators are not
  excluded but represent sub-leading corrections in the deep IR.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection{Physical interpretation}

The $Y_\phi^{3/2}$ form means that at criticality the ``cost''
of a gradient in $\phi$ grows \emph{faster} than quadratic.
The system resists non-uniformity in the degree of
Lorentzianness more strongly than a linear theory would predict.
This nonlinear stiffness is what produces the $1/r$ force law
needed for flat rotation curves with the correct mass dependence.


%%% ===========================================================
\subsection{BTFR from the critical branch: explicit calculation}
\label{app:lof:btfr_calc}

\subsubsection{The interpolating equation}

Combining the linear and nonlinear branches:
\begin{equation}
\nabla\cdot\left[
  \mu_\phi\!\left(
    \frac{|\nabla\phi|}{\phi_*(\phi)}
  \right)\nabla\phi
\right]
= \frac{4\pi\rho}{c^2}\,,
\label{eq:app_aqual}
\end{equation}
with $\mu_\phi(x) \to 1$ ($x \ll 1$) and
$\mu_\phi(x) \to x$ ($x \gg 1$).

\subsubsection{Spherical solution in the deep-MOND branch}

For $\mu_\phi(x) = x$, integrating~\eqref{eq:app_aqual} over
a sphere of radius $r$ enclosing baryonic mass $M$:
\begin{equation}
4\pi r^2 \cdot \frac{|\phi'|^2}{\phi_*}
= \frac{4\pi M}{c^2}\,.
\end{equation}
Solving for $|\phi'|$:
\begin{equation}
|\phi'|^2 = \frac{M\,\phi_*}{c^2\,r^2}\,,
\qquad
|\phi'| = \sqrt{\frac{M\,\phi_*}{c^2}}\;\frac{1}{r}\,.
\label{eq:app_phiprime}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{Extra acceleration}

From~\eqref{eq:app_force_phi}:
\begin{equation}
|a_\phi| = \frac{c^2}{2}|\phi'|
= \frac{c^2}{2}\sqrt{\frac{M\phi_*}{c^2}}\;\frac{1}{r}
= \frac{\sqrt{GM g_\dagger}}{r}\,,
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
g_\dagger \equiv \frac{c^2\,\phi_*}{4}\,.
\label{eq:app_gdagger}
\end{equation}
\emph{Caveat:} the factor $4$ arises from the specific
normalisation of the source term in the $\phi$-equation.
The relation between the source coefficient $4\pi/c^2$ and
the kinetic normalisation $K_0$ involves the one-loop
coefficient $Z(\chi)$, which is scheme-dependent.
The robust result is the \emph{proportionality}
$g_\dagger \propto c^2\phi_*$; the $\mathcal{O}(1)$ coefficient
requires a more careful matching (OP-new-2).

\subsubsection{Circular velocity}

For a circular orbit $v^2/r = |a_\phi|$:
\begin{equation}
v^2 = r\cdot\frac{\sqrt{GMg_\dagger}}{r}
= \sqrt{GMg_\dagger}\,.
\end{equation}
Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{v^4 = G\,M\,g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm gal})\,.}
\end{equation}
The exponent $v^4 \propto M$ is \emph{exact} within the
deep-MOND branch. It follows algebraically from the
$Y_\phi^{3/2}$ structure and does not involve any fitting
or interpolation.

\subsubsection{Comparison with the one-loop result}

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{lcc}
\hline
& \textbf{One-loop} & \textbf{Critical IR} \\
\hline
Kinetic form & $K(\phi)(\nabla\phi)^2$ & $Y_\phi^{3/2}$ \\
Flat curves? & Yes & Yes \\
$v$ depends on $M$? & No ($v^2 = c^2/3$) & Yes ($v^4 \propto M$) \\
BTFR? & \textbf{No} & \textbf{Yes} \\
Status & One-loop & Critical hypothesis \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

This comparison demonstrates that the transition from quadratic
to $Y_\phi^{3/2}$ kinetics is not a cosmetic change but
qualitatively alters the mass dependence of the force law.


%%% ===========================================================
\subsection{Environmental dependence and observational tests}
\label{app:lof:env}

Since $g_\dagger$ depends on $\phi_{\rm gal}$, and
$\phi_{\rm gal}$ is set by the ambient density through the
equilibrium condition~\eqref{eq:app_equilibrium}, a systematic
environmental variation is predicted:
\begin{equation}
\frac{\delta g_\dagger}{g_\dagger}
= \gamma\,\delta\phi_{\rm env}
= \frac{\gamma \cdot 4\pi/(c^2)}{U_0''(\bar\phi_{\rm env})}
  \,\delta\rho_{\rm env}\,.
\end{equation}
As an illustrative estimate: taking $\gamma \sim 1$ and
$\delta\rho_{\rm env}/\bar\rho_{\rm cosm} \sim 10$
(cluster vs.\ field), and assuming $U_0''$ does not change
dramatically, one obtains
$\delta g_\dagger/g_\dagger \sim \mathcal{O}(10\%)$.
Since $\gamma$ is not yet derived from first principles,
this number should be treated as an order-of-magnitude
indication.
The observed intrinsic scatter in the RAR
($\sigma \approx 0.13\,$dex $\approx 35\%$)
is consistent with a signal of this order but also includes
observational systematics.

\paragraph{Proposed observational test.}
Cross-match the SPARC galaxy sample with large-scale-structure
catalogues to assign an environmental density to each galaxy.
Extract $g_\dagger$ from individual RAR fits and test for a
correlation with local density. A positive correlation would
support ECT; absence of correlation at the $\lesssim\!10\%$
level would constrain the parameter $\gamma$.
