\subsection{Methodological summary: the tree of branches}
\label{app:lof:tree}

The development of the galactic sector did not proceed by free
choice among equally acceptable options. Rather, each step was
forced by a concrete failure of the previous route:

\begin{table}[H]
\centering
\caption{Branch selection in the development of the galactic
sector.}
\label{tab:lof_branches}
\small
\begin{tabular}{clp{7.5cm}}
\hline
\textbf{\#} & \textbf{Route} &
\textbf{Reason for termination / success} \\
\hline
1 & $v_0(r)$ & Radial mode Planck-heavy
  ($\xi \sim \ell_{\rm Pl}$); 5 sub-routes also fail \\
2 & Linear $\chi$ theory & Fifth force excluded by Cassini
  ($\alpha^2 \sim 1/5 \gg 10^{-5}$) \\
3 & Geometric $\phi$ coupling & $\checkmark$ \emph{Successful}:
  sign proven, screening derived \\
4 & One-loop $K(\phi)(\partial\phi)^2$ & Flat curves but no
  BTFR ($v$ independent of $M$) \\
5 & Critical $Y_\phi^{3/2}$ & $\checkmark$ \emph{Successful}:
  BTFR + screening + new prediction \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{table}

This chain of eliminations explains why the final theory is
not an arbitrary construction but the endpoint of a constrained
development.


%%% ===========================================================
\subsection{Final perspective}

At this stage the galactic sector of ECT should no longer be
described as a mere phenomenological modification of gravity.
Nor should it be overstated as a complete first-principles
derivation. Its correct status lies in between: it is a
physically motivated, internally constrained research programme
in which:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the relevant galactic degree of freedom is the
  Lorentz-order field $\phi$;
\item matter stabilises the Lorentzian phase
  ($d\bar\phi/d\rho > 0$, derived);
\item dense regions screen the scalar sector
  (chameleon-type, derived);
\item dilute near-critical regions activate a nonlinear
  infrared branch (strongly motivated by EFT and 3D scale
  invariance);
\item this branch reproduces the observed galactic scaling laws
  (BTFR, flat curves, quasi-universal $g_\dagger$);
\item and generates a new testable prediction: weak
  environmental modulation of the MOND acceleration scale.
\end{enumerate}

The principal gap that remains is the bridge between the
perturbative (one-loop) regime and the critical IR fixed point.
Closing this gap requires a non-perturbative analysis
(e.g.\ functional renormalisation group) of the $\phi$-sector
near the Euclidean$\leftrightarrow$Lorentzian transition.
This is listed as Open Problem~OP-new-1.


\section{Foundational summary and signature relations}
\label{app:laws_and_eqs}

This appendix section provides a compact but still substantive summary
of the framework.
Its purpose is not to replace the detailed derivations in the main text,
but to give the reader a final structured map of what ECT now claims in
its disciplined form.

\subsection{Condensed structural summary}
\label{sec:laws_ect}

The present ECT formulation can be organised around four structural
statements.

\begin{description}[leftmargin=1.2em, labelindent=0pt, style=unboxed]

\item[\textbf{(S1) Euclidean microscopic substrate.}]
The bare arena is a four-dimensional Euclidean manifold with
$O(4)$-invariant microscopic action and no preferred time direction.
This is the starting point of the theory, not yet a spacetime with
Lorentzian causal order.

\item[\textbf{(S2) Ordered Lorentzian branch.}]
Spontaneous symmetry breaking $O(4)\to O(3)$ selects an ordered
direction.
In the broken-phase EFT, this generates an effective Lorentzian
propagation structure whenever $\alpha>\beta$.
Time is therefore not inserted at the microscopic level but emerges as
part of the ordered branch.

\item[\textbf{(S3) Two branches of one condensate.}]
The ordered condensate separates into:
(a)~a geometric/macroscopic branch, governing effective metric response,
gravitational dynamics, cosmology, and weak-field phenomenology;
and
(b)~a coherent-topological/quantum branch, governing phase-sensitive
dynamics, winding sectors, decoherence, vacuum-response effects,
defect sectors, and reduced-state horizon thermality.

\item[\textbf{(S4) Explicit status discipline.}]
ECT no longer presents all important outputs as if they had equal
derivational status.
Instead, the present article separates structural Level~A results,
effective Level~B closures, and genuinely open problems.
This status discipline is not a cosmetic addition; it is part of the
current formulation of the framework.

\end{description}

\paragraph{Interpretive remark.}
These four structural statements should not be read as replacing the
detailed postulates and branch analyses in the main text.
Their role is to summarise, at the highest level, what kind of theory
ECT has become in its present formulation:
not a single-step derivation of all known physics, but a two-branch
ordered-medium framework with explicit status control over its claims.

\subsection{Signature relations of the present formulation}
\label{sec:signature_eqs}

For compact reference, the most important signature relations of the
current article are the following.

\begin{description}[leftmargin=1.2em, labelindent=0pt, style=unboxed]

\item[\textbf{(R1) Effective metric of the ordered branch.}]
\begin{equation}
  g_{\rm eff}^{AB}
  = \beta\,\delta^{AB} - \alpha\,n^A n^B.
\end{equation}
This is the central tensorial object of the ordered macroscopic branch.

\item[\textbf{(R2) Lorentzian branch condition.}]
\begin{equation}
  \alpha>\beta.
\end{equation}
Additional EFT windows may apply in more specialised discussions, but
$\alpha>\beta$ is the basic sign condition.

\item[\textbf{(R3) Ordered-branch propagation speed.}]
\begin{equation}
  c_*^2 = \frac{\beta}{\alpha-\beta}.
\end{equation}
The observational choice $c_*=c$ fixes the canonical normalisation of
the broken phase.

\item[\textbf{(R4) Geometric EFT matching of gravity.}]
\begin{equation}
  G_N = \frac{c_*^4}{8\pi M_G^2}.
\end{equation}
This is not a bare-postulate microscopic derivation, but the correct
macroscopic matching relation of the present article.

\paragraph{Reading of (R4).}
Relation (R4) should be interpreted as the macroscopic normalisation of
the tensor branch, not as a one-line derivation of Newton's constant
from bare microscopic data.
Its strength is that it makes the meaning of gravity in ECT explicit:
gravity measures the inverse compliance of the ordered tensor sector.
Its limitation is equally explicit:
the microscopic reduction to $M_G$ remains open.

\item[\textbf{(R5) Minimal coherent loop action.}]
\begin{equation}
  S_{\rm loop,min}=2\pi S_0.
\end{equation}
This establishes the structural action scale of the coherent branch.
The final physical identification $S_0=\hbar$ is not yet a Level~A
theorem.

\paragraph{Reading of (R5).}
Relation (R5) is one of the key structural outputs of the coherent
branch.
It establishes that the theory contains a distinguished action scale
already before the final observational identification with $\hbar$ is
made.
This is stronger than having no quantum scale at all, but weaker than a
completed derivation of standard quantum mechanics.
The present article therefore treats $S_0$ as structurally real while
keeping the final $S_0=\hbar$ step explicitly conditional.

\item[\textbf{(R6) Effective macroscopic closure.}]
\begin{equation}
  e^\phi G_{\mu\nu}
  + \Lambda_{\rm eff}(\phi)\,g_{\mu\nu}
  + \Theta_{\mu\nu}[\phi,n]
  = \frac{8\pi G_{\rm eff}(\phi)}{c^4}\,T_{\mu\nu}.
\end{equation}
This is the current $\phi$-first macroscopic closure, to be read at
Level~B.

\item[\textbf{(R7) Reduced-state decoherence logic.}]
For subsystem variables $q,q'$ coupled to an environment,
the effective reduced description is organised by a decoherence
functional/influence structure in which the diagonal sector is preserved
while off-diagonal coherence is suppressed under suitable bath
conditions.
This is the bridge from coherent amplitudes to macroscopic alternatives.

\item[\textbf{(R8) Horizon thermality without fundamental information
destruction.}]
Near-horizon thermality is interpreted in ECT as a reduced-state
phenomenon compatible with global coherent purity.
The theory therefore rules out fundamental non-unitary information
destruction as an admissible resolution, while leaving the explicit
strong-field constructive mechanism open.

\paragraph{Reading of (R8).}
The significance of (R8) is primarily negative but important:
within the present ECT postulate structure, fundamental non-unitary
destruction of information is not an admissible resolution of the
black-hole problem.
What remains open is not whether information may simply disappear, but
how apparent thermality, reduced-state mixedness, and global coherent
purity are realised constructively in the completed strong-field sector.
This is why the horizon discussion is already stronger than a vague
speculation, but not yet a finished constructive theorem.

\end{description}

\subsection*{How this appendix should and should not be used}

This appendix is intended as a compact structural map for the reader.
It is useful for orientation, but it should not be overread.
In particular:
\begin{itemize}
  \item it does not replace the detailed branch-by-branch derivations;
  \item it does not upgrade Level~B closures into Level~A theorems;
  \item it does not imply that all standard laws are already recovered
  from bare postulates alone.
\end{itemize}
Its role is to compress the framework faithfully, not to oversell it.

\subsection{How to read this appendix summary}

This appendix should be used as a compact map, not as a substitute for
the detailed sections.
For the actual derivations and status statements, the reader should rely
on the main text and on Tables~\ref{tab:ect_structure},
\ref{tab:ect-levels}, and~\ref{tab:ECT_predictions}.
In particular, the present appendix summary should not be misread as a
claim that all standard physical laws have already been derived as
unconditional bare-postulate theorems.
Its purpose is to collect the framework in a form that is concise,
internally consistent, and faithful to the article's current
Level~A / Level~B / Open discipline.


\subsection{Three scales in the present ECT formulation}
\label{app:cosmo:scales}

For historical reasons, older ECT drafts often described several
physically distinct scales using one common condensate notation.
In the present formulation these scales are separated explicitly.

\begin{enumerate}
  \item \textbf{Microscopic condensate / correlation scale.}
  The ordered phase possesses a short-distance condensate correlation
  length $\xi_{\rm cond}\sim m_\sigma^{-1}$,
  expected to be microscopic and in the strongest closures close to the
  Planck domain.

  \item \textbf{Macroscopic gravitational stiffness scale.}
  The tensor branch is controlled by the gravitational stiffness
  parameter $M_G$, related to observed gravity through the matching
  relation $G_N=c_*^4/(8\pi M_G^2)$.
  This is the relevant large-scale stiffness variable in the present
  macroscopic formulation.

  \item \textbf{Coherent action scale.}
  The coherent-topological branch contains a structural action scale
  $S_0$, fixed through the minimal loop action $S_{\rm loop,min}=2\pi S_0$.
  The final physical identification $S_0=\hbar$ remains a Level~B/open
  step.

  \item \textbf{Galactic/environmental weak-field scale.}
  In the present critical $\phi$-branch closure, galactic phenomenology
  is organised by the acceleration scale $g_\dagger$ together with the
  screening/environment scales discussed in the Macroscopic Physics part.
\end{enumerate}

This separation should replace the older shorthand in which one symbol
was used simultaneously for gravitational, quantum, and cosmological
roles.


\subsection{Dark-energy interpretation: present status}
\label{app:cosmo:de}

In the present article, late-time cosmic acceleration is not treated as
a bare cosmological constant inserted independently of the condensate,
but as part of the effective macroscopic closure associated with the
ordered vacuum background and the order-field sector.

The relevant statement is therefore not that dark energy has already
been derived from first principles as a unique output of the bare
microscopic action.
Rather, the current $\phi$-first macroscopic closure admits an
effective late-time vacuum contribution which can be parameterised in
terms of an effective equation of state,
\begin{equation}
  w(z)=w_0+w_a\,\frac{z}{1+z},
\end{equation}
with benchmark values such as $w_0\approx -0.83$ belonging to the
current closure~(Level~B) rather than to a completed Level~A theorem.
This is compatible with the DESI~2024 measurement
$w_0 = -0.827 \pm 0.059$~\cite{DESI2024}, providing a nontrivial
consistency check at the Level~B closure level.

The correct status is:
\begin{itemize}
  \item structural compatibility of late-time vacuum acceleration with
  the ordered condensate framework;
  \item Level~B for the explicit dark-energy closure used
  phenomenologically;
  \item open for a full microscopic derivation of the relevant
  effective potential and its late-time parameters.
\end{itemize}


\subsection{Effective gravitational coupling: present reading}
\label{app:cosmo:geff}

In earlier ECT drafts the cosmological effective coupling was often
written directly in terms of a legacy condensate amplitude notation.
In the present formulation the correct reading is more cautious.

At the macroscopic level, the observed Newton coupling is fixed by
geometric EFT matching,
\begin{equation}
  G_N=\frac{c_*^4}{8\pi M_G^2},
\end{equation}
while in the $\phi$-first closure one may write an effective
order-dependent gravitational response
\begin{equation}
  G_{\rm eff}(X)=G_N e^{-\phi(X)}.
\end{equation}
This should be interpreted as a closure variable describing slow
macroscopic variations of the ordered branch, not as a bare-postulate
microscopic derivation of time-varying gravity.

Accordingly, future scenarios involving the asymptotic behaviour of
$G_{\rm eff}$, $\phi$, or the ordered branch should be read as
closure-dependent cosmological scenarios rather than as unconditional
predictions of the bare theory.


%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Numerical algorithms}
\label{app:algorithms}

This appendix summarises the computational procedures used to generate
the figures in this paper.  Full source code (Python~3 with NumPy,
SciPy, and Matplotlib) is publicly available at
\url{https://github.com/chufelo/ECT-preprint-code} .

\subsection{Galaxy rotation curves}

The baryonic rotation velocity is constructed from three components:

\paragraph{Stellar disk.}
The Freeman~(1970) \cite{Freeman1970} exact formula for an exponential
disc of mass $M_\star$ and scale length $R_d$:
\begin{equation}
v_{\rm disc}^2(r) = \frac{G M_\star\, r^2}{2 R_d^3}
  \bigl[I_0(x)\,K_0(x) - I_1(x)\,K_1(x)\bigr],
  \qquad x = \frac{r}{2R_d}\,,
\end{equation}
where $I_n$ and $K_n$ are modified Bessel functions of the first and
second kind.

\paragraph{Bulge.}
The Hernquist~(1990) \cite{Hernquist1990} profile with mass $M_b$ and
scale radius $r_b$:
\begin{equation}
v_{\rm bul}^2(r) = \frac{G M_b\, r}{(r + r_b)^2}\,.
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Gas disc.}
Treated as an independent exponential disk with mass $M_{\rm gas}$
(including a factor 1.33 for He).

\paragraph{ECT total velocity.}
\begin{equation}
v_{\rm ECT}^2(r) = \sqrt{1 + (r/r_0)^2}
  \;\bigl(v_{\rm disc}^2 + v_{\rm gas}^2 + v_{\rm bul}^2\bigr).
\end{equation}

\subsection{Fitting procedure}

The single free parameter $r_0$ is determined by bounded scalar
minimisation (Brent's method) of
\begin{equation}
\chi^2(r_0) = \sum_{i=1}^{N}
  \frac{\bigl(V_{\rm obs}(r_i) - V_{\rm ECT}(r_i;\,r_0)\bigr)^2}
       {\delta V_i^2}\,,
  \qquad r_0 \in [0.01,\,100]\;\text{kpc}.
\end{equation}

The MOND comparison uses the zero-parameter interpolation
function~\eqref{eq:RAR} with
$g^\dagger = 1.2 \times 10^{-10}$\,m\,s$^{-2}$.

\subsection{RG running of $\lambda(\mu)$}

The one-loop $\beta$-function (Section~\ref{sec:running_coupling})
is integrated numerically from $\mu = M_{\rm Pl}$ downward using a
standard adaptive Runge--Kutta method, with boundary condition
$\lambda(M_{\rm Pl}) \approx 10^{-3}$.

\subsection{Figure production}

All figures use publication-quality settings: serif font (Times New
Roman), 9\,pt labels, inward tick marks, 220\,dpi output, with
$\texttt{bbox\_inches='tight'}$.

\paragraph{Regime diagram (Fig.~\ref{fig:regime_diagram}).}
The regime diagram plots the Lorentz-order field
$\phi = \ln(\chi/\chi_{\rm vac})$ against
$\log_{10}(g/g_\dagger)$.
The screening boundary is the locus where the chameleon-like
mass $m_\phi(\rho)$ equals the inverse distance to the
nearest mass source; to the right of this boundary (high $\phi$)
gravity is screened and Newtonian.
Representative astrophysical systems are placed at their
estimated $(\phi,\,g/g_\dagger)$ values:
Solar System ($\phi \approx 2.5$, $g/g_\dagger \sim 10^2$),
spiral disk ($\phi \approx 0.5$, $g/g_\dagger \sim 1$),
void dwarf ($\phi \approx -0.5$, $g/g_\dagger \sim 10^{-1.5}$),
cosmic void ($\phi \approx -1$, $g/g_\dagger \sim 10^{-4}$).
The script \texttt{fig\_regime\_diagram.py} in the code
repository produces this figure.

\section{Derivation of the force-law effective dimensionality}
\label{app:deff_method}

\textit{Status: Level~B (analytic $\phi$-closure for transparency).
This appendix uses the interpolating function
$\mu(x)=x/\sqrt{1+x^2}$ for analytical tractability.
The main observational comparisons in the galactic sector
use the empirical McGaugh~2016 form; the qualitative
$d_{\rm force}$ behaviour is closure-independent.}

\subsection{Definition}

For a gravitational force $g(r)$ obeying
$g \propto 1/r^{d-1}$ in $d$ effective dimensions,
the force-law dimensionality is
\begin{equation}
d_{\rm force}(r) = 1 - \frac{d\ln g_{\rm obs}}{d\ln r}\,.
\label{eq:app_dforce_def}
\end{equation}

\subsection{General derivation from $\phi$-closure}

Starting from
\begin{equation}
\mu(x)\,g_{\rm obs} = g_N(r)\,,
\qquad x \equiv g_{\rm obs}/g_\dagger\,,
\end{equation}
take the logarithmic derivative with respect to $\ln r$:
\begin{equation}
\frac{d\ln g_N}{d\ln r}
= \left(1 + \frac{d\ln\mu}{d\ln x}\right)
  \frac{d\ln g_{\rm obs}}{d\ln r}\,.
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\frac{d\ln g_{\rm obs}}{d\ln r}
= \frac{d\ln g_N/d\ln r}
       {1 + d\ln\mu/d\ln x}\,,
\end{equation}
and hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
d_{\rm force}(r)
= 1 + \frac{p_N(r)}{1 + d\ln\mu/d\ln x}\,,
}
\label{eq:app_dforce_general}
\end{equation}
where $p_N(r) \equiv -d\ln g_N/d\ln r$.

For a point mass, $g_N = GM/r^2$ gives $p_N = 2$.

\subsection{Specific result for $\mu(x) = x/\sqrt{1+x^2}$}

Compute:
\begin{equation}
\ln\mu = \ln x - \tfrac{1}{2}\ln(1+x^2)\,,
\qquad
\frac{d\ln\mu}{d\ln x}
= 1 - \frac{x^2}{1+x^2}
= \frac{1}{1+x^2}\,.
\end{equation}
Substituting into~\eqref{eq:app_dforce_general}:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
d_{\rm force}(x)
= 1 + \frac{2(1+x^2)}{2+x^2}\,.
}
\label{eq:app_dforce_closed}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Limiting cases}

\begin{tabular}{lcll}
\hline
Regime & $x$ & $d_{\rm force}$ & Physics \\
\hline
Screened & $\gg 1$ & $\to 3$ &
  $g \propto 1/r^2$, Newtonian \\
Transition & $= 1$ & $= 7/3 \approx 2.33$ &
  onset of flat rotation \\
Deep $\phi$-branch & $\ll 1$ & $\to 2$ &
  $g \propto 1/r$, $v_{\rm flat} = \mathrm{const}$ \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\medskip
The rotation velocity $v^2 = r\,g \propto r^{2-d_{\rm force}}$:
\begin{itemize}
\item $d_{\rm force} = 3$: $v \propto r^{-1/2}$ (Keplerian),
\item $d_{\rm force} = 7/3$: $v \propto r^{-1/6}$
  (strongly flattened),
\item $d_{\rm force} = 2.5$: $v \propto r^{-1/4}$
  (transition zone),
\item $d_{\rm force} = 2$: $v = \mathrm{const}$
  (flat rotation).
\end{itemize}

\subsection{Transition radius}

The transition $x = 1$ occurs at
\begin{equation}
r_* = \sqrt{\frac{GM}{g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})}}\,.
\end{equation}
Representative values:
$r_*(10^8\,M_\odot) \approx 0.3\,$kpc,
$r_*(5\times10^{10}\,M_\odot) \approx 8\,$kpc,
$r_*(5\times10^{11}\,M_\odot) \approx 24\,$kpc.

\subsection{Distinction from morphological dimensionality}

The force-law dimensionality $d_{\rm force}$ describes
the scaling of the gravitational interaction.
The morphological dimensionality $d_{\rm morph}$
describes the shape of matter distributions
(sheets: $\sim 2$, filaments: $\sim 1$).
They are related through the tidal tensor
$T_{ij} = \partial_i\partial_j\Phi_\phi$:
the number of collapsing eigenvalues of $T_{ij}$
determines $d_{\rm morph} = 3 - N_{\rm collapsed}$.
A quantitative derivation of $d_{\rm morph}$ from
the $\phi$-sector is listed as Open Problem~OP8.

\subsection{Numerical implementation}

Equation~\eqref{eq:app_dforce_closed} is evaluated
analytically.  The mapping $x(r)$ uses the exact
$\phi$-closure solution:
\begin{equation}
g_{\rm obs}^2 =
\frac{g_N^2 + \sqrt{g_N^4 + 4\,g_N^2\,g_\dagger^2}}{2}\,,
\qquad x = g_{\rm obs}/g_\dagger\,.
\end{equation}

The complete Python implementation is available at\\
\url{https://github.com/chufelo/ECT-preprint-code}.



\section{Cluster lensing: 2D projected $\phi$-closure}
\label{app:cluster_lensing}

\textit{Status: Level~B (exploratory algebraic $\phi$-closure).
The calculations below use the quasi-static spherical
$\phi$-branch closure as a proxy for a full cluster-scale
merger simulation. Results are order-of-magnitude estimates;
quantitative cluster-scale conclusions require a 3D
merger-scale $\phi$-solver~(OP22).}

This appendix documents the numerical methods, parameters,
and results for the cluster-merger calculations reported in
Section~\ref{sec:fifth_force}.
All code is available at
\url{https://github.com/chufelo/ECT-preprint-code}:
\texttt{cluster\_phi\_solver\_2d.py} (2D projected thin-lens)
and \texttt{calc\_cluster\_lensing.py} (spherical radial
profile).

A minimal projected cluster solver was constructed to test
the $\phi$-branch \emph{beyond} the single-number
approximation $M_{\rm ECT} \approx \mu_{\rm cl}\,M_{\rm bar}$.
The code constructs a baryonic surface-density map from
compact collisionless peaks and diffuse gas peaks, applies
the local thin-lens closure
$g_N \approx 2\pi G\,\Sigma_b$, and converts it into an
effective convergence map $\kappa(x,y)$ through the same
algebraic $\phi$-branch used in the galactic sector.
This is not yet a full merger-scale metric--$\phi$ solution,
but it already yields two non-trivial results: the
\emph{position} of the lensing peaks and the \emph{order of
magnitude} of the lensing enhancement.

In this formulation, the Bullet Cluster becomes a numerical
near-match problem rather than a simple yes/no argument:
the observed offset morphology is captured qualitatively
by the $\phi$-field response, while the amplitude deficit
remains at the level of a factor $\sim\!2$--$3$ and
therefore still requires additional cluster-scale dynamics
beyond the present closure~(Level~B; OP22).

\subsection{Spherical radial $\phi$-closure}

An NFW-like or $\beta$-model baryonic mass profile
$M_{\rm bar}(<r)$ is used to compute
$g_{\rm bar}(r) = GM_{\rm bar}(<r)/r^2$ at each radius.
The algebraic $\phi$-closure
$\mu(g/g_\dagger)\,g = g_{\rm bar}$ is then solved for
$g_{\rm obs}(r)$, giving the enhancement
$\mu_\phi(r) = g_{\rm obs}/g_{\rm bar}$ and the effective
mass $M_{\rm ECT}(<r) = \mu_\phi(r)\,M_{\rm bar}(<r)$.
For spherical symmetry, this algebraic closure coincides with
the corresponding reduced radial $\phi$-branch equation under
the present closure assumptions (by Gauss's-law analogy;
Level~B). No spatial discretisation is needed at this reduced
level, but the result should be read as a closure-level
approximation rather than as a completed first-principles
cluster solution. This approach is best suited for
\emph{amplitude} estimates with realistic baryon profiles.
Results: Table~\ref{tab:bullet_results}.

\subsection{2D projected thin-lens $\phi$-closure}

For merging clusters the spherical approximation breaks down
because the baryonic mass is distributed among spatially separated
components.  The 2D projected approach decomposes the baryonic
surface density into compact collisionless clumps and diffuse
X-ray gas:
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_b(x,y) = \Sigma_\star(x,y) + \Sigma_{\rm gas}(x,y)\,.
\end{equation}
Each component is represented by a sum of Gaussian peaks:
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_\star(x,y) = \sum_{i=1}^{N_\star}
\frac{M_{\star,i}}{2\pi s_{\star,i}^2}
\exp\!\left[
-\frac{(x-x_{\star,i})^2+(y-y_{\star,i})^2}{2s_{\star,i}^2}
\right],
\end{equation}
and similarly for gas peaks with masses $M_{{\rm gas},j}$
and widths $s_{{\rm gas},j}$.

In thin-lens approximation the projected Newtonian field
is~\cite{Clowe2006}
\begin{equation}
g_N(x,y) \approx 2\pi G\,\Sigma_b(x,y)\,,
\end{equation}
and the same algebraic $\phi$-closure as in the galactic
sector is applied locally:
\begin{equation}
\mu\!\left(\frac{g}{g_\dagger^{\rm cl}}\right)g = g_N\,,
\qquad
\mu(x) = \frac{x}{\sqrt{1+x^2}}\,.
\end{equation}
Solving for the enhancement factor gives
\begin{equation}
\nu(y) \equiv \frac{g}{g_N}
= \sqrt{\frac{1+\sqrt{1+4/y^2}}{2}}\,,
\qquad y = \frac{g_N}{g_\dagger^{\rm cl}}\,.
\label{eq:nu_cluster}
\end{equation}
The effective projected surface density for lensing is
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_{\rm eff}(x,y) = \nu\!\left(\frac{g_N}{g_\dagger^{\rm cl}}\right)
\Sigma_b(x,y)\,,
\end{equation}
and the convergence map is
\begin{equation}
\kappa(x,y) = \frac{\Sigma_{\rm eff}(x,y)}{\Sigma_{\rm crit}}\,.
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Important caveat.}
For spherically symmetric systems this algebraic closure
coincides with the corresponding reduced radial $\phi$-branch
equation under the present closure assumptions
(by Gauss's-law analogy; Level~B); it should be read
as a closure-level approximation throughout.
For a non-spherical merger the thin-lens sheet approximation
$g_N \approx 2\pi G\Sigma_b$ is only a proxy; the full
calculation requires solving
$\nabla\cdot[\mu(|\nabla\Phi|/a_0)\,\nabla\Phi] = 4\pi G\rho_{\rm bar}$
on a 3D grid.
The present results are therefore intermediate between a
single-number global estimate and a full merger-scale
metric--$\phi$ solver (OP22).

\subsection{Cluster parameters}

The parameters below are order-of-magnitude
characterisations consistent with X-ray and lensing
observations.  They should not be interpreted as
precision fits.

\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{lccccl}
\toprule
Cluster & $M_\star$ & $s_\star$ & $M_{\rm gas}$ &
$s_{\rm gas}$ & Offset \\
 & ($M_\odot$) & (kpc) & ($M_\odot$) & (kpc) & (kpc) \\
\midrule
Bullet (2 sub.) & $2\times5\times10^{12}$ & 70 &
  $6\times10^{13}{+}6\times10^{13}$ & 200--250 & 100--150 \\
MACS~J0025 & $2\times3\times10^{12}$ & 60 &
  $2\times2\times10^{13}$ & 250 & 150 \\
El Gordo & $8{+}5\times10^{12}$ & 60--80 &
  $5{+}3\times10^{13}$ & 280--300 & 200 \\
Abell~520 & $2\times3\times10^{12}$ & 80 &
  $3.5\times10^{13}$ (central) & 180 & 0 (gas core) \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

Sources: Bullet --- Paraficz et
al.~\cite{Paraficz2016}, Markevitch et
al.~\cite{Markevitch2004};
MACS~J0025 --- Brada\v{c} et al.~\cite{Bradac2008};
El Gordo --- Diego et al.~\cite{Diego2023};
Abell~520 --- Mahdavi et al.~\cite{Mahdavi2007}.

\subsection{Results}

\paragraph{Offset morphology.}

In all four clusters the $\kappa$-peaks of
$\Sigma_{\rm eff}$ track the component with higher
local surface density.
For Bullet, MACS~J0025, and El~Gordo the lensing
peaks coincide with the compact stellar clumps
($d_{\star\to\kappa} < 25\,$kpc), displaced from the
diffuse gas by $\Delta = 130$--$280\,$kpc.
For Abell~520 the lensing peak coincides with the
dense central gas core, as expected when the gas is
more compact than the stellar distribution.
Both morphologies are natural in ECT because the
$\phi$-field responds to local density contrast, not
to a universal collisionless species.

\paragraph{Total lensing amplitude.}

The integrated effective mass within standard apertures
yields $M_{\rm ECT}/M_{\rm obs} \approx 0.15$--$0.30$
for the 2D Gaussian profiles, and $\approx 0.34$--$0.45$
for the more realistic spherical $\beta$-model
(Table~\ref{tab:bullet_results}).
The range reflects systematic differences in baryonic
modelling, not different physics.
The enhancement factor $\mu_\phi \approx 1.1$--$1.7$
is modest because the thin-lens projected $g_N$ at
cluster-core radii ($R \lesssim 250\,$kpc) places
the system near the screened regime
($g_N/g_\dagger \sim 1$).
At larger radii ($R \gtrsim 500\,$kpc) where
$g_N/g_\dagger < 0.1$ the enhancement rises to
$\mu_\phi \sim 3$--$5$, but less baryonic mass is
enclosed there.

The deficit factor $\sim\!2$--$3$ (using the $\beta$-model) is comparable to
the well-known MOND cluster mass discrepancy
(factor $\sim\!2$).
Whether this can be closed by a full 3D solver,
environmental $g_\dagger$ modulation, or gravitational
slip is an open question (OP22, OP23).

\subsection{Sensitivity to baryonic modelling}

For the Bullet Cluster, the spherical $\beta$-model
gives $M_{\rm ECT}/M_{\rm obs} \approx 0.45$ at $R = 250\,$kpc,
while the 2D Gaussian thin-lens gives $\approx 0.27$.
The difference arises because the $\beta$-model concentrates
more baryonic mass at small radii, producing higher local
$g_{\rm bar}$ and absolute $M_{\rm ECT}$, while the
Gaussian profiles have less total mass within the same aperture.
Both are order-of-magnitude estimates.
The range $M_{\rm ECT}/M_{\rm obs} \approx 0.15$--$0.45$
across approaches and apertures brackets the true answer,
which requires a full 3D merger-scale computation (OP22).

The $\phi$-branch explains approximately one-third to
one-half of the observed lensing mass using the more
realistic $\beta$-model baryon profile.
The deficit factor is $\sim\!2$--$3$,
comparable to the MOND cluster mass discrepancy and
within the expected accuracy of these order-of-magnitude
estimates.


\section{Supplementary numerical calculations}
\label{app:supplementary}

\subsection{$G_N$ in SI}
In the present ECT formulation the observed Newton coupling enters through
geometric EFT matching rather than through a direct algebraic identification
with a single condensate amplitude.
The relevant relation is
\begin{equation}
  G_N \;=\; \frac{c_*^4}{8\pi M_G^2},
\end{equation}
where $M_G$ is the gravitational stiffness scale of the ordered tensor EFT.
At canonical matching one sets $c_*=c$ and identifies
$M_G=\bar M_{\rm Pl}$ observationally.
With $\bar{M}_{\rm Pl}=2.435\times10^{18}\;\mathrm{GeV}/c^2
=4.341\times10^{-9}\;\mathrm{kg}$ this gives
\begin{equation}
G_N \;=\; \frac{\hbar\,c}{8\pi\,\bar{M}_{\rm Pl}^2}
\;=\; \frac{1.055\times10^{-34}\times2.998\times10^{8}}
{8\pi\times(4.341\times10^{-9})^2}
\;\approx\; 6.678\times10^{-11}\;\mathrm{m^3\,kg^{-1}\,s^{-2}},
\end{equation}
in agreement with the CODATA value
$G_N = 6.674\times10^{-11}\;\mathrm{m^3\,kg^{-1}\,s^{-2}}$ up to rounding~($0.06\%$).
This subsection should therefore be read purely as a numerical
illustration of the matching relation, not as a first-principles
microscopic derivation of $G_N$ from the bare condensate action.

\begin{equation}
n_s=1-\frac{2}{N_e}=1-\frac{2}{60}=0.96\overline{6}\approx0.967.
\end{equation}

$1\sigma$ agreement.

quality}
ECT legacy benchmark ($r_0=5.7$ kpc, 1 parameter, superseded):
$\chi^2/N=2.84$.
$\Lambda$CDM/NFW (3 parameters: $M_{\rm vir}$, $c$, $r_s$):
$\chi^2/N=3.51$. MOND (0 parameters): $\chi^2/N=16.48$.

\section{Derivation of Newton's Constant from Action Variation}
% ============================================================
\section{$\phi$-first nonlinear gravity: full derivation}
\label{app:phi_first_EFE}
% ============================================================

This appendix gives the full derivation of the $\phi$-first scalar-tensor
IR closure, states all theorems precisely, and compares the resulting
equations with the analogous equations in related theories.

% -----------------------------------------------------------
\subsection*{A.1 Theorem A: Uniqueness of the quadratic propagator}
% -----------------------------------------------------------

\textbf{Statement.}
In the ordered branch of ECT, the leading quadratic $O(3)$-invariant
symmetric rank-2 kinetic tensor is, up to overall normalisation,
unique:
\begin{equation}
  K^{AB} = \beta\,\delta^{AB} - (\alpha{-}\beta)\,n^An^B.
  \label{eq:K_unique}
\end{equation}
This determines a single effective IR causal cone structure.
Extending this to universal metric coupling beyond the quadratic regime
is assumption~A4 (IR closure assumption; not proved beyond linear order).

\textbf{Proof.}
Any $O(3)$-invariant symmetric rank-2 tensor built from
$\{\delta^{AB}, n^A\}$ has the form $T^{AB}=a\,\delta^{AB}+b\,n^An^B$
with two scalars $a,b$. From $S_E$: $a=\beta$, $b=-(\alpha{-}\beta)$.
No other independent structure exists. $\square$

% -----------------------------------------------------------
\subsection*{A.2 Theorem B: $\phi$-parameterisation}
% -----------------------------------------------------------

Let $\chi(X)$ be the local Lorentz-order parameter of the ordered branch.
Its vacuum value $\chi_\infty$ is matched to
$(\alpha{-}\beta)$ in the homogeneous vacuum sector.
Define $\phi\equiv\ln(\chi/\chi_\infty)$,
$\bar{M}^2_{\rm Pl}\equiv v_0^2\chi_\infty$.
Since $M^2_{\rm eff}\propto v_0^2\chi$:
\begin{equation}
  M^2_{\rm eff}(\phi) = \bar{M}^2_{\rm Pl}\,e^\phi.
\end{equation}
This is an exact algebraic reparameterisation. $\square$

% -----------------------------------------------------------
\subsection*{A.3 Theorem C: Correct IR action (effective ansatz)}
% -----------------------------------------------------------

$S_{\rm IR}$ (eq.~\eqref{eq:phi_first_action} in the main text) is the minimal
local two-derivative IR ansatz consistent with A1--A4.
It is not derived from $S_E$ without additional assumptions.
The potential $U(\phi)$ is an effective ordered-branch potential;
its quadratic coefficient $m_\phi^2$ is fixed by the stiffness mass
of the $\chi$-field; higher coefficients require loop calculations.

% -----------------------------------------------------------
\subsection*{A.4 Theorem D: Correct field equations}
% -----------------------------------------------------------

Variation of $S_{\rm IR}$ gives the self-consistent system
(eqs.~\eqref{eq:gen_EE}--\eqref{eq:phi_eom} in the main text).
Note that the \emph{metric} equation contains the non-minimal terms
$\nabla_\mu\nabla_\nu M^2_{\rm eff} - g_{\mu\nu}\Box M^2_{\rm eff}$
arising from $\delta(M^2_{\rm eff}(\phi)R)/\delta g^{\mu\nu}$;
these are absent in standard GR and are characteristic of the
$\phi$-first scalar-tensor closure.

% -----------------------------------------------------------
\subsection*{A.5 Corollary E: Einstein limit}
% -----------------------------------------------------------

In the homogeneous screened regime
$\phi=\phi_0=\mathrm{const}$, $n^A=\bar{n}^A=\mathrm{const}$:
\begin{equation}
  \nabla_\mu M^2_{\rm eff}=0,\quad
  \Box M^2_{\rm eff}=0,\quad
  T^{(\phi)}_{\mu\nu}\to 0\ (\phi\ \text{constant}),
\end{equation}
while the vacuum contribution of the scalar sector is carried by
$-U(\phi_0)g_{\mu\nu}$ already present in eq.~\eqref{eq:gen_EE}
(no double counting). The metric equation reduces to:
\begin{equation}
  G_{\mu\nu} + \Lambda_{\rm eff}(\phi_0)\,g_{\mu\nu}
  = 8\pi G_{\rm eff}(\phi_0)\,T^{\rm mat}_{\mu\nu}
  \label{eq:Einstein_limit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
  G_{\rm eff}(\phi_0) = \frac{G_N}{e^{\phi_0}},\qquad
  \Lambda_{\rm eff}(\phi_0)
  = \frac{U(\phi_0)+\rho_{n,{\rm vac}}(\phi_0)}{M^2_{\rm eff}(\phi_0)}.
\end{equation}
This is a strict result given A1--A4. $\square$

\textit{Note.} This subsection does not constitute a derivation of
the galactic / MOND-like branch, which requires additional assumptions
about non-homogeneous $\phi$-sector solutions
(Section~\ref{sec:mp_galactic}).

% -----------------------------------------------------------
\subsection*{A.6 Theorem F: Lovelock uniqueness of the pure-metric IR limit}
% -----------------------------------------------------------

\textbf{Additional assumption A5.}
$\phi$ and $n^A$ are frozen or integrated out; the remaining
pure-metric IR theory is local, diffeomorphism-invariant, and
two-derivative at leading order in 4D.

\textbf{Lovelock theorem (1971)~\cite{Lovelock1971}.}
Under A5, the leading pure-metric two-derivative IR field equations
are uniquely of Einstein form:
\begin{equation}
  G_{\mu\nu} + \Lambda\,g_{\mu\nu} = 8\pi G\,T_{\mu\nu}.
  \label{eq:Lovelock_EFE}
\end{equation}
\textit{Limitations.} After integrating out $\phi$ and $n^A$,
corrections $\sim R^2,\,R_{\mu\nu}R^{\mu\nu}$ are generated
but suppressed as $(E/m_\varphi)^2$ in the IR.
Theorem~F is a statement about leading IR uniqueness,
not a completed microscopic derivation from $S_E$. $\square$

% -----------------------------------------------------------
\subsection*{A.7 Comparison with related theories}
% -----------------------------------------------------------

Table~\ref{tab:phi_first_comparison} places the ECT $\phi$-first
closure in context with Einstein-aether theory, scalar-tensor gravity,
and standard GR.

\begin{table}[H]
\centering
\caption{ECT $\phi$-first IR closure compared to related theories.
$\phi$ = local stiffness/Lorentz-order field;
$n^A$ = orientation director;
$G_{\rm eff}$ = effective gravitational coupling.
Entries in \textbf{bold} indicate ECT-specific features.}
\label{tab:phi_first_comparison}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.35}
\begin{tabular}{@{}p{3.2cm}p{3.0cm}p{3.0cm}p{3.0cm}p{3.0cm}@{}}
\toprule
Feature & GR & Brans-Dicke / ST & Einstein-aether & ECT ($\phi$-first) \\

  \textbf{$\phi$ (order field); $g^{\rm eff}$ emergent} \\

  \textbf{$G_N e^{-\phi(X)}$ from condensate} \\

  \textbf{yes ($n^A$, from SSB)} \\

  \textbf{$O(4)\to O(3)$ SSB} \\
