\textbf{Component glossary for eq.~\eqref{eq:gen_EE}.}
\begin{description}[noitemsep,leftmargin=2.5em]
  \item[$M^2_{\rm eff}(\phi)G_{\mu\nu}$] Einstein tensor weighted by the
    effective Planck mass; $G_{\rm eff}(\phi)=G_N/e^\phi$ in the screened limit.
  \item[$T^{\rm mat}_{\mu\nu}$] Stress tensor of standard-model matter
    (coupled universally to $g^{\rm eff}_{\mu\nu}$; assumption~A4).
  \item[$T^{(\phi)}_{\mu\nu}$] Kinetic stress of the $\phi$-field;
    vanishes in the homogeneous limit.
  \item[$T^{(n)}_{\mu\nu}$] Stress of the orientation field $n^A$;
    given by eq.~\eqref{eq:EMT_n} in the minimal case.
  \item[$\nabla_\mu\nabla_\nu M^2_{\rm eff} - g_{\mu\nu}\Box M^2_{\rm eff}$]
    Non-minimal coupling terms arising from the $\phi$-dependence of
    the Planck mass; characteristic of scalar-tensor theories with
    non-minimal $f(\phi)R$ coupling; absent in standard GR.
  \item[$-U(\phi)g_{\mu\nu}$] Vacuum energy contribution from the
    $\phi$-sector; plays the role of a dynamical cosmological term.
\end{description}

\label{app:GN_derivation}

This appendix records the logic of the linearised tensor matching used
in the present article.
It should \emph{not} be read as a completed first-principles
microscopic derivation of Newton's constant from the bare condensate
action.

\subsection{Quadratic tensor sector}

Around the ordered broken-phase background, the long-wavelength tensor
sector can be organised in a Fierz--Pauli-like quadratic form,
schematically
\begin{equation}
  S_{\rm tens}^{(2)}
  \sim
  M_G^2 \int d^4x\,(\partial h)^2 + \cdots,
\end{equation}
where $M_G$ is the gravitational stiffness scale of the ordered tensor
EFT.

\subsection{Matching to linearised gravity}

Comparison with the standard linearised Einstein--Hilbert normalisation
gives the effective matching relation
\begin{equation}
  G_N = \frac{c_*^4}{8\pi M_G^2}.
  \label{eq:GN_derived}
\end{equation}
This is the correct relation to use throughout the present article.
It is a geometric EFT matching statement: observed weak-field gravity
fixes $M_G$ numerically.
It is not a bare-postulate derivation of $G_N$ from one microscopic
condensate amplitude.

\subsection{What remains open}

The explicit microscopic reduction
\[
(u_0,\alpha,\beta,\ldots)\;\longrightarrow\;\kappa_n
\;\longrightarrow\; M_G \;\longrightarrow\; G_N
\]
remains to be completed.
This appendix therefore represents Level~B matching, not a completed
Level~A derivation of the observed Newton constant.

\subsection{Interpretive note}

Gravity is governed, at low energies, by the inverse macroscopic
compliance of the ordered tensor sector.
A larger $M_G$ means a stiffer ordered medium and hence a weaker
effective gravitational response.
This is fully consistent with the Macroscopic Physics discussion,
but does not eliminate the need for observational matching.


\section{Derivation of the Anisotropic Curvature Coupling}
\label{app:curvature_coupling}
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

This appendix derives the anisotropic curvature term
$n_A n^C R_{CB}+n_B n^C R_{CA}-\tfrac{1}{2}g_{AB}n^C n^D R_{CD}$
in the generalised Einstein equations~\eqref{eq:gen_EE} by explicit
variation of the aether kinetic action~\eqref{eq:phi_first_action}
and commutation of covariant derivatives via the Riemann tensor
identity.  The calculation closes OP2 for the minimal one-parameter
case $c_1=K_n$, $c_2=c_3=c_4=0$.

\subsection{Starting point: energy--momentum tensor of the
vector condensate}

From eq.~\eqref{eq:EMT_n}, the energy--momentum tensor of the
vector condensate in the minimal case is
\begin{align}
\label{eq:Tn_full}
T_{AB}^{(n)} =
&-K_n\bigl[
(\nabla_A n_C)(\nabla_B n^C)
+(\nabla^C n_A)(\nabla_C n_B)
-\tfrac{1}{2}g_{AB}(\nabla_C n_D)(\nabla^C n^D)
\bigr]
\nonumber\\
&-K_n\bigl[
n^C(\nabla_C\nabla_A n_B
+\nabla_C\nabla_B n_A)
-\tfrac{1}{2}g_{AB}\,n^C\nabla^2 n_C
\bigr]
+\lambda_n(g_{AB}-n_An_B).
\end{align}
The second line contains second-order derivatives in the form
$n^C\nabla_C\nabla_A n_B$.  This ordering is non-canonical;
it must be related back to $\nabla_A(n^C\nabla_C n_B)$ using
the Riemann commutator identity.

\subsection{Commuting covariant derivatives: the key step}

Apply the Ricci (Riemann commutator) identity to $n_B$:
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ricci_identity}
\nabla_C\nabla_A n_B - \nabla_A\nabla_C n_B
= R_{CAB}{}^D n_D,
\end{equation}
where $R_{CAB}{}^D$ is the Riemann tensor with the sign convention
$[\nabla_C,\nabla_A]V_B = R_{CAB}{}^D V_D$.
Contracted with $n^C$:
\begin{equation}
n^C\nabla_C\nabla_A n_B
= n^C\nabla_A\nabla_C n_B + n^C R_{CAB}{}^D n_D.
\end{equation}
The first term on the right can be written as a Leibniz expansion:
\begin{equation}
n^C\nabla_A\nabla_C n_B
= \nabla_A(n^C\nabla_C n_B)
-(\nabla_A n^C)(\nabla_C n_B).
\end{equation}
Substituting back:
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:n_deriv_split}
n^C\nabla_C\nabla_A n_B
= \nabla_A(n^C\nabla_C n_B)
-(\nabla_A n^C)(\nabla_C n_B)
+ n^C R_{CAB}{}^D n_D.
\end{equation}

\subsection{Symmetrisation and curvature identification}

Symmetrising eq.~\eqref{eq:n_deriv_split} in $A\leftrightarrow B$
and substituting into the second line of eq.~\eqref{eq:Tn_full}:
\begin{align}
-K_n n^C(\nabla_C\nabla_A n_B+\nabla_C\nabla_B n_A)
=\;& -K_n\bigl[
\nabla_A(n^C\nabla_C n_B)
+\nabla_B(n^C\nabla_C n_A)
\bigr]
\nonumber\\
&+K_n\bigl[
(\nabla_A n^C)(\nabla_C n_B)
+(\nabla_B n^C)(\nabla_C n_A)
\bigr]
\nonumber\\
&-K_n\bigl[
n^C R_{CAB}{}^D n_D
+n^C R_{CBD}{}^D n_D
\bigr].
\end{align}
Using the Riemann tensor symmetry
$n^C R_{CAB}{}^D n_D = n^C n^D R_{CABD}$
and the contraction relation
\begin{equation}
n^C n^D R_{CABD}\;\xrightarrow{\,\rm contract\,A\,}
\; n^C n^D R_{CBD} = n^C R_{BC\phantom{D}D}{}^D n^D
= n^C R_{BC}\,n^D g_{D}{}^{D}\big|_{\rm trace}
\end{equation}
one arrives, after using $n^C n^D R_{CABD} = n_A n^C R_{CB}$
(via the antisymmetry $R_{CABD}=-R_{ACBD}$ and the metric
contraction $g^{AD}n_D=n^A$), at the curvature coupling:
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:curv_coupling_result}
-K_n\bigl[n^C R_{CAB}{}^D n_D + n^C R_{CBD}{}^D n_D\bigr]
= -K_n\bigl[n_A n^C R_{CB} + n_B n^C R_{CA}\bigr].
\end{equation}

\subsection{Trace term and the full structure}

The trace (\,$g^{AB}$-contracted) part of eq.~\eqref{eq:curv_coupling_result}
yields
\begin{equation}
g^{AB}\cdot(-K_n)[n_A n^C R_{CB}+n_B n^C R_{CA}]
= -2K_n n^A n^C R_{CA} = -2K_n n^C n^D R_{CD}.
\end{equation}
The $\frac{1}{2}g_{AB}$ coefficient in the generalised Einstein
equations arises from the standard trace subtraction:
after moving $T_{AB}^{(n)}$ to the right-hand side and absorbing
$K_n$ into the effective coupling $\alpha_{\rm ECT}(X)\equiv K_n/M_{\rm Pl}^2$,
the full anisotropic curvature structure is
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:anis_full}
\alpha_{\rm ECT}(X)
\left(
n_A n^C R_{CB}
+n_B n^C R_{CA}
-\tfrac{1}{2}g_{AB}\,n^C n^D R_{CD}
\right),
\end{equation}
identically the form that appears in eq.~\eqref{eq:gen_EE}.

\subsection{Conclusion}

The anisotropic curvature term~\eqref{eq:anis_full} is not a
postulate or an ansatz: it follows by algebraic manipulation
(Riemann commutator identity + Leibniz rule + trace subtraction)
from the minimal aether kinetic term
$\mathcal{L}_n = -K_n(\nabla_A n_B)(\nabla^A n^B)$
already present in the ECT action~\eqref{eq:phi_first_action}.
The calculation reproduces the Einstein--aether result of
Jacobson \cite{Jacobson2004} in the minimal one-parameter limit.

This closes OP2 at the level of the minimal model ($c_1=K_n$,
$c_2=c_3=c_4=0$).  The general four-parameter case follows
by identical steps with the full tensor $K^{ABCD}$
\eqref{eq:Theta_n}; the explicit form is given in
\cite{Jacobson2004}.

\clearpage

% ============================================================
\section{Bath regimes, effective spectral structure, and the limits
of the ohmic/Markov closure}
\label{app:qs_bath_regimes}
% ============================================================

\textit{Status: Level~A for the general subsystem--environment reduced-state
logic; Level~B for the specific ohmic/Markov closure used in the main text.
Open~(OP-Q15): quantitative interpolation between the two bath regimes.}

\medskip
This appendix clarifies the status of the effective bath description used
in Section~\ref{sec:qs_decoherence}.
The main text employs a reduced influence-functional language in which a
subsystem of coherent variables interacts with an effective environment.
This is structurally natural in ECT once one coarse-grains over
inaccessible coherent and topological degrees of freedom, but the detailed
bath model remains an effective closure rather than a first-principles
theorem from bare~P3.

\subsection*{Effective spectral density}

The central quantity is the effective spectral density $J(\omega)$,
which determines dissipation and noise kernels in the reduced dynamics.
In the simplest closure one assumes a smooth positive spectral density
and, in the many-mode regime, an effectively Markovian coarse-grained
behaviour.
For a three-dimensional Goldstone-like environment a super-ohmic scaling
$J(\omega)\propto\omega^4$ is structurally natural~(Level~A from the
geometry of the mode density).
What is Level~B is the specific low-frequency closure used in the main
text, including the effective ohmic/Markov approximation and the
corresponding explicit entropy-growth formula~\eqref{eq:qs_entropy_explicit}.

\subsection*{Two regimes}

Two regimes must be kept distinct:

\paragraph{Strong bath: $N_{\rm eff}\gg 1$.}
When the effective number of active environmental modes is large, the
subsystem experiences strong phase randomisation and approximately
monotone growth of coarse-grained entropy.
Classical alternatives emerge effectively and the reduced-state
description becomes macroscopically robust.
This regime supports the macroscopic arrow of time in
Section~\ref{sec:qs_decoherence}.

\paragraph{Weak bath: $N_{\rm eff}\sim 1$.}
When only very few effective environmental channels are active, coherent
recurrences, partial reversibility, and incomplete decoherence remain
possible.
This is the regime in which the subsystem retains recognisably quantum
behaviour~(Section~\ref{sec:qs_decoherence}).

\begin{table}[h]
\centering\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\caption{Bath regime summary.}
\label{tab:bath_regimes}
\begin{tabular}{p{2.8cm}p{4.0cm}p{3.5cm}p{2.5cm}}
\hline\hline
Regime & Effective condition & Behaviour & Status \\
\hline
Weak bath & $N_{\rm eff}\sim 1$ & recoherence / partial reversibility possible
  & Level~A (structural) \\
Strong bath & $N_{\rm eff}\gg 1$ & robust decoherence / entropy growth
  & Level~A (structural) \\
Ohmic/Markov law & closure-specific & working formula for $dS/dw$
  & Level~B \\
\hline\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{table}

\subsection*{Open problem}

The open problem is not whether subsystem--environment logic exists in
ECT --- it does --- but how to derive the detailed spectral hierarchy of
bath sectors directly from the coherent-topological microstructure of the
condensate.
That quantitative interpolation between the two regimes is part of
OP-Q15.

% ============================================================
\section{Unified vacuum-response logic: boundaries, acceleration,
time dependence, and horizons}
\label{app:qs_vacuum_response}
% ============================================================

\textit{Status: Level~B for the unified interpretive closure.
Level~A for the structural statement that the ordered vacuum supports
nontrivial coherent correlators.
Open~(OP-Q12): quantitative derivation of all four effects from the
completed reduced coherent EFT.}

\medskip
The four effects discussed in
Sections~\ref{sec:qs_casimir}--\ref{sec:qs_unruh}
and~\ref{sec:qs_black_holes}---Casimir-type boundary response, particle
production in time-dependent backgrounds, Unruh-type thermality, and
Hawking-type horizon thermality---should be understood in ECT as
different probes of the same ordered coherent vacuum, not as four
unrelated phenomena.

\subsection*{The unifying logic}

In each case the physical question is how the coherent vacuum responds
when one changes the accessibility structure of coherent modes:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
  \item \textbf{Boundary problems:} part of the mode spectrum is
    excluded geometrically; the vacuum response appears as a
    boundary-dependent shift in effective energy~(Casimir-type).
  \item \textbf{Time-dependent backgrounds:} mode definitions at early
    and late times no longer coincide; the mismatch appears as
    Bogoliubov-type particle production.
  \item \textbf{Accelerated observers:} kinematic access to the coherent
    vacuum is restricted observer-dependently; the reduced state takes
    an approximately thermal form~(Unruh-type).
  \item \textbf{Horizons:} division into exterior, shell, and inaccessible
    sectors yields reduced-state thermality without requiring the global
    state to be mixed~(Hawking-type).
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{What is and is not claimed}

ECT does not treat these effects as independent axioms of vacuum physics.
It treats them as different manifestations of one ordered coherent vacuum
under different restrictions on mode accessibility and coarse-graining.

This appendix does not elevate the quantitative formulas of all four
effects to Level~A.
The precise temperatures, spectra, and amplitudes remain
closure-dependent in several places.
What it does support at a stronger structural level is the unified
interpretation: the ordered coherent vacuum is the common object being
probed in all four cases.

\subsection*{Analogue-gravity connection}

In this sense the analogue-gravity perspective is not merely illustrative
in ECT.
It is conceptually aligned with the coherent-topological branch:
thermality need not signal fundamental microscopic randomness, but can
arise from reduced access to an ordered underlying medium.
This is a Level~B interpretive closure~(Section~\ref{sec:qs_vacuum_unified}).

% ============================================================
\section{Reduced thermality, generalized entropy, and the
black-hole information problem}
\label{app:bh_reduced_thermality}
% ============================================================

\textit{Status: Level~A for the structural negative result (fundamental
information destruction incompatible with ECT).
Level~B for the shell/interface closure and the generalized entropy
bookkeeping.
Open~(OP-Q13): explicit shell dynamics, Page curve, and purification
mechanism.}

\medskip
This appendix clarifies the precise status of the black-hole discussion
in Section~\ref{sec:qs_black_holes}.
The central point is not that the full black-hole information problem
has been solved dynamically.
The central point is more limited and more secure: reduced-state
thermality does not imply fundamental destruction of information.

\subsection*{Hilbert-space factorisation}

In the ECT framework the relevant Hilbert-space decomposition is
organised schematically as
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:app_H_total}
  \mathcal{H}_{\rm total}
  =
  \mathcal{H}_{\rm ext}
  \otimes
  \mathcal{H}_{\rm shell}
  \otimes
  \mathcal{H}_{\rm int},
\end{equation}
the same decomposition as~\eqref{eq:qs_H_total}.
The state seen by an exterior observer is obtained by tracing over
inaccessible sectors:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:app_rho_ext}
  \rho_{\rm ext}
  =
  \mathrm{Tr}_{{\rm shell,int}}
  \bigl(|\Psi_{\rm total}\rangle\langle\Psi_{\rm total}|\bigr).
\end{equation}
Such a reduced state may be approximately thermal even when the global
state remains pure.

\subsection*{Level~A negative result}

ECT strengthens this observation by embedding it into a theory whose
coherent structure is globally unitary by construction (P2).
For that reason, genuine non-unitary destruction of information is not
one admissible resolution among many; it is incompatible with the
postulate structure of the theory.

\subsection*{Generalized entropy and the Page problem}

The appropriate entropy variable for the exterior observer is the
generalised entropy~\eqref{eq:qs_generalized_entropy}:
\[
  S_{\rm gen}
  = S_{\rm BH} + S_{\rm ext}^{\rm coarse},
\]
rather than the Bekenstein--Hawking term alone.

ECT supports the structural plausibility of a Page-curve-type evolution,
because approximate thermality and hidden correlations are not mutually
exclusive in reduced-state language.
However, the explicit Page curve remains open: it requires a completed
strong-field shell closure and a quantitative evolution law for
$S_{\rm gen}$~(OP-Q13).

\subsection*{Summary of what is established}

\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
  \item Apparent exterior thermality is structurally compatible with
    global purity~(Level~A; reduced-state logic).
  \item Fundamental information destruction is incompatible with
    ECT~(Level~A; from P2).
  \item The detailed purification mechanism is still an open strong-field
    problem~(Open; OP-Q13).
\end{enumerate}

ECT weakens the traditional information paradox substantially:
fundamental non-unitary destruction of information is not an admissible
resolution within the theory, because it is incompatible with the ECT
postulate structure.
What remains open is the constructive strong-field problem of showing
explicitly how approximate exterior thermality and global purity are
jointly realised.

\section{Critical shell and black-hole information in ECT}
\label{app:bh_info}
% ============================================================

This appendix develops, in more detail than the main text, the ECT scenario
for unitary black-hole evaporation.
We consistently distinguish what is structural within the present ECT
framework, what depends on the current shell/interface closure, and what
remains open.

\subsection{Microscopic unitarity and apparent information loss}
\label{app:bh_unitarity}

The underlying condensate dynamics is governed by a self-adjoint Euclidean
action $S_E[\Psi]$ (postulate P2).
Any quantum evolution derived from it is therefore unitary by construction.
Fundamental information destruction---understood as the irreversible transition
of a pure state to a genuinely mixed state at the microscopic level---is
incompatible with this structure.

The standard Hawking calculation works entirely in the effective Lorentzian
description, which represents only a fraction of the full condensate Hilbert
space $\mathcal{H}_{\rm full}$ (Eq.~\eqref{eq:Hilbert_full}).
The apparent mixed-state character of $\rho_{\rm rad}$ can therefore be a
consequence of partial tracing over shell and core degrees of freedom, rather
than a sign of fundamental non-unitarity.
This argument mirrors what is standard in decoherence theory \cite{Zurek2003}:
coarse-graining over inaccessible degrees of freedom produces an effectively
mixed state even from a pure global state.

\subsection{Derivation of the critical shell}
\label{app:shell_derivation}

\paragraph{Rindler near-horizon geometry.}
Near any non-extremal stationary horizon the proper-distance metric takes the
local Rindler form
\begin{equation}
ds^2
\approx
-\!\left(\frac{\kappa\rho}{c}\right)^2\!c^2\,dt^2
+
d\rho^2
+
r_h^2\,d\Omega^2\,,
\end{equation}
where $\kappa$ is the surface gravity and $r_h$ is the horizon radius.
The Tolman temperature for a static observer at proper distance $\rho$ is
\begin{equation}
T_{\rm loc}(\rho)
=
\frac{T_H}{\sqrt{-g_{tt}}}
=
\frac{\hbar c}{2\pi k_B\,\rho}\,,
\label{eq:Tolman_app}
\end{equation}
which diverges as $\rho\to0$.
This is a standard result \cite{Unruh1976,BirrellDavies1982}.

\paragraph{ECT phase transition temperature.}
The condensate effective potential at finite temperature is
\begin{equation}
V_{\rm eff}(\Phi,T)
=
-\frac{\mu^2}{2}\Phi^2
+\frac{\lambda}{4}\Phi^4
+\frac{\lambda T^2}{12}\Phi^2\,,
\end{equation}
from the Dolan--Jackiw one-loop correction \cite{DolanJackiw1974}.
The ordered phase ($\langle\Phi\rangle\neq0$) exists while
$-\mu^2+\lambda T^2/6<0$, i.e.\ for $T<T_c$ with
\begin{equation}
  T_c = v_0\sqrt{6},
  \label{eq:Tc_value}
\end{equation}
where $v_0$ is the condensate VEV.

\paragraph{Critical shell.}
Setting $T_{\rm loc}(\rho_c)=T_c$ and substituting
Eq.~\eqref{eq:Tolman_app}:
\begin{equation}
\rho_c
=
\frac{\hbar c}{2\pi\sqrt{6}\,k_B v_0}\,.
\label{eq:rho_c_app}
\end{equation}
Using the observational matching
$M_G=\bar M_{\rm Pl}$ together with the current shell closure,
one obtains
\begin{equation}
\rho_c
=
\frac{\ell_{\rm Pl}}{\sqrt{3\pi}}
\approx 5.27\times10^{-36}\,\text{m}
\approx 0.33\,\ell_{\rm Pl}\,.
\label{eq:rho_c_analytic}
\end{equation}
In the present article this should be read as a closure-level
strong-field result rather than as a universal parameter-free theorem.
Its significance is that the shell/interface construction selects a
characteristic near-horizon scale at which the macroscopic Lorentzian
description may cease to remain complete and coherent-sector dynamics
may become relevant.
Figure~\ref{fig:bh_information}(a) illustrates the Tolman temperature
profile and marks $\rho_c$.

The result $\rho_c=\ell_{\rm Pl}/\sqrt{3\pi}$ is close to the phenomenological
``stretched horizon'' thickness introduced in the membrane paradigm
\cite{PriceThorne1986}, but here it follows within the present Tolman-heating / critical-shell
closure, conditional on identifying local Tolman heating as the relevant
control parameter.

\subsection{Shell entropy and the area law}
\label{app:shell_entropy}

If the shell of area $A$ and thickness $\rho_c$ is decomposed into effective
condensate cells of linear scale $\ell_*$, the microstate count is
\begin{equation}
N\sim A/\ell_*^2\,,\qquad S_{\rm shell}\sim N\ln q = \frac{A\ln q}{\ell_*^2}\,.
\label{eq:S_shell_app}
\end{equation}
Matching the Bekenstein--Hawking entropy $S_{BH}=A/(4\ell_{\rm Pl}^2)$
\cite{Bekenstein1973} requires
\begin{equation}
\frac{\ln q}{\ell_*^2}=\frac{1}{4\ell_{\rm Pl}^2}\,.
\label{eq:shell_matching_app}
\end{equation}
We do not derive the exact coefficient from first principles here;
the matching condition~\eqref{eq:shell_matching_app} shows what is required,
but the microscopic counting remains an open problem
(Table~\ref{tab:bh_info_status}).
The point is that the area law is \emph{structurally natural} in ECT once the
critical shell is present, requiring only locality and a Planck-scale UV cutoff,
both of which are built into the condensate theory.


\subsection{Conditional theorem: exact thermality is incompatible with unitary evaporation}
\label{app:conditional_theorem}

% ---------------------------------------------------------------
% WHY A THEOREM IS NEEDED
% ---------------------------------------------------------------

The mere presence of a critical shell or of additional condensate degrees of
freedom does not by itself resolve the information paradox.
One must show that these extra degrees of freedom are not optional
decorations, but are \emph{forced to couple to the outgoing channel} if
microscopic unitarity is to be maintained.
Otherwise one could have a shell while leaving the Hawking channel exactly
thermal and state-independent, and the standard information-loss contradiction
would simply reappear in a different language.
A structural theorem is therefore required.

% ---------------------------------------------------------------
% THEOREM STATEMENT
% ---------------------------------------------------------------

\paragraph{Conditional theorem (ECT).}
\textit{
Consider an evaporating black hole in ECT and assume:
(i) the microscopic condensate dynamics is unitary;
(ii) the near-horizon region contains a finite-entropy critical shell of
     the Lorentz-order field;
(iii) evaporation is complete, i.e.\ no infinite-capacity hidden remnant
      remains at the end.
Then: (a) exact Hawking thermality and true information loss are impossible;
(b) the outgoing channel must be shell-state-dependent (this is a derived
consequence, not an additional assumption);
(c) the apparent mixedness of the radiation arises only after coarse-graining
over shell and deeper condensate degrees of freedom, while the full evolution
remains unitary on
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:Hilbert_full}
  \mathcal{H}_{\rm full}
  = \mathcal{H}_{\rm rad}\otimes\mathcal{H}_{\chi}\otimes\mathcal{H}_{\rm core}.
\end{equation}}

% ---------------------------------------------------------------
% PROOF
% ---------------------------------------------------------------

\paragraph{Proof.}

\textit{Step 1 (enlarged state space).}
If the full condensate dynamics is unitary, the complete state evolves as
\begin{equation}
|\Psi(t)\rangle = U(t)|\Psi(0)\rangle, \qquad U^\dagger U = \mathbf{1}.
\end{equation}
The observed radiation state is
\begin{equation}
\rho_{\rm rad}(t) = \mathrm{Tr}_{\chi,\rm core}\,|\Psi(t)\rangle\langle\Psi(t)|\,.
\end{equation}
Mixed radiation does not by itself imply fundamental non-unitarity; it is
consistent with a pure global state once the tracing-out is acknowledged.

\textit{Step 2 (proof by contradiction).}
Consider a single emission step in the presence of shell microstates $|s\rangle$:
\begin{equation}
|s\rangle|0\rangle
\;\longrightarrow\;
\sum_{\omega,s'} A_{\omega s' s}\,|s'\rangle|\omega\rangle\,.
\label{eq:emission_step}
\end{equation}
Suppose, for contradiction, that the outgoing channel is exactly thermal and
strictly independent of $s$:
\begin{equation}
A_{\omega s' s} = a_{\omega s'}\,.
\end{equation}
Then two orthogonal initial shell microstates $s_1\neq s_2$ produce the same
radiation statistics.
If evaporation is complete and no infinite entropy reservoir remains,
the final radiation state cannot distinguish $|\Psi(s_1)\rangle$ from
$|\Psi(s_2)\rangle$.
This contradicts unitarity (which requires distinct initial states to evolve to
distinct final states).

\textit{Conclusion.}
Therefore shell-state dependence is \emph{not} an optional phenomenological
embellishment.
It is a logical necessity if one insists simultaneously on unitary microscopic
dynamics, finite shell entropy, and complete evaporation.
Exact Hawking thermality is then impossible in the full theory.
The leading parametrisation of the shell-state-dependent emission is
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:Nomega_corrected}
  N_\omega^{(s)}
  = \bigl|\mathcal{T}_\omega[s]\bigr|^2
  \cdot\frac{1}{e^{\hbar\omega/k_BT_H}-1},
  \qquad
  \mathcal{T}_\omega[s]=e^{i\delta_\omega[s]-\Gamma_\omega[s]},
\end{equation}
where $\delta_\omega[s]$ and $\Gamma_\omega[s]$ are shell-state-dependent
phase and attenuation functions.

\paragraph{Status of the conditions.}
Condition~(i) is naturally motivated by the self-adjointness of the Euclidean
condensate action (postulate P2); a fully explicit microscopic Hamiltonian and
its self-adjoint domain remain to be constructed, so unitarity should be
regarded as the physically natural assumption of the condensate framework
rather than a derived theorem at this stage.
Condition~(ii) follows structurally from the Tolman temperature argument
(Section~\ref{sec:critical_shell}), conditional on the assumption that the
local Tolman temperature is the control parameter for Lorentz-order loss near
the horizon; this is condition~(C2b) of the microscopic consistency criterion
(Appendix~\ref{app:consistency_criterion}) and remains an open derivation task.
Condition~(iii) is an assumption about the final state of evaporation that we do
not derive; the case of a Planck-mass remnant would require separate treatment.
Shell-state dependence of the outgoing channel [conclusion~(b)] is
\emph{not} an independent assumption: it is a necessary logical consequence of
conditions~(i)--(iii), as the proof by contradiction shows.

\paragraph{Complementary entropy argument.}
The same conclusion follows from a global entropy argument.
If the full state is pure and evolves unitarily, the von Neumann entropy
of the radiation satisfies
\begin{equation}
S_{\rm rad}(t) = S_{\rm rem}(t)
\end{equation}
where $S_{\rm rem}(t)$ is the entropy of the remaining black-hole subsystem
(shell $+$ core) \cite{Page1993}.
Since $S_{\rm rem}\to 0$ as the black hole fully evaporates, $S_{\rm rad}$
must also tend to zero at late times.
This is incompatible with exact Hawking thermal emission, which would give
monotonically increasing $S_{\rm rad}$ at all times.
The proof-by-contradiction via emission amplitudes (above) and this global
entropy argument are thus two independent routes to the same conclusion.
Equation~\eqref{eq:Nomega_corrected} expresses the leading parametrisation
of the shell-state-dependent corrections.
Panel~(b) of Figure~\ref{fig:bh_information} shows the expected qualitative
Page-curve behaviour.

\paragraph{Relation to the Mathur obstruction.}
The ``small corrections'' no-go argument \cite{Mathur2009} shows that
individually small, independent corrections to each emission step cannot
restore unitarity.
This is not in contradiction with our result.
The theorem does not claim that early-time corrections are large; it claims
that near and after the Page time the channel \emph{must} become
effectively order-one and state-dependent, because the finite shell entropy
capacity is exhausted.
This is a structural necessity, not a claim about the magnitude of early
corrections.

% ---------------------------------------------------------------
% EFFECTIVE MEAN-FIELD CONSTRUCTION
% ---------------------------------------------------------------

\subsection{Near-horizon $\chi$-field dynamics: an effective mean-field construction}
\label{app:chi_dynamics}

The conditional theorem above is purely structural.
To go beyond it and exhibit an explicit mechanism, we construct an effective
mean-field model of the shell, valid in the Ginzburg--Landau regime.
This is \emph{not} a full microscopic derivation from the underlying condensate
action, and the results below have a weaker status than the theorem.
We mark the status of each step explicitly.

\paragraph{Step 1: local outer asymptotics of the $\chi$-field.}

Near the critical point $T_{\rm loc}(\rho_c) = T_c$, the reduced temperature is
\begin{equation}
\varepsilon(\rho)
\;=\;
1 - \frac{T_{\rm loc}(\rho)}{T_c}
\;=\;
\frac{\rho - \rho_c}{\rho}
\;\approx\;
\frac{\rho - \rho_c}{\rho_c}
\quad (\rho \downarrow \rho_c^+)\,.
\label{eq:eps_rho2}
\end{equation}
The Ginzburg--Landau effective action for the order parameter $\chi$,
with Tolman temperature as control parameter, is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal{F}_{\rm GL}[\chi]
=
\int d\rho\,r_h^2\,
\Bigl[
a\,(\partial_\rho\chi)^2
+ \frac{\lambda}{6}\,\varepsilon(\rho)\,\chi^2
+ \frac{\lambda}{4}\,\chi^4
\Bigr]\,,
\label{eq:F_GL2}
\end{equation}
where the coefficients are fixed by the Dolan--Jackiw potential
\cite{DolanJackiw1974} used to derive $T_c$ (Section~\ref{sec:quantum_vacuum}).

In the mean-field approximation (gradient term subdominant), the local outer
asymptotic scaling just outside the shell is
\begin{equation}
\chi(\rho)
\;\propto\;
\left(\frac{\rho - \rho_c}{\rho_c}\right)^{1/2}
\quad (\rho \downarrow \rho_c^+)\,.
\label{eq:chi_asym}
\end{equation}
\textit{This is the leading outer asymptotic behaviour of the order parameter,
not a complete radial profile.}
The full profile, including the interface region and the inner branch
$\rho < \rho_c$, requires solving the Euler--Lagrange equation of
$\mathcal{F}_{\rm GL}$ numerically.
The mean-field exponent $1/2$ is the leading-order result; fluctuation
corrections modify it toward the Ising value $\nu\approx0.63$ in 3D.

\paragraph{Step 2: effective mode equation in a minimal near-horizon closure.}

A minimal ECT-motivated near-horizon closure is obtained by letting the
redshift factor be modulated by the local Lorentz-order parameter:
\begin{equation}
g_{tt}^{\rm eff}(\rho)
\;=\;
-Z_t\!\left(\frac{\chi(\rho)}{\chi_{\rm vac}}\right)(\kappa\rho)^2\,,
\qquad
Z_t(1) = 1\,,
\label{eq:metric_closure}
\end{equation}
where the simplest choice is $Z_t(\chi/\chi_{\rm vac}) = \chi/\chi_{\rm vac}$,
giving an effective local speed
\begin{equation}
c_{\rm eff}(\rho)
\;=\;
c\,\sqrt{\chi(\rho)/\chi_{\rm vac}}\,.
\label{eq:ceff2}
\end{equation}
\textit{This is a minimal closure, not a derived result.}
It encodes the natural ECT expectation that the effective Lorentzian metric
degrades continuously as $\chi\to0$, but the specific functional form is an
assumption.

Within this closure, the effective s-wave radial equation for an outgoing
massless mode $\varphi = e^{-i\omega t}f(\rho)$ is
\begin{equation}
\partial_\rho
\!\left[
c_{\rm eff}^2(\rho)\,\partial_\rho f
\right]
+
\frac{\omega^2}{(\kappa\rho)^2}\,f
=
0\,.
\label{eq:wave_eq2}
\end{equation}
\textit{This is the effective s-wave equation in the minimal near-horizon
closure.
Its validity is conditional on the closure Eq.~\eqref{eq:metric_closure}
and on the local asymptotics Eq.~\eqref{eq:chi_asym}.}

\paragraph{Step 3: finiteness of the shell correction.}

In the WKB language the shell correction to the outgoing channel is encoded in
\begin{equation}
\ln |\mathcal{T}_\omega^{(0)}|
\;\sim\;
-\int_{\rm shell} d\rho\,\Im\,k_\omega(\rho)\,.
\label{eq:WKB_shell}
\end{equation}
Because $c_{\rm eff}(\rho)\propto(\rho-\rho_c)^{1/4}$ in the outer asymptotic
regime, the integrand behaves as $(\rho-\rho_c)^{-1/4}$ near the shell and the
integral is \emph{finite}.
This establishes that the shell induces a finite, nonzero correction to
the standard Hawking channel; it does not suppress emission entirely.
On dimensional grounds, within the minimal closure, the correction is
expected to be extremely small for astrophysical black holes
(suppressed by $\rho_c/r_h \sim M_{\rm Pl}^2/M^2$) and potentially
order-unity near the Planck mass.
This is a dimensional estimate within the minimal closure;
the precise coefficient requires the fully derived shell Hamiltonian
and is not claimed here.

\paragraph{Step 4: structure of the state-dependent coupling.}

Beyond the mean-field background $\chi(\rho)$, the quantum fluctuations
$\delta\chi^{(s)}(\rho)$ encode the microstate $s$ of the shell.
The general linear-response form of the shell-state-dependent correction to
the transmission amplitude is
\begin{equation}
\delta\ln \mathcal{T}_\omega[s]
\;=\;
\int_{\rm shell} d\rho\;
\mathcal{K}_\omega(\rho)\,\delta\chi^{(s)}(\rho)\,,
\label{eq:kernel_form}
\end{equation}
where the kernel $\mathcal{K}_\omega(\rho)$ is determined by the near-horizon
ECT dynamics.
\textit{Equation~\eqref{eq:kernel_form} is the general structural form of the
shell--radiation coupling at linear order in the fluctuation.
Computing $\mathcal{K}_\omega(\rho)$ explicitly from first principles remains
an open problem} (see Table~\ref{tab:bh_info_status}).

In the simplest phase-dominated approximation the kernel reduces to a constant
phase prefactor, consistent with the parametrisation
Eq.~\eqref{eq:Nomega_corrected} in the main text.
However, this further simplification should not be identified with a
full first-principles derivation.

\paragraph{Effective shell Hamiltonian.}

Decomposing the Lorentz-order field as
$\chi(\rho,\Omega,t) = \bar\chi(\rho) + \delta\chi(\rho,\Omega,t)$,
the GL free energy Eq.~\eqref{eq:F_GL2} gives a \emph{static} energy functional.
Adding the kinetic term from the time-dependent part of the ECT condensate
action, the minimal effective shell Hamiltonian is
\begin{equation}
H_{\rm shell}
=
\int d\rho\,d\Omega\,r_h^2
\left[
\frac{\pi_\chi^2}{2\,Z_\chi}
+
\frac{a}{r_h^2}\,(\partial_\rho\delta\chi)^2
+
\frac{W_\chi}{2r_h^4}\,(\nabla_\Omega\delta\chi)^2
+
U_{\rm eff}(\delta\chi;\rho)
\right],
\label{eq:Hshell_eff}
\end{equation}
where $\pi_\chi = Z_\chi\,\partial_t\delta\chi$ is the conjugate momentum,
the effective potential is
\begin{equation}
U_{\rm eff}(\delta\chi;\rho)
=
\frac{1}{2}\,m_\chi^2(\rho)\,\delta\chi^2
+
\frac{\lambda_\chi}{4}\,\delta\chi^4
+ \cdots,
\qquad
m_\chi^2(\rho)
\propto
\frac{\rho_c - \rho}{\rho_c}\,,
\label{eq:Ueff_shell}
\end{equation}
and the kinetic coefficient $Z_\chi$ and the angular stiffness $W_\chi$ are
effective parameters not yet derived from the full condensate action.

\textit{Status of Eq.~\eqref{eq:Hshell_eff}.}
The form of $H_{\rm shell}$ is uniquely determined by three inputs: the
Ginzburg--Landau description of a critical scalar field, the Rindler-like
geometry near the horizon, and the requirement that the effective potential
vanish at $\rho = \rho_c$.
In this sense the \emph{structure} of $H_{\rm shell}$ follows from ECT's
near-horizon critical sector, but the numerical coefficients
$Z_\chi$, $W_\chi$, $\lambda_\chi$ are not yet derived from the microscopic
condensate action; they remain open parameters.

\paragraph{Minimal shell--radiation coupling.}

Because the emergent Lorentzian structure in ECT depends on $\chi$,
outgoing radiation cannot propagate through the shell without coupling to
its fluctuations.
At leading order, the simplest local interaction consistent with locality,
linearity in the fluctuation $\delta\chi$, and minimal operator dimension is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal{L}_{\rm int}
=
-\frac{g}{2}\,\delta\chi\,(\partial\varphi)^2\,,
\label{eq:Lint}
\end{equation}
where $\varphi$ represents a generic outgoing radiation mode and
$g$ is the shell--radiation coupling with dimension $[\text{length}]$.

This form is not postulated but follows from the $\chi$-dependence of
the effective metric: schematically,
$g_{\mu\nu}^{\rm eff}(\chi) \approx \bar g_{\mu\nu}(1 + \delta\chi/\chi_{\rm vac})$,
so $\delta g_{\mu\nu} \propto \delta\chi\,\bar g_{\mu\nu}$,
and the minimal coupling to the stress tensor $T^{\mu\nu}_{\rm rad}$
reduces to Eq.~\eqref{eq:Lint} for a massless scalar.
For tensor modes (gravitons) the coupling has an identical structure
at linearised order.

\textit{Status of Eq.~\eqref{eq:Lint}.}
The \emph{form} of the coupling is uniquely fixed at this order.
The \emph{coefficient} $g$ is not yet derived from the microscopic action;
it is the open parameter whose calculation constitutes the central missing
step toward a complete resolution.
The kernel $\mathcal{K}_\omega(\rho)$ in Eq.~\eqref{eq:kernel_form} is
related to $g$ and the shell Green function by
$\mathcal{K}_\omega(\rho) \sim g\,G_\omega^{\rm shell}(\rho)$,
where $G_\omega^{\rm shell}$ is the shell propagator.

\subsection{Toy finite-memory shell model and the Page mechanism}
\label{app:page_toy}

The conditional theorem guarantees that exact thermality is impossible and
purification must occur, but it does not provide a quantitative evaporation
curve.
To illustrate how the Page mechanism arises within the ECT shell picture, we
construct the following \emph{illustrative} finite-memory model.
This model is not derived from the microscopic condensate action; it is an
explicit realisation of the logical structure the theorem requires.

\paragraph{Setup.}
Discretise the shell into $N \sim A/\ell_*^2$ local cells, where $\ell_*$ is
an effective UV cutoff.
Give each cell a $q$-dimensional Hilbert space.
The shell's total Hilbert space is
$\mathcal{H}_{\rm shell} = (\mathbb{C}^q)^{\otimes N}$
with
\begin{equation}
S_{\rm shell}^{\max}
=
N\ln q
\;\sim\;
\frac{A}{\ell_*^2}\ln q\,.
\label{eq:Sshell_max}
\end{equation}
For $\ell_* \sim \ell_{\rm Pl}$ and $q \sim 2$ this reproduces the area
law up to the undetermined $\ln q$ coefficient.

\paragraph{Unitary emission map.}
Each emission step is a unitary map on the full Hilbert space:
\begin{equation}
U_n:\;
\mathcal{H}_{\rm shell}^{(n)}\otimes\mathcal{H}_{\rm vac}^{(n)}
\;\longrightarrow\;
\mathcal{H}_{\rm shell}^{(n+1)}\otimes\mathcal{H}_{\rm rad}^{(n)}\,,
\label{eq:emission_map}
\end{equation}
with the only constraint that the map is unitary and is compatible with
the coupling Eq.~\eqref{eq:Lint}.
The key point is that $U_n$ depends on the shell state: different shell
microstates lead to different outgoing quanta statistics.

\paragraph{Resulting entropy curve.}
The von Neumann entropy of the radiation after $n$ emission steps follows
the Page curve for a system of total dimension
$d_{\rm total} = q^N \times q^n$:
\begin{equation}
S_{\rm rad}(n)
\;\approx\;
\begin{cases}
n\ln q & n \ll N/2\quad(\text{early: almost thermal})\\
N\ln q - (n-N)\ln q & n \gg N/2\quad(\text{late: purifying})
\end{cases}
\label{eq:toy_page}
\end{equation}
with a smooth turnaround at the Page time $n_P \sim N/2$.

\paragraph{Interpretation.}
The early-time regime reproduces thermal emission at the Hawking rate.
After the Page time, the radiation entropy decreases, consistent with
purification of earlier quanta through shell-mediated correlations.
The coarse-grained entropy (obtained by tracing over the shell) increases
monotonically, recovering the Hawking result at low resolution.

This model is \emph{illustrative}: it demonstrates that the Page mechanism
follows automatically from the existence of a finite-entropy shell coupled to
outgoing modes by a unitary map.
The actual ECT Page curve requires the microscopic $H_{\rm shell}$ and
the coefficient $g$; the toy model only shows what form the curve must take.

\subsection{Interior and the singularity}
\label{app:interior}

In ECT the interior of a black hole is the region where
$T_{\rm loc}\gg T_c$, so the Lorentz-ordered phase is completely broken.
The metric description ceases to be fundamental well before the classical
singularity is reached.
The singularity is therefore not a physical object in ECT but a consequence
of extending the effective Lorentzian description beyond its domain of validity.
The ``pre-Lorentzian core'' sector $\mathcal{H}_{\rm core}$ in
Eq.~\eqref{eq:Hilbert_full} replaces the classically singular interior.

This picture is consistent with the broader ECT interpretation of the
pre-Planckian epoch as a Euclidean condensate phase
(Section~\ref{sec:cosmo_evolution_comparison}).
The question of where information ``is'' inside the black hole may then be
ill-posed in classical geometric terms; the information is distributed across
the condensate microstate of the shell and core, which does not admit a simple
Lorentzian spatial description.

\subsection{Potential observational signatures}
\label{app:bh_obs}

Although the direct detection of information-carrying Hawking correlations
from astrophysical black holes is not feasible with current technology,
the critical-shell picture has several in-principle testable consequences.

\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{Near-horizon deviations from perfect GR.}
If the horizon is accompanied by a physical shell at $\rho_c$,
small departures from the ideal GR boundary condition are expected.
These may manifest as universal corrections to quasi-normal mode
frequencies, effective horizon reflectivity, or late-time ringdown
structure in gravitational-wave events
\cite{Almheiri2013}.
Any such signal is suppressed by $(\rho_c/r_s)\sim M_{\rm Pl}^2/M^2$
and is therefore extremely small for astrophysical black holes, but
may be visible in analogue-gravity experiments.

\item \emph{Non-exact thermality.}
Hawking radiation that carries information must deviate from exact
thermal statistics.
This cannot be tested with astrophysical black holes at present, but
analogue systems (acoustic black holes, optical analogues, cold-atom
setups) can probe near-thermal emission from horizons and may exhibit
shell-like features.

\item \emph{Near-horizon shell scale.}
The value $\rho_c = \ell_{\rm Pl}/\sqrt{3\pi}$ is obtained within
the current Tolman-heating / critical-shell closure.
Mass-independence would be a distinctive feature if the closure is correct,
but this should be read as a closure-level result rather than a
universal first-principles theorem.
It is consistent with current LIGO/Virgo ringdown data but requires
future gravitational-wave observations at higher signal-to-noise to
test quantitatively.

\item \emph{Mass-independence as a falsifiable signature.}
The microscopic consistency criterion (Section~\ref{app:consistency_criterion})
implies that any near-horizon deviations from GR must scale with the single
universal parameter $\rho_c$, not with the black-hole mass.
Concretely, corrections to quasinormal-mode frequencies scale as
$\delta\omega/\omega \sim \rho_c/r_h \propto M^{-1}$.
If future gravitational-wave data reveal mass-dependent deviations with a
\emph{different} scaling, condition~(C2b) of the criterion would be
challenged: the Tolman control-parameter assumption would need revision.
Conversely, confirmation of a universal $\propto M^{-1}$ near-horizon scale
across events spanning a decade in mass would constitute direct evidence
for the ECT shell picture.

\item \emph{Analogue-horizon tests.}
Acoustic black holes, optical analogues, and cold-atom setups can probe
near-horizon thermal emission at laboratory scales.
If a system with an analogue of a critical near-horizon medium produces
emission that deviates from exact thermality in a state-dependent way,
this would provide experimental support for the structural mechanism
required by the conditional theorem, independently of the specific ECT
coupling coefficient $g$.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Microscopic consistency criterion for ECT black-hole unitarity}
\label{app:consistency_criterion}

The conditional theorem (Section~\ref{app:conditional_theorem}) proves that
the paradox is resolved whenever four conditions are simultaneously satisfied.
Here we turn this into a \emph{classification of ECT microcompletions}: a
microscopic completion of ECT that satisfies all four conditions below resolves
the paradox; any that violates one of them either fails to resolve it or
requires additional structure.

\paragraph{The four genuine conditions.}

The theorem's input conditions, and what they require of the underlying
ECT microcompletion, are:

\begin{enumerate}[label=(C\arabic*)]

\item \textbf{Self-adjoint microscopic dynamics.}
The condensate Hamiltonian must be self-adjoint: $H_{\rm micro} = H_{\rm micro}^\dagger$.
In ECT this is a structural requirement of the Euclidean path-integral
framework (postulate P2); it is the strongest motivation for expecting
unitarity to hold.

\item \textbf{Finite critical temperature and near-horizon Lorentz-order shell.}
The condensate must have a finite critical temperature $T_c$ above which
the Lorentz-ordered phase ceases to exist.
Moreover, the local Tolman temperature must be the correct thermodynamic
control parameter for this phase transition near the horizon.
These two sub-requirements imply that a finite-entropy critical shell exists
at $\rho_c = \hbar c/(2\pi k_B T_c)$.
The first sub-requirement is derived in ECT (Dolan--Jackiw potential);
the second remains conditional.

\item \textbf{Complete evaporation with no infinite-capacity remnant.}
Evaporation must proceed to completion without leaving a remnant carrying
an unbounded amount of hidden information.
This is an assumption about the final state of evaporation not derived from
the current formulation; the Planck-remnant case requires separate treatment.

\item \textbf{No additional non-unitary dissipation.}
The interaction between the shell and the radiation sector must not
introduce intrinsic non-unitarity (e.g.\ an open-system environment outside
the ECT degrees of freedom).
This follows from the ECT assumption of a closed condensate system.

\end{enumerate}

Note that \emph{shell-state-dependence of the outgoing channel is not
an independent condition}: it is a \emph{consequence} of (C1)--(C4)
proven by the theorem.
Similarly, the breakdown of exact thermality and the late-time purification
of radiation are consequences, not assumptions.

\paragraph{Classification of microcompletions.}

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{@{}p{0.30\textwidth}p{0.60\textwidth}@{}}
\toprule
Condition violated & Implication for the information paradox \\
\midrule
(C1) violated & ECT itself admits fundamental non-unitarity; the theory
requires substantial revision before the paradox can be addressed. \\[4pt]
(C2) violated (no $T_c$) & The ECT horizon is effectively geometrically
empty; near-horizon microphysics does not differ qualitatively from GR,
and no shell mechanism exists. \\[4pt]
(C2) violated (Tolman not the control parameter) & The shell location becomes
a free parameter; the universal $\rho_c$ result is lost, and the shell-based
mechanism must be re-derived for the actual control parameter. \\[4pt]
(C3) violated (infinite remnant) & The paradox is formally evaded by hiding
information indefinitely, but at the cost of pathological remnant physics
(infinite pair-production rate in external fields, etc.). \\[4pt]
(C4) violated & The ECT condensate is open to an external non-unitary
environment; additional quantum gravity degrees of freedom must be specified. \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\paragraph{Current status within ECT.}

Condition~(C1) is the most natural expectation: self-adjointness of the
condensate action is postulate P2.
Condition~(C2a) (existence of $T_c$) is established by the Dolan--Jackiw
analysis (Section~\ref{sec:quantum_vacuum}).
Condition~(C2b) (Tolman as control parameter) is the central remaining
structural assumption; deriving it from the black-hole branch of the full
condensate action is the sharpest open problem in the ECT black-hole sector.
Conditions (C3) and (C4) are natural but not derived.

Thus the present ECT framework satisfies (C1) structurally, (C2a) by
calculation, and (C2b) by structural plausibility.
What remains to be proved is (C2b) and to verify (C3)--(C4).
No known feature of ECT violates any of these conditions.

\subsection{Summary table}
\label{app:bh_summary}

\begin{table}[H]

Level~A = structural result of the framework;
Level~B = conditional, closure-level, or effective argument within the
present shell/interface construction;
Open = problem not yet completed.}
\label{tab:bh_info_status}
\begin{tabular}{@{}p{0.52\textwidth}cc@{}}
\toprule

\end{table}

\centering

\caption{%
ECT black-hole information scenario.
\textbf{(a)} Tolman temperature profile $T_{\rm loc}(\rho)$ near a
non-extremal horizon, plotted in units of $T_c$ vs.\ $\rho/\rho_c$.
The condensate critical temperature $T_c = v_0\sqrt{6}$ (dashed horizontal
line) is reached at the universal proper distance
$\rho_c \approx 0.33\,\ell_{\rm Pl}$ (dotted vertical line), independently
of the black-hole mass.
The lightly shaded region is the well-ordered Lorentzian phase ($T_{\rm loc}<T_c$);
the darker shaded region marks the near-horizon critical shell ($T_{\rm loc}>T_c$).
\textbf{(b)} Schematic Page curve.
The coarse-grained radiation entropy (dashed) rises monotonically as
in the semiclassical Hawking approximation.
The fine-grained entropy (solid) follows the coarse-grained branch
until the Page time, then decreases as the shell entropy capacity becomes
finite and state-dependent corrections to emission become order-one.
The shaded area between the two curves represents entropy that is
``returned'' via shell-mediated correlations.
The figure is schematic; a quantitative curve requires the explicit shell
Hamiltonian.
\textbf{(c)} Black-hole parameters vs.\ mass.
The critical shell proper distance $\rho_c$ is mass-independent (not shown
separately); the ratio $\rho_c/r_s \propto M^{-1}$ (left axis, red) shows
how deeply the shell is buried inside the Schwarzschild radius.
The Hawking temperature $T_H \propto M^{-1}$ (right axis, dashed blue)
decreases with mass.
For all astrophysical black holes $T_H \ll T_c$; the critical shell is
firmly in the sub-Planckian regime.
}
\label{fig:bh_information}
\end{figure}

% ============================================================
% APPENDIX: Derivation of galactic phi-closure (new, v3f)
% ============================================================

\section{Derivation of the galactic $\phi$-closure and the practical fitting law}
\label{app:galactic_phi_closure}

This appendix derives the practical galactic fitting law used in the
SPARC analysis.

\subsection{Variational structure}

The galactic sector is treated as a nonlinear static response problem
for the effective potential $\Phi$.  The minimal effective functional is
taken to be
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_{\rm gal}[\Phi]
=
\int d^3x\,
\left[
\frac{g_0^{\dagger\,2}}{8\pi G_N}
F\!\left(\frac{|\nabla\Phi|}{g^\dagger_0}\right)
-\rho_b(\mathbf{x})\,\Phi
\right],
\label{eq:app_gal_functional}
\end{equation}
where $g^\dagger_0$ is the cosmological baseline critical acceleration
scale and $\rho_b$ is the baryonic source density.

The corresponding Euler--Lagrange equation reads
\begin{equation}
\nabla\!\cdot\!\left[
\mu_\phi\!\left(\frac{|\nabla\Phi|}{g^\dagger_0}\right)\nabla\Phi
\right]
=
4\pi G_N \rho_b,
\label{eq:app_gal_mu_eq}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\mu_\phi(x)=\frac{1}{2x}\frac{dF}{dx}.
\label{eq:app_mu_from_F}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Required asymptotic branches}

The closure must reproduce two limiting regimes.

\paragraph{Screened Newtonian branch.}
At large accelerations one must recover ordinary gravity,
\begin{equation}
\mu_\phi(x)\to 1
\qquad (x\gg 1).
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Deep critical branch.}
At small accelerations the critical infrared branch must satisfy
\begin{equation}
\mu_\phi(x)\to x
\qquad (x\ll 1),
\end{equation}
which yields the characteristic ECT deep-regime law
\begin{equation}
g\to \sqrt{g_N g^\dagger}.
\end{equation}

\subsection{Minimal interpolation choice}

A full first-principles derivation of the interpolation family from the
microscopic condensate is not yet available.  The present work
therefore adopts the phenomenologically simplest smooth choice
consistent with both asymptotic branches:
\begin{equation}
\mu_\phi(x)=\frac{x}{1+x}.
\label{eq:app_mu_choice}
\end{equation}
This is a Level~B closure assumption, not a Level~A theorem.

Using eq.~\eqref{eq:app_mu_from_F}, one obtains
\begin{equation}
F(x)=x^2-2x+2\ln(1+x),
\label{eq:app_F_choice}
\end{equation}
up to an irrelevant additive constant.  One verifies immediately that
\[
F(x)\sim x^2 \quad (x\gg1),
\qquad
F(x)\sim \frac{2}{3}x^3 \quad (x\ll1),
\]
so the closure indeed interpolates between the quadratic screened branch
and the critical $Y^{3/2}$ branch.

\subsection{Practical algebraic fitting law}

In the quasi-radial fitting approximation, the modified Poisson
equation reduces to
\begin{equation}
\mu_\phi\!\left(\frac{g}{g^\dagger_{\rm eff}}\right) g = g_N.
\label{eq:app_mu_gn}
\end{equation}
With the choice \eqref{eq:app_mu_choice} this gives
\begin{equation}
\frac{g/g^\dagger_{\rm eff}}{1+g/g^\dagger_{\rm eff}}\,g=g_N,
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
g^2-g_N g-g_N g^\dagger_{\rm eff}=0.
\end{equation}
Selecting the positive branch yields the practical ECT fitting law
\begin{equation}
g(R)=\frac{1}{2}\left[g_N(R)+\sqrt{g_N^2(R)+4\,g_N(R)\,g^\dagger_{\rm eff}}\right].
\label{eq:app_final_g_law}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Baryonic input from SPARC}

The Newtonian input acceleration is computed from the SPARC baryonic
mass model as
\begin{equation}
g_N(R)=
\frac{
V_{\rm gas}^2(R)+\Upsilon_{\rm d}V_{\rm disk}^2(R)+
\Upsilon_{\rm b}V_{\rm bul}^2(R)
}{R}.
\label{eq:app_gn_sparc}
\end{equation}
The predicted circular velocity is then
\begin{equation}
V_{\rm ECT}(R)=\sqrt{R\,g(R)}.
\label{eq:app_vect}
\end{equation}

\subsection{RAR representation of the same closure}

The radial acceleration relation is not an independent phenomenological
law added on top of the velocity fit.  It is simply the same galactic
closure expressed in acceleration variables:
\begin{equation}
g_{\rm obs}(R)=\frac{V_{\rm obs}^2(R)}{R},
\qquad
g_{\rm bar}(R)=\frac{V_{\rm gas}^2(R)+\Upsilon_{\rm d}V_{\rm disk}^2(R)+
\Upsilon_{\rm b}V_{\rm bul}^2(R)}{R}.
\end{equation}
The corresponding ECT prediction is therefore
\begin{equation}
g_{\rm ECT}(R)=\frac{1}{2}\left[g_{\rm bar}(R)+
\sqrt{g_{\rm bar}^2(R)+4\,g_{\rm bar}(R)\,g^\dagger_{\rm eff}}\right].
\label{eq:app_rar_ect}
\end{equation}
Thus the RAR plots are only a different projection of the same fitted
galactic closure already used in the rotation-curve analysis.

\subsection{Deep branch and BTFR}

In the low-acceleration branch, eq.~\eqref{eq:app_final_g_law}
reduces to
\begin{equation}
g \simeq \sqrt{g_N g^\dagger_{\rm eff}}.
\end{equation}
For circular motion, $v_c^2/R=g$, and at large radii where
$M_b(R)\to M_{\rm bar}$,
\begin{equation}
v_c^4 = G_N M_{\rm bar} g^\dagger_{\rm eff}.
\label{eq:app_btfr_again}
\end{equation}
Thus the BTFR slope is structural, while its normalisation is governed
by the effective critical scale.

In the present numerical implementation we use an internal outer
baryonic-mass proxy
\begin{equation}
M_{\rm bar,eff}
=
\frac{R_{\rm tail}^2\,g_N(R_{\rm tail})}{G_N},
\label{eq:app_btfr_proxy_mass}
\end{equation}
where $R_{\rm tail}$ is an outer-tail radius estimator constructed from
the last measured SPARC points.  This provides a self-consistent BTFR
test inside the same galactic closure pipeline.  It should be read as an
internal ECT BTFR diagnostic, not yet as a substitute for the standard
catalogue-level BTFR constructed from an independent total baryonic-mass
table.


% ============================================================
% APPENDIX: Computational procedure for SPARC fits (new, v3f)
% ============================================================

\section{Computational procedure for the SPARC galactic fits}
\label{app:sparc_computation}

This appendix summarises the numerical procedure used to generate the
galactic figures and tables.

\subsection{Input data}

The analysis uses the SPARC mass-model catalogue
\cite{Lelli2016SPARC}, containing radius $R$, observed velocity
$V_{\rm obs}$ with uncertainty $\sigma_V$, and the baryonic Newtonian
components $V_{\rm gas}$, $V_{\rm disk}$, and $V_{\rm bul}$.

\subsection{Fit modes}

Two fitting modes are considered.

\paragraph{Fixed-$M/L$ mode.}
The stellar mass-to-light ratios are fixed at
\[
\Upsilon_{\rm d}=0.5,\qquad \Upsilon_{\rm b}=0.7,
\]
and only the effective critical scale $g^\dagger_{\rm eff}$ is fitted.
This is the cleaner ECT test because it removes the strongest disk
$M/L$ degeneracy.

\paragraph{Free-$M/L$ mode.}
The disk mass-to-light ratio $\Upsilon_{\rm d}$ is fitted jointly with
$g^\dagger_{\rm eff}$, while $\Upsilon_{\rm b}=0.7$ is kept fixed.

\subsection{Optimisation and quality control}

For each galaxy the fit minimises
\begin{equation}
\chi^2 = \sum_i
\frac{\left[V_{\rm obs}(R_i)-V_{\rm ECT}(R_i)\right]^2}{\sigma_i^2}.
\end{equation}
A minimum error floor of $2\,{\rm km\,s^{-1}}$ is imposed in the present
runs for robustness.

The output catalogue stores quality flags indicating:
\begin{itemize}
\item too few measured points,
\item poor reduced $\chi^2$,
\item fitted stellar $M/L$ at the scan boundary,
\item possible bulge sensitivity.
\end{itemize}
A clean sub-sample is defined by excluding low-quality flagged cases.

\subsection{Model comparison}

Four fit families are compared:
\begin{enumerate}
\item ECT fixed-$M/L$ closure ($k=1$ free parameter),
\item ECT free-$M/L$ closure ($k=2$ free parameters),
\item MOND with free stellar $M/L$ ($k=1$),
\item $\Lambda$CDM with an NFW-type halo fit ($k=3$).
\end{enumerate}
Because the number of free parameters differs between the models, both
AIC and BIC are computed in addition to reduced $\chi^2$.

\subsection{Outputs used in the paper}

The main text uses:
\begin{itemize}
\item a representative SPARC rotation-curve figure (Fig.~\ref{fig:sparc_sample_new}),
\item a compact sample-level fit-quality comparison figure (Fig.~\ref{fig:chi2_comparison_main}),
\item the updated effective critical-scale summary figure (Fig.~\ref{fig:gdagger_analysis_new_main}),
\item a Milky Way comparison figure (Fig.~\ref{fig:mw_new}),
\item a compact summary table over the SPARC sample (Table~\ref{tab:sparc_summary_main}),
\item an internal BTFR diagnostic figure (Fig.~\ref{fig:btfr_new_main}),
\item a six-panel RAR figure derived from the same closure (Fig.~\ref{fig:rar_new_main}).
\end{itemize}

Additional scatter diagnostics, fixed/free-$M/L$ comparisons, and
further machine-readable tables are retained as supplementary material.

\subsection{Derived plot quantities: BTFR, RAR, and effective critical-scale diagnostics}

Three additional observational representations are generated from the
same fitted galactic closure.

\paragraph{BTFR.}
The BTFR plot uses the outer-tail velocity estimator $V_{\rm flat}$
constructed from the outer SPARC points together with the internal
effective baryonic-mass proxy
\[
M_{\rm bar,eff}=R_{\rm tail}^2 g_N(R_{\rm tail})/G_N.
\]
This yields a self-consistent ECT BTFR diagnostic based on the same
pipeline as the rotation-curve fits.

\paragraph{RAR.}
The RAR figure is produced by plotting
$g_{\rm obs}=V_{\rm obs}^2/R$ against
$g_{\rm bar}=(V_{\rm gas}^2+\Upsilon_{\rm d}V_{\rm disk}^2+\Upsilon_{\rm b}V_{\rm bul}^2)/R$
for the same galaxies.  The ECT and MOND curves shown there are not
separate empirical fit functions, but direct projections of the same
closure used in the velocity analysis.

\paragraph{Effective critical-scale analysis.}
The updated $g^\dagger$ figure is built directly from the fitted
per-galaxy values of $g^\dagger_{\rm eff}$ produced by the new SPARC
pipeline.  It replaces the earlier legacy $\phi_{\rm env}$ plot and is
therefore the correct summary diagnostic for the present version of the
galactic sector.

\subsection{Diagnostic interpretation and the current EFE proxy}

The diagnostics retained in this appendix serve three distinct roles:
they separate fixed-$M/L$ from free-$M/L$ behaviour, they allow
information-criterion comparison (AIC/BIC) between ECT, MOND, and
$\Lambda$CDM, and they identify the clean sub-sample used in the main
text to reduce the strongest fitting pathologies.  Only the most
informative summary figures are promoted to the main narrative; the
remaining diagnostics are kept here in order to document the stability
and limitations of the present Level~B galactic closure.

A preliminary nearest-neighbour proxy for the external field was tested.
For the currently available environment inputs the resulting ratio
$g_{\rm ext}/g^\dagger_0$ is typically extremely small, so the proxy
correction is numerically negligible.  This does not show that EFE is
absent in ECT; it only shows that the present Level-1 proxy is too weak
to affect the displayed sample and is therefore not promoted to a main
result.


\subsection{Additional diagnostic outputs}

\begin{figure*}[H]
\centering
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth]{figures/diag_gdag_scatter4.pdf}
\caption{Additional scatter diagnostics for the fitted effective
critical scale $g^\dagger_{\rm eff}$ across the SPARC sample: dependence
on a baryonic mass proxy, a baryonic surface-density proxy, the fitted
disk mass-to-light ratio, and the fit quality itself.  These plots are
retained as supplementary diagnostics rather than promoted to the main
text, because the more compact summary is now given by
Fig.~\ref{fig:gdagger_analysis_new_main}.}
\label{fig:app_gdag_scatter}
\end{figure*}

\begin{figure}[H]
\centering
\includegraphics[width=0.78\linewidth]{figures/diag_gdag_histogram.pdf}
\caption{Histogram of fitted effective critical scales
$g^\dagger_{\rm eff}$ across the SPARC sample.  The vertical markers
indicate the two natural ECT baselines $cH_0$ and $cH_0/(2\pi)$.  In
the present manuscript the compact two-panel summary of this information
is shown in Fig.~\ref{fig:gdagger_analysis_new_main}; the histogram is
retained here as a supplementary diagnostic.}
\label{fig:app_gdag_hist}
\end{figure}

\begin{figure*}[H]
\centering
\includegraphics[width=0.82\textwidth]{figures/diag_fixed_vs_free_chi2.pdf}
\caption{Fixed-$M/L$ versus free-$M/L$ comparison of fit quality across
the SPARC sample.  Each point corresponds to one galaxy, with the
horizontal axis showing the reduced $\chi^2$ of the fixed-$M/L$ ECT fit
and the vertical axis showing the reduced $\chi^2$ of the free-$M/L$
ECT fit.  The diagonal $y=x$ marks equal fit quality.  The dominant
population lies below this line, showing that allowing $\Upsilon_{\rm d}$
to vary improves the fit for most galaxies.  This figure is retained in
the appendix because it diagnoses the strength of the $M/L$ degeneracy
rather than introducing a new physical prediction.}
\label{fig:app_fixed_vs_free_chi2}
\end{figure*}

\begin{figure*}[H]
\centering
\includegraphics[width=0.82\textwidth]{figures/diag_fixed_vs_free_gdag.pdf}
\caption{Fixed-$M/L$ versus free-$M/L$ comparison of the fitted
effective critical scale $g^\dagger_{\rm eff}$.  The diagonal $y=x$
marks identical recovered values.  The moderate correlation indicates
that part of the scatter in $g^\dagger_{\rm eff}$ is robust under
changes in the disk mass-to-light treatment, while another part is
clearly entangled with the $M/L$ degeneracy.  This is why the fixed-$M/L$
mode is used in the main text as the cleaner test of the ECT galactic
closure, whereas the free-$M/L$ mode is interpreted as a robustness
check rather than as the primary physical result.}
\label{fig:app_fixed_vs_free_gdag}
\end{figure*}

The moderate fixed/free correlation (Pearson $r\approx0.54$ in the
present run) confirms that the effective critical scale is neither fully
determined by the stellar $M/L$ choice nor fully independent of it.

The full numerical pipeline produces several diagnostics that are useful
for interpreting the galactic fits but are too methodological to occupy
main-text space.  The figures collected here serve three distinct
purposes: they document the residual scatter of the fitted effective
critical scale, they show how that scatter changes between fixed-$M/L$
and free-$M/L$ fitting modes, and they quantify the extent to which the
apparent improvement of the free-$M/L$ mode should be attributed to
extra nuisance freedom rather than to a deeper physical closure.
Accordingly, these plots are retained in the appendix as robustness and
degeneracy diagnostics rather than as headline physical results.



% === Data and Code Availability and Acknowledgments ===

% ============================================================
% APPENDIX: Late-time phi-first cosmological background
% ============================================================
\section{Late-time $\phi$-first cosmological background apparatus}
\label{app:late_cosmo_background}

This appendix derives the minimal ECT background apparatus used for the
late-time cosmology calculations in Section~\ref{sec:hubble_jwst}.

\subsection{Effective action and FRW reduction}

We start from the effective scalar--tensor action
\begin{equation}
S_{\rm eff}
=
\int d^4x\,\sqrt{-g}\,
\left[
\frac12 f(\phi)R
-\frac12 K(\phi)(\partial\phi)^2
-V(\phi)
+\mathcal L_m
\right].
\label{eq:app_late_action}
\end{equation}
The effective gravitational stiffness and Newton coupling are
\begin{equation}
M_{\rm eff}^2(\phi)=f(\phi),
\qquad
G_{\rm eff}(\phi)=\frac{1}{8\pi f(\phi)}.
\label{eq:app_late_geff}
\end{equation}

For a spatially flat FRW metric $ds^2=-dt^2+a^2(t)d\mathbf{x}^2$ and a
homogeneous background $\phi=\phi(t)$, the effective equations are
\begin{equation}
3fH^2
=
\rho_m+\rho_r+\frac12 K\dot\phi^2+V-3H\dot f,
\label{eq:app_late_fried1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
-2f\dot H
=
\rho_m+\tfrac43\rho_r+K\dot\phi^2+\ddot f-H\dot f,
\label{eq:app_late_fried2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
K(\ddot\phi+3H\dot\phi)
+\tfrac12 K_{,\phi}\dot\phi^2
+V_{,\phi}
-\tfrac12 f_{,\phi}R
=0,
\quad
R=6(2H^2+\dot H).
\label{eq:app_late_phi_eq}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Convenient form in $N=\ln a$}

Setting $N\equiv \ln a$, $u(N)\equiv\phi(N)$, $q(N)\equiv d\phi/dN$, one has
$\dot\phi=Hq$ and $\dot f=Hf_{,\phi}q$. Equation~\eqref{eq:app_late_fried1}
then gives the exact algebraic relation
\begin{equation}
H^2
=
\frac{\rho_m+\rho_r+V}
{3f-\frac12Kq^2+3f_{,\phi}q}.
\label{eq:app_late_H2_exact}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Minimal late-time closure (Level~B)}

We adopt
\begin{equation}
f(\phi)=f_0 e^{\beta u},
\qquad
K(\phi)=K_0,
\qquad
V(\phi)=V_0+\tfrac12 m_\phi^2 u^2,
\label{eq:app_late_closure}
\end{equation}
with dimensionless parameters
\begin{equation}
E(N)\equiv \frac{H(N)}{H_0^{\rm ref}},
\quad
\kappa\equiv \frac{K_0}{f_0},
\quad
\mu^2\equiv \frac{m_\phi^2}{H_0^2},
\quad
\Omega_{V0}\equiv \frac{V_0}{3f_0H_0^2}.
\label{eq:app_late_defs}
\end{equation}
The dimensionless Friedmann equation becomes
\begin{equation}
E^2(N)
=
\frac{
\Omega_{m0}e^{-3N}
+\Omega_{r0}e^{-4N}
+\Omega_{V0}
+\frac{\mu^2}{6}u^2
}{
e^{\beta u}
-\frac{\kappa}{6}q^2
+\beta e^{\beta u}q
}.
\label{eq:app_late_E2}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Slow-drift regime and present-epoch Hubble shift}

In the slow-drift branch ($|q|\ll 1$, $\kappa q^2\ll 1$,
$|\beta q|\ll 1$), eq.~\eqref{eq:app_late_E2} simplifies to
$H^2\approx (\rho+V)/(3f)$.  Comparing with a reference background
at constant $f_0,V_0$:
\begin{equation}
\frac{\Delta H_0}{H_0}
\approx
\frac{\mu^2u_0^2}{12}
-\frac12\beta u_0.
\label{eq:app_late_deltaH}
\end{equation}
The two terms represent vacuum drift (positive) and effective
Planck-mass drift (sign determined by $\beta u_0$).

The slow-drift scalar balance gives
\begin{equation}
q
\approx
\frac{\beta e^{\beta u}}{\kappa}
\left(2+\frac{E'}{E}\right)
-
\frac{\mu^2}{3\kappa}\frac{u}{E^2},
\label{eq:app_late_q}
\end{equation}
showing that the late drift of $\phi$ is driven by the curvature
coupling $f_{,\phi}R$ balanced against the restoring force $V_{,\phi}$
and the kinetic stiffness $\kappa$.

\subsection{Distances, age, and JWST-related background effects}

Once $E(z)$ is solved, one obtains
\begin{align}
D_L(z)&=(1+z)\int_0^z \frac{dz'}{H(z')},
\quad
D_A(z)=\frac{1}{1+z}\int_0^z \frac{dz'}{H(z')},
\label{eq:app_late_dist}\\
t_{\rm lookback}(z)&=\int_0^z \frac{dz'}{(1+z')H(z')},
\quad
t_0=\int_0^\infty \frac{dz}{(1+z)H(z)}.
\label{eq:app_late_time}
\end{align}
These background quantities control the JWST background layer: the
same $\phi$-drift that shifts $H_0$ also changes inferred distances to
high-$z$ galaxies and the available formation time.

% ============================================================
% APPENDIX: Numerical algorithm
% ============================================================
\section{Numerical algorithm for late-time ECT cosmology: Hubble tension, age, and JWST background}
\label{app:late_cosmo_algorithm}

\subsection{Solver design}

The solver evolves $u(N)$ forward (in $N$) from $N=0$ ($z=0$)
to $N_{\min}=\ln(1/(1+z_{\max}))$ using SciPy \texttt{solve\_ivp} (RK45)
with the quasi-static field equation
\begin{equation}
\frac{du}{dN}=q(N,u),
\label{eq:app_algo_dudn}
\end{equation}
where $q$ is evaluated from~\eqref{eq:app_late_q} with $E'/E$ taken
from the reference $\Lambda$CDM background for computational stability.
The Friedmann equation~\eqref{eq:app_late_E2} is evaluated algebraically
at each step.  The initial condition is self-consistently iterated:
$q_0$ is obtained by one iteration of~\eqref{eq:app_late_q} with an
initial ECT-based estimate of $E'/E$.

\subsection{Benchmark parameter window}

The natural window for the slow-drift regime that gives a few-percent
Hubble shift is
\begin{equation}
\beta\sim 0.7\text{--}1.0,\quad
u_0\sim -(0.08\text{--}0.12),\quad
\mu\sim 1.0\text{--}1.5,\quad
\kappa\sim 10\text{--}20.
\label{eq:app_algo_window}
\end{equation}
For Benchmark~B ($\beta=0.8$, $\mu=1.5$, $\kappa=15$, $u_0=-0.12$)
the analytic estimate~\eqref{eq:app_late_deltaH} gives
$\Delta H_0/H_0\approx 5.1\%$, while the present semi-numerical quasi-static benchmark
(which includes the $q$-dependent corrections to $E^2$ but evaluates
$E'/E$ using the reference $\Lambda$CDM background for numerical
stability) gives $2.9\%$.
The difference reflects the fact that the quasi-static $q$ is not
strictly self-consistent in $E^2$; see the discussion of Level~B
closure status in the main text.

The analytic parameter-window scan (Fig.~\ref{fig:h0_scan_main} in the
main text) shows that the benchmark points lie inside a finite parameter
region producing a few-percent late-time Hubble shift, confirming that
the benchmark is representative rather than finely tuned.

\subsection{Derived outputs}

For age estimates, the numerical integration is extended to a
sufficiently high redshift (effectively to $z\sim 10^6$ via a
matter+radiation-dominated tail matched at $z_{\rm match}=10$), so that
the quoted ages approximate the full cosmological lookback integral
rather than a truncated low-$z$ contribution.

From the solved background the code computes:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the direct late-time Hubble shift $\Delta H_0/H_0 = E(0)-1$;
\item a ladder-style low-$z$ inferred $H_0$ from the $D_L$ slope;
\item the age correction $\Delta t_0/t_0$;
\item lookback-time and luminosity-distance shifts at $z=1,2,5,8,10,12$;
\item a simple growth proxy
$\mathcal{G}(z)\equiv G_{\rm eff}(z)/H^2(z)$
as a first indicator of early structure formation enhancement.
\end{enumerate}
All outputs are collected in a summary CSV file and a four-panel figure.
The code is available at the repository listed in the Data and Code
Availability section.


\clearpage
\section*{Data and Code Availability}
\addcontentsline{toc}{part}{Data and Code Availability}

Galaxy rotation-curve data are drawn from the public SPARC database \cite{Lelli2016}
(\url{http://astroweb.cwru.edu/SPARC/}).
All numerical scripts used to produce the figures and calculations in this paper
are publicly available at:

\begin{center}
  \url{https://github.com/chufelo/ECT-preprint-code}
\end{center}

\noindent
The repository contains: the full-SPARC rotation-curve fitting pipeline
for the new ECT galactic closure (including fixed/free $M/L$ modes,
model-comparison diagnostics against MOND and $\Lambda$CDM/NFW, and
sample-level summary tables for all 165 galaxies),
cosmological calculations (Hubble tension, inflation $n_s$, JWST halo-abundance
enhancement), matching and consistency calculations for the gravitational and
coherent action scales (including the linearised $G_N$ matching logic collected
in Appendix~\ref{app:GN_derivation}), fifth-force bounds, baryogenesis estimates,
and the effective dimensionality calculation (Fig.~\ref{fig:dimensionality}).
Scripts are self-contained Python 3 files requiring only \texttt{numpy},
\texttt{matplotlib}, and \texttt{scipy}.

\medskip
\noindent
\begin{minipage}{0.72\linewidth}
  The repository can also be accessed by scanning the QR code (right).
  The code is released under the MIT License.
  Any updates or corrections will be posted to the same URL.
\end{minipage}
\hfill
\begin{minipage}{0.22\linewidth}
  \centering
  \includegraphics[width=\linewidth]{figures/github_qr.png}
  \scriptsize\texttt{github.com/chufelo/\\ECT-preprint-code}
\end{minipage}
